People v. Veralli


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Dutchess County


64 Misc. 2d 321; 314 N.Y.S.2d 723; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1265



October 9, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for an order dismissing a three-count indictment charging him with the crimes of criminally selling, and possession of a dangerous drug upon the ground that the grand jury that returned his indictment was unconstitutionally selected.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the grand jury that returned his indictment was unconstitutionally selected and, therefore, acquired no jurisdiction over him because it was composed of individuals over the age of 21 years, and particularly had excluded from its membership youths between 18 and 21 years who constitute a distinct class, all being in violation of his rights of equal protection of the law and due process as guaranteed by the Federal and State Constitutions. The court found that federal courts have held that a State may confine the selection of jurors to persons within certain ages and furthermore exclude minors from the jury without violating constitutional rights. The court held that although defendant's contention that youths between 18 and 21 years constituted a distinct attitudinal class, such contention was highly speculative and was not substantial enough to hold that a grand jury was unconstitutionally composed if it did not have an 18 to 21 year age membership. The court concluded that N.Y. Jud. Law §§ 662 and 684 prohibiting minors from serving on grand juries were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment.


HEADNOTES

Grand Jury -- qualifications of jurors -- prohibition against minors serving on grand juries is not unconstitutional; Grand Jury which indicted defendant, drawn from panel consisting of persons not less than 21 years of age, has not been unconstitutionally selected in violation of defendant's rights.

Sections 662 and 684 of the Judiciary Law, which prohibit minors from serving on grand juries, are not unconstitutional, and a Grand Jury which indicted defendant, deliberately drawn from a panel consisting of persons not less than 21 years of age, has not been unconstitutionally selected in violation of 19-year-old defendant's rights.

 

1819 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Berry v. Stewart


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


64 Misc. 2d 590; 315 N.Y.S.2d 379; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1287



September 29, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion for a stay is denied and petitioner is directed to comply with the order of the Superintendent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner underwriting association, citing N.Y. Ins. Law §§ 34, 651-658, filed an application for a stay in its proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 to review and vacate a determination and order of respondent Superintendent of Insurance of the State of New York that the underwriting association provide increased fire and excess coverage insurance to respondent insured.


OVERVIEW: The underwriting association was created to promote community development by providing fire and extended coverage insurance for insurable properties necessary to attract private capital to central city areas. The underwriting association urged that it and its members would be irreparably harmed if a stay was not granted pending appellate review because it would be compelled to write, against its considered judgment, on property it considered more than usually hazardous, double the amount of insurance it desired to write after careful and thorough consideration. The court denied the motion. The court found that no stay was warranted which would impede the implementation of the experimental legislation, particularly in the light of its purposes.The court pointed out that an increase in insurance limits would be appropriately compensated by premiums. The court determined that a stay would unduly injure the interests of the people of the state.


OUTCOME: The court denied the underwriting association's motion for a stay of the Superintendent's determination and order that it provide the insured increased coverage, directed the underwriting association to comply with the order of the Superintendent, and ordered the transfer of the proceeding to the appellate division.


HEADNOTES

Insurance -- fire and extended insurance in distressed economic areas -- proceeding for judicial review of order of Superintendent of Insurance, directing New York Property Insurance Underwriting Association (Insurance Law, art. 17-B) to issue $ 800,000 policy to supermarket in distressed economic area, is transferred to Appellate Division, but association is ordered meantime to comply with such order of Superintendent of Insurance.

After a hearing, the Superintendent of Insurance ordered the New York Property Insurance Underwriting Association (Insurance Law, art. 17-B, §§ 651-658) to issue to a large supermarket located in a distressed economic area a policy of fire and extended insurance on the contents of its premises in the amount of $ 800,000, instead of the $ 400,000 limit which said association's appeals committee had approved. The association has instituted this judicial review proceeding, which concededly must be transferred to the Appellate Division. Pending the Appellate Division's determination, Special Term will not stay enforcement of the order of [***2] the Superintendent of Insurance. The store is ready to pay the increased premium. If it cannot obtain adequate insurance, the store may have to curtail its inventory, and this would diminish its service to the neighborhood and the volume of its business and require it to lay off employees. A principal purpose of article 17-B is to assure adequate fire and extended insurance, so that private capital may be attracted to distressed central city areas. The Superintendent's order is not patently unconstitutional. This judicial review proceeding is transferred to the Appellate Division, and meantime the association is ordered to comply with the Superintendent's order.

 

1820 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Roe v. Roe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, Kings County


65 Misc. 2d 335; 316 N.Y.S.2d 94; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1291



September 28, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner putative father filed an application to obtain a declaration of paternity and an order of filiation. The court, on its own motion, questioned the father's standing to originate the proceeding. The court designated a law guardian on behalf of a child to assist the court in resolving the question of standing insofar as the resolution of that question might also have affected the interests of the child pursuant to N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 249.


OVERVIEW: Respondent mother was married to a man other than the father at the time she gave birth to the child. She divorced her then husband and married the father, who alleged that he was the father of that child. The court stated that the "manner provided by law" for the establishment of paternity was found in N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act art. V. N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act art. V, § 522 directly related to the issue at hand. Clearly, the "manner provided by law" for the establishment of paternity did not permit the father to originate the proceeding. The court found that the father was not deprived of access to the laws and his remedy under N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act art. V was not his only remedy. An action for a declaratory judgment had been regarded as appropriate to determine the status of a child, including legitimacy, parentage, and the like pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3001. The action for a declaratory judgment in a case such as this would have been the more desirable remedy because in that action, the child, as well as the first husband of the mother, should have been made parties pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 1001(a). The court concluded that the father did not have standing to originate this proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the father's petition.


HEADNOTES

Children born out of wedlock -- paternity proceeding -- putative father of child has no standing to institute paternity proceeding.

A paternity proceeding cannot be maintained by a man for the purpose of adjudging that he is the father of the child who was born to his wife during her previous marriage (Family Ct. Act, §§ 511, 522, 523). In a paternity proceeding, neither the previous husband nor the child is a necessary party. If this man wishes to protect the child from a neglectful mother, he may bring a neglect proceeding. If he wishes custody of the child, he may institute a habeas corpus proceeding. If he wishes to obtain a binding adjudication of illegitimacy and support obligations and a determination as to who inherits from whom, he may institute a plenary action for a declaratory judgment against her and her previous husband and of course the child. But his paternity petition is dismissed.

 

1821 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Franco v. Board of Elections


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


64 Misc. 2d 19; 314 N.Y.S.2d 615; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1310



September 21, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate filed an application to validate an independent petition nominating him as a candidate of the Conservation Party for the office of District Court Judge in a general election. Respondent, the Board of Elections of the County of Nassau, contested the petition for candidacy.


OVERVIEW: The candidate presented an independent nominating petition seeking to have his name placed on the ballot in a third line as a candidate of the "Conservation Party" for the office of District Court Judge. The sheets presented on his behalf to the Board contained 1,617 signatures. The Board reviewed the petition and declared 450 of the signatures presented void for various reasons. The candidate filed an application to validate the petition. The candidate acknowledged that the valid signatures on his independent petition fell short of the statutory requirement of 1,500 voters, but contended that the legislative requirement that an independent candidate had to obtain a greater number of signatures than a regular party candidate was violative of the equal protection clause of the Federal Constitution. The court entered judgment for the Board and dismissed the candidate's petition, holding that N.Y. Elec. Law § 138(5)(c) was constitutional. Further, the candidate's use of the name "Conservation Party" in his petition violated N.Y. Elec. Law § 138(4) because the name was almost identical to that of the existing "Conservative Party."


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment in favor of the Board and dismissed the candidate's petition.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- party names -- statute requiring 1,500 signatures for independent nominating petition as against 1,000 for nominating petitions of regular parties is constitutional; since petitioner's independent nominating petition has less than 1,500, it is invalid -- petitioner cannot have third column on ballot -- attempted use of name "Conservation" for party violates Election Law ( § 138, subd. 4) because of similarity to "Conservative" party already in existence.

1. Section 138 (subd. 5, par. [c], cl. [1]) of the Election Law requires 1,500 signatures for a county office outside the City of New York on an independent nominating petition, but for a regular party candidate for such an office, the petition needs only 1,000 signatures (Election Law, § 136, subd. 2, par. [d]). The larger number of signatures required for an independent petition does not constitute a denial of the equal protection of the laws in violation of the Constitution. Section 138 (subd. 5, par. [c], cl. [1]) of the Election Law is constitutional. Since petitioner's petition lacked 1,500 valid signatures, it was properly rejected.

2. Since petitioner [***2] is already the candidate of two regular parties, the grant of this petition would place petitioner's name on the ballot in a third column which, under the circumstances, would violate section 248 of the Election Law.

3. The attempted use of the name "Conservation Party" violates subdivision 4 of section 138 of the Election Law which provides that the name selected for the independent body making the nomination "shall not include the name or part of the name * * * of a then existing party". The name "Conservation" is almost identical to the name "Conservative" for an already existing party. The use of the name "Conservation" would create confusion.

 

1822 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Udut v. Nyquist


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Niagara County


63 Misc. 2d 1066; 314 N.Y.S.2d 396; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1322



September 17, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion to dismiss the complaint is granted; motion for temporary injunction is denied. No costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents filed a preliminary injunction against defendants, a school superintendent and a school board and its president (school board), to restrain the school board from effectuating a plan to integrate schools through bussing. The school board filed a motion to dismiss the parents' complaint.


OVERVIEW: The school board adopted a plan that created circular attendance school districts and that transferred children from schools near their homes to other schools by means of bussing. The parents claimed that the plan was unconstitutional and violated N.Y. Educ. Law § 3201(2) (1969). The court granted the school board's motion to dismiss. The court held that the plan was promulgated to achieve and maintain racial integration of schools, that the plan achieved interracial understanding for the children, that the school board acted with care, caution, and utmost deliberation, and that the school board did not act arbitrarily or capriciously. The court also held that bussing under the plan did not extend beyond normal geographic school zones, that the plan promoted equal protection of the law, that the plan corrected racial imbalance, that § 3201(2) and the plan were constitutional, and that the parents' complaint was insufficient.


OUTCOME: The court granted the school board's motion to dismiss the parents' complaint and denied the parents' motion for a temporary injunction.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- racial imbalance -- bussing, in order to reduce racial imbalance or overcrowding, does not require prior request or permission of parents and does not contravene Education Law ( § 3201, subd. 2) -- class action by parents of two white children dismissed.

The elected Board of Education of the School District of the City of Niagara Falls, whose 21 elementary schools have about 9,000 pupils, is now, at the opening of schools in September, 1970, bussing about 1,300 of its pupils among 8 of its schools, in order to reduce racial imbalances and overcrowding. State aid for this plan amounts to $ 94,338, and Federal aid for this plan amounts to $ 88,000, and the contracts for the bussing alone involve $ 109,000. Aids or helpers are on busses to protect pupils. A purported class action by the parents of two such transferred white children, for an injunction against the whole plan, is dismissed. An injunction now would disrupt the city's whole educational system. The board's plan is sound, reasonable, and in accord with constitutional principles, and it does not contravene [***2] the Education Law ( § 3201, subd. 2), since said subdivision states that "nothing contained in this section shall prevent the assignment of a pupil in the manner requested or authorized by his parents or guardian"; that is, this subdivision does not require prior parental request or permission for the operation of the plan.

 

1823 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Beltrand


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, New York County


63 Misc. 2d 1041; 314 N.Y.S.2d 276; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1334



September 14, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion to suppress is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by an information with possession of a dangerous drug, possession of a hypodermic instrument, criminal trespass, possession of burglars tools, and loitering in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 240.35(6). Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the information and a motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: A police officer observed defendant in the lobby of a city housing project carrying a box containing women's clothing and carrying a woman's coat over his arm. The officer found a screwdriver, a hypodermic needle, a syringe, a bottle cap, and cotton containing heroin in the box. Defendant claimed that § 240.35(6) was unconstitutional and that the evidence was seized as a result of an unlawful search and seizure. The court granted in part defendant's motion to dismiss and granted defendant's motion to suppress. The court held that: (1) § 240.35(6), which made it a crime to loiter "in or about a place without apparent reason," was vague, indefinite, and uncertain; (2) § 240.35(6), which provided that a person could be arrested for "circumstances that justify suspicion," did not amount to probable cause; (3) § 240.35(6) did not define a crime and failed to provide the necessary standards by which the prohibited conduct could be tested; and (4) § 240.35(6) was unconstitutional. The court also held that no lawful order was given to defendant to not enter the building, that defendant could not be held on the charge of criminal trespass, and that the search and seizure were illegal.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion to dismiss the information as to the charges of loitering and criminal trespass. The court granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized in the search.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- loitering -- information charging loitering not dismissed since some evidence justifies charge -- loitering statute (Penal Law, § 240.35, subd. 6) is vague and unconstitutional -- arrest for criminal trespass did not justify search and seizure, hallway of multiple dwelling being public place within trespass statute -- search and seizure were illegal and contraband seized is suppressed.

1. An information charging defendant with loitering (Penal Law, § 240.35, subd. 6) in the lobby of a building will not be dismissed, there being some evidence that defendant was loitering, that circumstances existed justifying the officer's suspicion that defendant was engaged in a crime (i.e., an anonymous call that someone was selling stolen property at that address) and that defendant failed to give a reasonably credible account of his conduct.

2. Subdivision 6 of section 240.35 of the Penal Law states that a person is guilty of loitering when he "Loiters * * * in or about a place without apparent reason and under circumstances which justify suspicion that he may be engaged or about to engage in crime". The phrase "in or about [***2] a place without apparent reason" is vague, indefinite and uncertain and, consequently, unconstitutional. Moreover a statute providing that a person may be arrested by reason of "circumstances which justify suspicion" of the commission of a crime is unconstitutional. An arrest to be valid depends on whether the officers had probable cause to make it.

3. The arrest for criminal trespass (Penal Law, § 140.10) did not validate the search and seizure. The hallways of multiple dwellings must be considered public places within the trespass statute. Defendant cannot be held for trial on the charge of criminal trespass. The charges of loitering and criminal trespass are dismissed.

4. The search and seizure incidental to an unlawful arrest were illegal and a motion to suppress the contraband seized is granted.

 

1824 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re C.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, New York County


63 Misc. 2d 1019; 314 N.Y.S.2d 255; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1340



September 10, 1970 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Department of Social Services of New York City, New York, filed an adoption proceeding against respondent mother after the mother's child was removed from her custody as a result of neglect.


OVERVIEW: The mother was a narcotics addict whose child had been removed from her custody for neglect. The Department sought to place the child for adoption through a nonsectarian agency. The Department claimed that the mother's consent was not required under N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 111. The mother claimed that N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 116 required that the child be placed with a Catholic agency and be adopted by Catholics. The court ordered that the child be placed for adoption through the nonsectarian agency. The court held that the mother and her counsel were notified that N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 111 would be considered, that an extensive hearing on the issue of consent was held, that the mother would not ever be able to provide stable and suitable care for the child, and that § 111 authorized the adoption of the child without the mother's consent. The court also held that adoptive parents were not available through the Catholic agency, that the nonsectarian agency offered to place the child in an adoptive home, and that N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 116 authorized the placement of the child through the nonsectarian agency with adoptive parents of a different religion.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the child be placed for adoption through the nonsectarian agency with adoptive parents of a different religion.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Infants -- child neglect -- placement for adoption -- out-of-wedlock child, now almost three years old, neglected by its narcotic-addicted Puerto Rican Catholic mother, shall be placed with nonsectarian agency for possible adoption by only apparently available couple, Puerto Rican Protestant husband and Jewish wife.

1. A child was born out of wedlock to a Puerto Rican woman who is admittedly a narcotics addict and who has been receiving aid-to-dependent-children welfare moneys since the child's birth, and who has been repeatedly asked to undertake rehabilitative treatment and has repeatedly failed to do so. The father too was a narcotics addict and for the past two years he has been in Sing Sing Prison. Since the child's birth, the mother has been incarcerated several times for prostitution, robbery, and possession of narcotic drugs. At the age of two the child was hospitalized and the abject neglect in which he had been born and reared was revealed and this neglect proceeding was commenced. The child is now almost three years old. The mother deems herself to be a Catholic; however, no Catholic agency has been found which can give assurance that it can find adoptive parents [***2] for this child. On the other hand, the Windham Children's Service, a nonsectarian agency of high standing, offers to place the child almost immediately in an adoptive home, because this agency has already studied and approved a husband and wife -- he a Puerto Rican Protestant and she a Jew -- who are applying to adopt a Puerto Rican child. After due notice and hearings (Family Ct. Act, § 1044 et seq.) the Family Court directs that this child be placed with said Windham Children's Service for adoption.

2. In these exigent circumstances, and after due notice to the mother and full hearings (Family Ct. Act, § 1044 et seq.), the consents of the mother and father of this out-of-wedlock, neglected child, to the adoption, can be dispensed with (Domestic Relations Law, § 111).

3. Such placement is "practicable" and in the "best interests of the child" (Family Ct. Act, § 116, subds. [a], [e], [g]). There is no ground consistent with the United States Constitution (1st and 14th Amdts.) for attributing "religious wishes" to an adoptive child of such tender age.

 

1825 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Winston


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Monroe County


64 Misc. 2d 150; 314 N.Y.S.2d 489; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1349



September 3, 1970 



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the City Court of Rochester convicting the defendant of the crime of inciting to riot in violation of section 240.08 is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Rochester City Court, Criminal Branch (New York), which convicted him of the crime of inciting to riot in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 240.08.


OVERVIEW: At a popular music concert at a war memorial, the crowd became unruly. Rocks and bottles were thrown. Defendant urged the crowd on, and the police arrested him. Defendant was convicted of inciting to riot in violation of § 240.08. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that defendant's words and conduct were designed to further incite a turbulent crowd and to re-enter the war memorial by physically overwhelming the police. The People had presented a prima facie case against defendant. Section 240.08 was consistent with the First Amendment. Because defense counsel had not objected at trial, defendant could not succeed on his claims that the district attorney had improperly used leading questions and had failed to comply with N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 813-f.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- inciting to riot -- judgment of Rochester City Court, on verdict of guilty of urging 10 or more persons to engage in tumultuous and violent conduct (Penal Law, § 240.08), is affirmed by Monroe County Court -- statute is constitutional -- defense counsel did not object to District Attorney's failure to give advance notice that People would offer confession in evidence (Code Crim. Pro., § 813-f).

1. Section 240.08 of the Penal Law ("Inciting to riot") is constitutional and was validly and constitutionally applied to this case. Defendant, by words and acts, urged "ten or more persons to engage in tumultuous and violent conduct of a kind likely to create public alarm." At a musical concert in an auditorium, after security guards had scuffled with a person in the audience and [***2] had taken such person into a room, defendant successfully urged the crowd to attack the guards and the police who arrived. The verdict of guilty was amply supported by the evidence. Judgment of the Rochester City Court, convicting defendant of inciting to riot, is affirmed by the Monroe County Court.

2. Although the District Attorney had failed to notify defendant in advance that the People would offer a confession or admission in evidence (Code Crim. Pro., § 813-f), defense counsel made no objection at the trial; and no claim is now made that defense counsel was incompetent.

A. E. Nettleton Co. v. Diamond


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Onondaga County


63 Misc. 2d 885; 313 N.Y.S.2d 893; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1369



August 25, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] There being no questions of fact presented by the parties hereto, and the questions of law having been decided herein, judgment is granted declaring section 358-a of the Agriculture and Markets Law unconstitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company sought a judgment declaring, inter alia, N.Y. Agric. & Mkts. Law § 358-a unconstitutional and to enjoin enforcement of its provisions. The company then brought on a motion to enjoin enforcement of the statue, pending a disposition of the original action for declaratory judgment.


OVERVIEW: The paramount consideration in this case was whether the Mason Act was violative of due process or is a valid exercise of the police power. The court held that to the extent the Mason Act included all 27 subspecies of crocodylia, none of which were indigenous to New York State and without regard to whether they are endangered or not, it was arbitrary. The court found that the Mason Act had no significant relation to the health, safety or general welfare of citizens of New York State. Since the Mason Act failed to justify its existence as a valid exercise of the police power and since it did materially interfere with the property rights of the company, it violated the Due Process Clause of the 14th Amendment of the United States Constitution, and N.Y. Const. Art. 1, § 6. There being no questions of fact presented by the parties, and the questions of law having been decided, judgment was granted declaring N.Y. Agric. & Mkts. Law § 358-a unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgement in favor of the company, finding the statute in question to be unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- alligator shoes -- plaintiff manufactures, in New York State, shoes made of hides of species of alligators which are indigenous to South America and which have not been designated as endangered species (U. S. Code, tit. 16, § 668aa et seq.); as applied to such shoes, section 358-a of our Agriculture and Markets Law is unconstitutional and void.

 Section 358-a of the Agriculture and Markets Law prohibits, under criminal and forfeiture penalties, the sale or the manufacture of any product made from the skins or hides of alligators or crocodiles. Plaintiff manufactures in New York State shoes made of the hides of two species of alligators or crocodiles known as tinga and tinga alligator, and otherwise known as caiman latirostris and caiman sclerops. Neither of these two species has been designated as endangered species by the United States Secretary of the Interior pursuant to the Endangered Species Conservation Act of 1969 (U. S. Code,  [***2] tit. 16, § 668aa et seq.). Alligators and crocodiles are not indigenous to New York State; in fact, the afore-mentioned two species are indigenous to South America. As applied to such hides purchased by plaintiff and such shoes manufactured and sold by plaintiff, section 358-a of our Agriculture and Markets Law is confiscatory, unreasonable, unconstitutional and invalid (U. S. Const., 14th Amdt.; N. Y. Const., art. I, § 6).

De Kosenko v. Brandt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


63 Misc. 2d 895; 313 N.Y.S.2d 827; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1424



July 29, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a female litigant, challenged the constitutionality of N.Y. Jud. Law § 599(7), which permitted women to claim exemption from jury service.


OVERVIEW: The litigant contended that the jury service exemption denied her the right to a trial by a jury of her peers, in violation of N.Y. Const. art. I, § 1, and deprived her of equal protection of the laws under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and N.Y. Const. art. I, § 2. The court ruled, however, that exemption of women from jury service did not constitute an unconstitutional exclusion. The court reviewed case law on similar exemptions and concluded that the prerogative of a woman to exempt herself from jury service was widely recognized.


OUTCOME: The court denied the litigant's motion challenging the jury service exemption.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- jury -- women's right to claim exemption from jury service (Judiciary Law, § 599, subd. 7) is constitutional.

This is a civil action in the New York Supreme Court, triable by jury. The plaintiff, a female, contends that the statutory right of all women who are called to jury service to claim exemption therefrom (Judiciary Law, § 599, subd. 7) will, in the ordinary course of events, result in a jury pool in which only 19% are women, and that such statutory exemption will, in effect, deny to her her constitutional rights to a trial by a jury of her peers and to the equal protection of the laws (N. Y. Const., art. I, § 2; U. S. Const., 14th Amdt.; cf. Civil Rights Law, § 13); wherefore she asks the court to annul and disregard such statutory exemption. However, the United States Supreme Court has already upheld the constitutionality of subdivision 7 of section 599 of the Judiciary Law. Accordingly, her motion is denied.

 

1828 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Summers v. Wyman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


64 Misc. 2d 67; 314 N.Y.S.2d 430; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1433



July 27, 1970 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner welfare recipient brought a class action to compel the county social services commissioner to withhold from her monthly assistance grant sufficient funds to pay her utility bills. The utility company brought an action against the recipient for unpaid arrears on her utility bills.


OVERVIEW: The recipient had previously participated in a practice known as "withhold" whereby parties who were deemed financially incapable of handling money had a portion of their benefits withheld for the purposes of paying their utility bills directly to the utility companies. After the program ceased, the recipients utilities were cut off. The recipient claimed that the refusal of the commission to grant "withhold" status to recipients with demonstrated inability to handle cash violated applicable statutes and regulations. The recipient also sought a declaration that refusing to give utility service to persons who were in arrears in payments of previous bills was unconstitutional discrimination against poor persons. The court denied class status but ruled in favor of the individual recipient finding that pursuant to N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 18, § 381.2 (a) it was mandatory that "withhold" should follow demonstrated inability to handle cash. The court also failed to find any evidence on which to characterize any legally offensive inadequacy of utility service provisions.


OUTCOME: The court denied class status but held that the commissioner was obligated to withhold sufficient funds to pay the recipients utility bills on a finding that the recipient had previously been judged incompetent to handle her financial matters.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Social services -- withholding of utility payments from recipient's allowance -- petitioner recipient of welfare who cannot handle cash is not entitled to maintain class action to compel Commissioner of Social Services to withhold sums for utility payments -- proceeding is not time barred -- exhaustion of petitioner's administrative remedies is not required -- under regulation of State Commissioner of Social Services which preceded enactment of 1969 statute allegedly forbidding such withholding, County Commissioner has authority to withhold utility payments for welfare recipients shown to be unable to handle cash; county is directed to withhold -- back utility allowances must be paid by county as emergency payment -- petition dismissed against State Commissioner of Social Services -- utility does not discriminate against poor by discontinuing service for nonpayment -- petitioner cannot run up excess utility charge -- judgment on utility's counterclaim against petitioner granted on default -- utility's cross claim against county is severed so county may have opportunity to answer.

1. Petitioner, a recipient of public assistance who claims that she is unable to handle cash and [***2] seeks a judgment directing the County and State Commissioners of Social Services to withhold from her monthly allowances sufficient sums to pay her lighting utility bill, is not entitled to maintain a class action in behalf of all those similarly situated. The proceeding will continue for petitioner alone.

2. The County Commissioner's assertion that the proceeding is time barred because petitioner knew of his decision to terminate "withhold" status in July, 1969 is rejected. The need to demand "withhold" status did not arise until May, 1970 when the utility threatened termination of services. The demand then made was timely and this proceeding was commenced within four months.

3. Petitioner was not required to exhaust her administrative remedies before resort to litigation.

4. Section 131-a (subd. 1) of the Social Services Law, enacted effective July 1, 1969, provides that payment of public assistance shall be made in monthly allowances in accordance with standards established by regulation but not in excess of the schedules and that such schedules "shall be * * * exclusive of shelter and fuel for heating". A regulation of the State ( 18 NYCRR 381.2 [a]), despite this section,  [***3] remained unchanged and provided that when the recipient was shown to be unable to handle cash, payment of all or part shall be withheld, to insure payments to meet a threatened shut-off of utility services ( 18 NYCRR 381.2 [b]). No inconsistency exists between the statute and the regulation. The county thus had authority to withhold the utility allowance despite the enactment of the statute. The matter is not within the discretion of the commissioner for the regulation is mandatory that "withhold" shall follow demonstrated inability to handle cash. The county is directed to resume "withhold" of utility payments.

5. The back utility allowances which should have been withheld shall be paid to the utility by the county as an emergency payment. Since the county knew that petitioner was unable to handle her own money, by insisting that she pay her own utility bills, the county is equally responsible for the current delinquency.

6. Since the State has not been called upon to act, has not refused to perform any act directed by law nor has acted illegally as to petitioner, the petition against the State is dismissed.

7. Petitioner is not entitled to a determination that the utility,  [***4] by terminating service to persons who are in arrears, discriminates against the poor. Since the publicly assisted poor receive utility allowances, they are not deprived of such services because they are poor.

8. Petitioner may not run up an excess charge for utility services and expect full reimbursement from the county.

9. A counterclaim is now authorized in an article 78 CPLR proceeding ( CPLR 7804) and since petitioner has failed to reply to the utility's counterclaim for arrears, the utility is entitled to judgment against petitioner by default.

10. The utility's cross claim against the county for assuming liability is not authorized and may be made only by permission, which the court grants but in the absence of an answer from the county, which it should have an opportunity to interpose, the cross claim is severed.

 

1829 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. McGuire


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, Long Beach, Nassau County


63 Misc. 2d 639; 313 N.Y.S.2d 56; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1439



July 24, 1970 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with using a surfboard in the waters adjacent to the city beach, in violation of Long Beach, N.Y., Municipal Code ch. 6, art. 1, § 6-113.2(c).


OVERVIEW: The complaining witnesses claimed that defendants were surfing on their surfboards approximately 75 feet from the shore line of the beachfront of the city. Defendants contended that the city had no jurisdiction beyond the mean high water line of the ocean and that § 6-113.2(c) was unconstitutional because the city was attempting to exercise jurisdiction beyond its geographical limits. The court found defendants guilty of violating § 6-113.2(c). The court concluded that under N.Y. Gen. City Law § 20(8), the state delegated to the cities powers to administer and control the waters adjacent to the beach. Thus, Long Beach, N.Y., Municipal Code ch. 6, art. 1, § 6-113.2(c) was constitutional as a proper exercise of the police power by the city. Because defendants were surfing in the waters adjacent to the beach, they violated § 6-113.2(c).


OUTCOME: The court found defendants guilty of violating the statute prohibiting use of a surfboard in the waters adjacent to the city beach.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- regulation of waterfront -- City of Long Beach had power to regulate waterfront to distance of three miles and section of Municipal Code forbidding use of surfboards without license adjacent to beach park is constitutional; defendants are found guilty of violating section.

Subdivision (c) of section 6-113.2 of the Long Beach Municipal Code, which forbids the use of surfboards without a license in the waters adjacent to Ocean Beach Park, is not unconstitutional as an attempt, as defendants contend, to exercise jurisdiction beyond the mean high water line which line, defendants contend, is the southerly boundary of the city limits. Section 7-a of the State Law gives the State jurisdiction to a line three miles from the coast line. By subdivision 8 of section 20 of the General City Law, cities were granted power to regulate utilization of the waterways, and the Legislature by adopting the Charter of the City of Long Beach gave it exclusive control over its public waters. The section of the Municipal Code is a proper exercise of the police power and since defendants were surfing in the waters adjacent to the beach, they violated the section and are [***2] found guilty.

 

1830 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Kennilworth Management Co. v. Ithaca


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Tompkins County


63 Misc. 2d 617; 313 N.Y.S.2d 35; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1444



July 22, 1970 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners filed a motion for summary judgment in their declaratory judgment action seeking a determination that they were entitled to receive water and sewer services from defendant city based on the terms of a standard water contract after the city refused to provide those services based on an alleged shortage of water.


OVERVIEW: The city and an outside water district signed a standard contract for the provision of water and sewer services to the district. Although the property owners' land was located within that water district, the city denied water and sewer services to them. The property owners filed a declaratory judgment action seeking a ruling that they were entitled to the services, but the court dismissed the action, holding that the property owners did not have an absolute contractual right to receive water from the city. The court determined that the city had the broad right to discontinue the supply of water to consumers living outside the municipal boundaries. The sale of surplus water outside the city was an activity expressly legalized by statute and was subject to the ever-present limitation that the rights and interests of city inhabitants came first. It was not unreasonable or arbitrary for the city to look to the future of its water supply before committing itself to an extension of service that could cause trouble in the future. The court refused to comment upon whether the property owners had a cause of action for damages based on breach of the city's contract with the district.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the property owners' complaint seeking a declaratory judgment that they were entitled to receive water and sewer services from the city based on the terms of a standard water contract.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- right of nonresident of city to water -- plaintiffs, whose properties are located in water district with which defendant city contracted to sell surplus water, are not entitled to water service where city determined that its water supply was endangered -- court cannot say that city is not acting in good faith -- since plaintiffs are not users of water they are not entitled to notice of city's intention to discontinue service; no breach of contract resulted -- complaint in action for declaratory judgment is dismissed.

1. Defendant city, which entered into a contract with another water district, in which plaintiffs' properties are located, to supply it with its excess water, is not obligated to supply water to plaintiffs. The sale of surplus water outside the city limits is subject to the limitation that the rights and interests of city residents come first. Plaintiffs have no absolute contractual right to receive water from the city once the city has determined, as here, that its water supply would be endangered by a further extension within the other water district.

2. The court cannot say that the city is not acting in good faith in making its [***2] determination not to extend its water facilities further.

3. While the provision of the contract calling for notice of the city's intention to discontinue service because of danger to its own supply, coupled with its agreement to use reasonable diligence to continue the supply until a new source could be found, was intended as a protection to outside consumers depending on the city source, there is no point in requiring notice since plaintiffs are not yet consumers of city water. The failure to give notice of an intention to refuse further extension is not a breach of the contract under the circumstances here.

4. The complaint seeking declaratory judgment is insufficient in law insofar as plaintiffs rely on the contract and the court declines as a matter of discretion to pass judgment on the other issues raised.

 

1831 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Kraemer v. Office of Employee Relations


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


63 Misc. 2d 708; 313 N.Y.S.2d 302; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1448; 75 L.R.R.M. 2283



July 21, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The action (changed herein from an article 78 proceeding to an equitable action for injunction) is dismissed without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the president of a labor union council, filed a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 seeking to annul a provision of an agreement between respondent, the Office of Employee Relations, and a certified labor union, which required a state employee to be exclusively represented by the certified labor union in processing contract grievances. The president also sought to enjoin the Office from carrying out that portion of the contract.


OVERVIEW: Elections were conducted, and the certified union was duly elected to represent certain units of state employees. On behalf of the state, respondent Director of Employee Relations entered into contracts with the certified union with respect to each of the units of state employees. The contracts required a state employee to be exclusively represented by the certified union in processing contract grievances. The president sought to annul the exclusivity provisions of the contracts and to enjoin respondents from carrying out the provisions. He contended that a public employee had a right to select an employee organization for representation and that the challenged provisions abridged that right in violation of public policy. The court held that the contracts did no violate the rights of a state employee and dismissed the president's action. The court noted that there was no denial to any state employee of his right to join any employee organization and that there was no denial of his right to press his grievance against the state. However, once elected, the certified union was empowered to contract with the state on all employment matters including the grievance procedure.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the action.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- representation of State employees -- provision in collectively negotiated agreements between State and Civil Service Employees Association, that no employee organization other than latter might initiate or represent State employees in processing contract grievances, does not impose unreasonable or unconstitutional limitation upon rights of State employee to select employee organization and press his grievances against State -- article 78 proceeding is not proper vehicle to attack validity of contract -- court treats proceeding to annul said provision as action in equity for injunction and dismisses it.

1. A provision, contained in each of several collectively negotiated agreements entered into by the State and the Civil Service Employees Association (CSEA), the duly elected collective negotiations representative of State employees in various units, that "No employee organization other than CSEA may initiate or represent an employee in the processing of contract grievances" does not impose an unreasonable or unconstitutional limitation [***2] upon the rights of a State employee to select an employee organization and press his grievances against the State.

2. Since an article 78 proceeding is not the proper vehicle to attack the validity of a contract, the court treats a proceeding to annul said provision, brought by the president of another employee organization, as an action in equity for an injunction, and dismisses the action.

 

1832 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Luria


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Surrogate's Court of New York, Kings County


63 Misc. 2d 675; 313 N.Y.S.2d 12; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1454



July 15, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The executor's request to strike the demand for jury trial is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner widow filed an action objecting to an account filed by respondent executor and demanded a jury trial. The case went before the court on the widow's jury trial demand.


OVERVIEW: Decedent made a trust provision for decedent's widow in decedent's will. The widow elected against the will, and her right to election was upheld. The executor filed an account, and the widow filed objections concerning securities listed as assets of the estate. The widow by her claim sought to impress a trust on the securities to the extent that the securities were purchased with the widow's funds. The case went before the court on the widow's jury demand. The court granted the executor's request to strike the jury demand. The court held that the widow waived her right to jury trial by not commencing an action at law but instead advancing her claim on the judicial settlement of the account. The widow's claim was not at law but for equitable relief against the executor for an accounting as the fiduciary of the estate. The widow would not be entitled to a jury trial in an action for the same relief against her deceased husband if her husband were alive. The relief requested would require the court to determine the extent of the widow's interest in the securities which would be measured in turn by money relief, not by awarding title to specific securities.


OUTCOME: The court granted the executor's request to strike the widow's demand for a jury trial in the widow's action objecting to the executor's account.


HEADNOTES

Trial -- trial by jury -- widow of decedent, who has filed objections to account of his executor concerning securities listed therein as assets of his estate, alleged that she and her husband had commingled savings pursuant to agreement that securities purchased with joint funds would be owned jointly -- looking at nature and substance of claim, it is one to impress trust on securities to extent of her interest therein and for accounting by executor as fiduciary of estate -- since relief is cognizable only in equity, she is not entitled to trial by jury -- in any event, she has waived right to jury trial by advancing claim on judicial settlement of account -- right is waived where claim for equitable relief is combined with one at law.

1. The widow of a decedent has filed objections to the account of his executor, concerning securities listed therein as assets of his estate. Without claiming title to any specific securities, she alleges that she and her husband had commingled their savings pursuant to an agreement that securities purchased with their joint funds would be owned jointly, but that he [***2] had sold some which had been purchased in their joint names and purchased others in his individual name. Looking at the nature and substance of her claim, which is determinative of whether she has the right to a trial by jury, it is one to impress a trust on the securities to the extent of her interest therein and for an accounting by the executor as a fiduciary of the estate. Since this relief is cognizable only in equity, she is not entitled to a trial by jury.

2. Even if her claim were to be regarded as one at law, as an action for money only, she has waived any right to a jury trial by advancing it on the judicial settlement of the executor's account rather than by commencing an action at law.

3. The right to trial by jury is waived where a claim for equitable relief is combined with one at law.

 

1833 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Crystal Lake Camp Corp. v. Silver


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Civil Court of the City of New York, Special Term, New York County


63 Misc. 2d 562; 313 N.Y.S.2d 68; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1465



July 13, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons set forth, I grant the motion to vacate the service and to dismiss the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation sought damages in an action alleging that defendant customer breached a contract that provided for attendance by her son at the corporation's camp. The customer filed a motion to dismiss the complaint on the ground of lack of personal jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The customer was a resident of Nassau County, the corporation had offices in New York County and Queens County, the contract was executed at the corporation's Queens county office, and the camp was located in a community not within the boundaries of New York City. The court dismissed the corporation's complaint because the court did not have jurisdiction under the long-arm statutes of N.Y. C.P.L.R. 302 and N.Y. City Civ. Ct. Act § 404(a). The court held that the only event that linked the action to New York City was the execution of the contract and that there was no evidence that the customer had purposely availed herself of the privilege of conducting activities within the city, so as to invoke the benefits and protections of its laws. The court also found that the customer was not transacting business within the meaning of § 404(a) to allow long-arm jurisdiction because her activity in the city was not profit making or commercial in any way.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the service on the customer and granted the customer's motion to dismiss the corporation's complaint for breach of contract.


HEADNOTES

Courts -- jurisdiction -- transaction of business -- mother residing in Nassau County who enters Queens County to sign contract for son's attendance at up-State children's camp was not transacting business in New York City and New York City Civil Court did not acquire jurisdiction of her.

The long-arm section (404) of the New York City Civil Court Act does not give the court jurisdiction of a mother, residing in Nassau County, who comes to Queens County where a second office of the operator of a children's summer camp is located, to sign a contract for her son's attendance at the camp, located in up-State New York. By such act defendant mother was not transacting any business in Queens County.
