Smithtown v. Serby


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


District Court of New York, Fourth District, Suffolk County


64 Misc. 2d 734; 315 N.Y.S.2d 445; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1492



June 29, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The defendant's motion is denied in its entirety.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with violations of Smithtown, N.Y., Code ch. 54, §§ 54-3, 56-6-A in allowing certain premises to be used as a physician's office. Defendant submitted a motion to vacate a search warrant and to dismiss the information.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a physician, maintained an office in a residential district. The court issued a search warrant authorizing a town investigator to search the premises to establish a violation of the town's building zone ordinance. Defendant was later charged with violating the ordinance in that he did not reside at the premises and thus, the office was not a home professional office. Defendant submitted a motion to vacate the search warrant and to dismiss the information on the grounds that it was defective and based on an unconstitutional ordinance. The court held that the town's building zone ordinance was constitutional, despite the fact that it did not define the term "resident," because it was clear in its meaning and its intent. The court also held that the granting of the search warrant was reasonable because the same high standards for reasonable grounds required in a criminal matter were not required in a building or zoning violation.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- search warrant to inspect building -- search warrant may issue, authorizing town inspector to examine house which defendant physician purports to use both as residence and office, under zoning ordinance.

A search warrant may issue, authorizing a town investigator to inspect a house which defendant physician occupies as both residence and office in asserted compliance with the town's zoning ordinance. The physician's motion, on constitutional grounds, to vacate the warrant and dismiss the information, is denied.

 

1835 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


New Rochelle v. Sigel


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


65 Misc. 2d 962; 319 N.Y.S.2d 208; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1511



June 24, 1970 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owners sought an order directing respondent city to pay just compensation at the time of the vesting of title for property taken by it in advance of an award by commissioners pursuant to a local law contained in the city charter.


OVERVIEW: The local law provided that title passed to the city upon the qualification of commissioners appointed and upon the appointment the city could enter into and take possession of the property. Title to the owners' property had been taken by the city, and the owners sought advance compensation before the commissioners, based on the amount of the lowest appraisal finally fixed the amount. The city asserted that such compensation was not provided for in the local law, thus, could not be paid. The court granted the owners' petition. The court held that in enacting the local law, the city could not ignore fundamental common law, statutory, and constitutional provisions, which provide for prompt and just compensation when title vests. The court noted that N.Y. Condemn. Law § 24 required a deposit for partial compensation when possession was taken, thus, such partial compensation should have been made when the city actually took title under its local law.


OUTCOME: The court granted the owners' petition directing the city to pay just compensation at the time of the vesting of title for property taken by it in advance of an award by commissioners pursuant to a local law contained in the city charter.


HEADNOTES

Eminent domain -- advance payment -- despite lack of provision for advance payment of award (New Rochelle City Charter, § 171, as amd.), court directs city to pay in advance 75% of amount of city's appraisal.

Section 171 of the New Rochelle City Charter, as amended, provides that the City Council may, by resolution, declare its intent to acquire real property by condemnation, and may further declare that the title to the real property shall pass to the [***2] city upon the qualification of the Commissioners appointed to condemn the property. The section further provides that, thereupon, the city may take possession of the property, and that the Commissioners shall add interest to their awards at 4% per annum from the date of their qualification (Local Laws, 1964, No. 4 of City of New Rochelle). Other statutes -- but not this one -- provide for a 75% advance payment (cf. Highway Law, § 30, subd. 13; Public Housing Law, § 125, subd. 2; Agriculture and Markets Law, § 27, subd. 12; Mental Hygiene Law, § 46, subd. 12; see, also, Condemnation Law, §§ 15, 24, 27). The court directs the city to pay the property owner, in advance, 75% of the amount of the city's appraisal of his property.

 

1836 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fiorillo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Montgomery County


63 Misc. 2d 480; 311 N.Y.S.2d 574; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1512



June 23, 1970 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants in a criminal action challenged the court's issuance of eavesdropping warrants upon application by the county's district attorney.


OVERVIEW: The district attorney was authorized in the warrants as the law enforcement agency to intercept certain communications. Defendants alleged that the eavesdropping warrants should have specified the names of the persons authorized to execute the warrants, should have been limited in scope as to what communications could be intercepted, and should have contained a provision for termination after seizure of a specific conversation. The court rejected defendants' objections to the warrants, holding that: (1) the warrants were clearly limited as to time, place, and subject matter within the meaning and limits of N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 819(6); (2) proof of a conspiracy to promote gambling required a broad investigation requiring many contracts of gambling and many communications and conversations, and the interception should not have automatically terminated upon the first conversation which involved gambling; and (3) it was within the court's discretion to direct in the warrants that the eavesdropping should continue beyond that first conversation and up to a period of 30 days so that the desired and authorized objective could be obtained.


OUTCOME: The court overruled defendants' objections to the warrants.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- eavesdropping -- eavesdropping warrants need not name persons authorized to execute them -- defendants have no standing to object to eavesdropping of conversations with persons not connected with gambling conspiracy -- direction that warrants continue for 30 days was within discretion of court -- warrants are limited as to time, place and subject matter.

1. Eavesdropping warrants need not specifically name the persons authorized to execute the warrants. The statute does not require it and it is impractical.

2. Even if communications not subject to interception are received under the warrants from some outside person not involved in the gambling conspiracy, defendants have no standing to protest.

3. It was within the court's discretion to direct in the warrants that the eavesdropping should continue beyond the first interception involving gambling and up to 30 days so that proof that a conspiracy to promote gambling existed could be adduced.

4. These warrants are not general but are limited as to time, place and subject matter within the meaning of the statute.

 

1837 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. McCray


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Rockland County


63 Misc. 2d 803; 313 N.Y.S.2d 772; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1523



June 18, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the defendant's motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by a sealed indictment with the crime of criminally selling a dangerous drug in the third degree, a class C felony. He was arrested after the issuance of a bench warrant, pursuant to N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 300. Defendant brought a motion to dismiss the indictment based upon the People's failure to timely bring defendant before the court for an arraignment.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's arrest on the bench warrant, he remained in custody for 13 days before he was brought before the court for an arraignment when the court unofficially learned of defendant's confinement. During confinement, defendant was not advised of his constitutional rights, and he was not afforded an opportunity to retain counsel or to have bail set. Defendant was not interrogated or subjected to any police activity during his confinement. Defendant, at arraignment, alleged no single instance of specific prejudice resulting from his confinement in which his ability to adequately defend himself against the crime was impaired. Although the court did not condone the delay in the arraignment, the court refused to dismiss the indictment merely because of the delay where the delay was not purposeful. The court found that a district attorney had authority under N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 300 to procure a bench warrant and that, when the process was undertaken, the People had the primary, but not the exclusive, duty to bring defendant before the court without unnecessary delay, as required by N.Y. Crim. Proc. §§ 165, 301.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- bench warrant issued by District Attorney -- District Attorney may issue bench warrant to arrest indicted defendant (Code Crim. Pro., § 300); statute is constitutional -- District Attorney's warrant should expressly direct prompt arraignment -- in instant case, during 13 days which elapsed between arrest and arraignment nothing occurred to prejudice defendant's constitutional rights; hence, indictment will not be dismissed.

1. When a Grand Jury has brought in a felony indictment, a bench warrant for the arrest of the defendant may be issued by the District Attorney, without prior application to the court (Code Crim. Pro., § 300). This statutory provision is constitutional.

2. The court is of the opinion that, in such case, the District Attorney's warrant should expressly direct that the defendant shall be arraigned "without unnecessary delay" (cf. Code Crim. Pro., § 165).

3. In the instant case, the District Attorney's warrant did not contain such a direction; and 13 days elapsed between the arrest and the arraignment. However, during those 13 days the defendant was not interrogated or coerced, and the delay [***2] did not seriously prejudice his statutory and constitutional rights to have counsel and to have bail fixed. Under the circumstances of this particular case, the defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment is denied.

 

1838 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Hepper v. Hillsdale


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Columbia County


63 Misc. 2d 447; 311 N.Y.S.2d 739; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1528



June 17, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion for summary judgment to the extent that such law be declared to be void is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town enacted an ordinance making it a misdemeanor to use any building, structure, or premises, directly or indirectly for the treatment, care, rehabilitation, or occupation by any person addicted to the use of any narcotic. Plaintiff, a self-help center operator, brought suit against the town, alleging substantial harm personally and to his enterprise. He sought judgment declaring the ordinance unconstitutional and void.


OVERVIEW: The self-help center operator ran a facility for individuals 16 years and older who were dependent on narcotics or drugs. He argued that the town's ordinance was unconstitutional, and the court agreed. Under art. 9 of the N.Y. Mental Hyg. Law § 200, the state had enacted a comprehensive program to protect the safety, morals, health, and general welfare of all the citizens of the state as they might be affected by narcotic or drug addiction. Therefore, the ordinance was pre-empted in this area of concern. The town took the position that drug and narcotic addiction was a social evil and that its ordinance was salutary in that it combated such evil. However, the court determined that the thrust and import of the act was not to regulate or control a drug rehabilitation center in the town but to prohibit such centers from operating. The purpose of the ordinance was inconsistent with the organic law of the state and, therefore, was unreasonable, arbitrary, and oppressive to a valid state purpose. The court held that the ordinance should be declared unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion for summary judgment to the extent that the ordinance be declared void.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- ordinance of town in conflict with State law -- town ordinance prohibiting drug addiction rehabilitation centers conflicts with Mental Hygiene Law (art. 9, § 200 et seq.) and is void -- complaint in action for declaratory judgment and answer present legal question only.

1. An ordinance of a town making it a misdemeanor to use premises for the treatment of persons addicted to drugs and imposing a fine of $ 100 per day for each violation is in conflict with section 200 et seq. of article 9 of the Mental Hygiene Law making it a purpose of the State to provide for the rehabilitation of drug addicts and providing for the treatment of addicts in State rehabilitation centers and in State approved privately operated facilities. The purpose of the ordinance is not regulate rehabilitation centers but to prohibit them from operating and is unreasonable, arbitrary and oppressive to a valid State purpose. The ordinance is void.

2. Plaintiff purchased real property in defendant town intending to use it as a rehabilitation center for drug addicts. The complaint,  [***2] in his action for judgment declaring the ordinance void, together with defendant's answer presents a justiciable controversy involving only a question of law. An action for declaratory judgment is proper and summary judgment is available for accelerating the determination of the controverted legal question.

 

1839 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Keystone Associates v. State


Claim No. 49592


Court of Claims of New York


63 Misc. 2d 455; 312 N.Y.S.2d 360; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1531



June 16, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] As we do not have jurisdiction of the subject matter of the claim, the State's motion to dismiss the claim is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State sought an order dismissing the claim of plaintiff owners on the grounds that the court lacked jurisdiction of the subject matter of the claim and, further, that the claim failed to state a cause of action. The owners' claim was predicated on the appropriation under eminent domain proceedings, pursuant to 1966 N.Y. Law ch. 691, of a building that formerly housed an opera but was sold for construction of an office building.


OVERVIEW: After the association vacated the building and prior to turning it over to the new owner, 1966 N.Y. Laws 691 was enacted which sought to preserve the old building and provided $ 200,000 as security for its condemnation and appropriation for use as an auditorium for operas, musical, and cultural events. Owing to judicial decisions, including appellate affirmation, that the statute constituted a taking of the owners' property, that the $ 200,000 was insufficient to cover the damage certain to be suffered by them, and that by limiting recovery to that amount the Legislature illegally invaded the judicial province, the property was returned to the owners. However, the court lacked jurisdiction to consider their claim for damages resulting from the temporary appropriation of the property, which included legal fees and litigation disbursements, increased construction and wrecking costs, and loss of profits, because such claims sounded in tort and not in appropriation. As tort claims, therefore, they were denied because there were no state officials or agencies involved in any respect in the operation of the statute and the state had not waived its sovereign immunity from liability.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's motion to dismiss the building owners' claim.


HEADNOTES

State -- liability for legislative enactment -- State is not liable for damages resulting from unconstitutional legislative enactment.

A claim by the lessee of the fee of the premises formerly housing the Metropolitan Opera to recover damages resulting from the enactment of a statute, later held to be an unconstitutional condemnation statute which failed to provide just compensation, fails to state a cause of action. The damage is damnum absque injuria. The sole relevant act by State officers was the enactment of a statute. The State has not waived its sovereign immunity from liability therefor. The Court of Claims has no jurisdiction of the subject matter of the claim and it is dismissed.

 

1840 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Heram Holding Corp. v. Albany


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, Albany County


63 Misc. 2d 152; 311 N.Y.S.2d 198; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1550



June 9, 1970 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the owner of 30 acres of vacant land adjacent to a heavy industrial area, challenged zoning ordinances of defendant, the City of Albany, which rezoned the owner's property from a heavy industrial zone to a single-family residence zone. The owner sought to have the ordinances declared void and further sought injunctive and incidental relief.


OVERVIEW: The City, by ordinance, rezoned the owner's vacant property to "A" residential, and, two years later, the City adopted a new comprehensive zoning ordinance, re-designating the property as "R-1" or single-family residential. The owner contended that the ordinances were confiscatory, they violated the comprehensive plan, they were arbitrary, and they violated the purposes of N.Y. Gen. City Law § 20(24), (25). The restrictions sufficiently invaded the owner's rights to afford declaratory relief. The court found the ordinances unreasonable where a professional planner stated that the property was suitable for heavy industrial and not for residential purposes. The planners for the City also reached the same conclusion. The court further found that the rezoning was of limited benefit to the community as a whole and was not in the best interests of the health, safety, or welfare of the community. Additionally, the great disparity in value and the economic impact on the owner from the rezoning resulted in severe financial loss. The owner not only overcame the presumption of constitutionality of the rezoning ordinances but also demonstrated their unconstitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court granted the owner's requested relief as it applied to the owner's property.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- plaintiff was not required to exhaust administrative remedies before commencing action to declare zoning ordinances which changed zone of his property from heavy industrial to residential void -- property was suitable for heavy industrial use and was placed in residential zone not in accordance with well considered plan; area is surrounded by trucking firms and highways are traversed by heavy trucks; ordinances as applied to plaintiff's property are void.

1. With respect to plaintiff's land placed in a heavy industrial zone when a zoning ordinance was adopted by defendant city in 1924 in which it remained until 1966, when it was rezoned to "A" residential, plaintiff is not required to exhaust administrative remedies first by application for a variance before commencing this action to declare the zoning ordinance of 1966 and a new comprehensive ordinance of 1968 void.

2. Plaintiff's professional planner and that of defendant city determined that plaintiff's land was suitable for heavy industrial use and not for residential purposes. The ordinances of 1966 and 1968 as they affect plaintiff's property were not in accordance with a comprehensive [***2] or well-considered plan as required by subdivision 25 of section 20 of the General City Law. The zoning does not benefit the community as a whole and is not in the best interests of the health, safety or welfare of the community. For residential purposes there is great disparity in the value of the land and the zoning for residences has resulted in a severe financial loss to plaintiff. The land is in an industrial area whose highways are traversed by high percentages of large tractor-trailers. There are numerous trucking concerns in the area. Heavy industrial areas should be insulated from residential areas. The ordinances as applied to plaintiff's property are therefore void.

 

1841 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Holtzman v. Power


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


62 Misc. 2d 1020; 313 N.Y.S.2d 904; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1558



June 5, 1970 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidates sought a declaratory judgment regarding the unconstitutionality of an amendment to N.Y. Elec. Law § 242-a and directing respondent Board of Elections (board) to determine ballot positions by lot. The candidates asserted that the legislation violated N.Y. Const. art. III, § 17, and denied nonincumbent candidates equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted an amendment which provided that incumbent candidates would be placed in the first ballot position for the current primary election in the city. The candidates filed suit alleging that the legislation violated N.Y. Const. art. III, § 17, and denied nonincumbent candidates equal protection. An appellate court ordered on remand that the candidates add the incumbent candidates as parties and referred to a special referee the issue of whether a candidate had some advantage by being named first on an election ballot. The referee found that there was such an advantage. The court confirmed the findings of the referee, holding that aside from the factual determination, such a belief appeared to be so widespread and so universally accepted as to make it almost a matter of public knowledge. The court held that there was no rational basis for affording such favoritism to a candidate merely on the basis of his having been successful at a prior election, and therefore, that the legislation was violative of basic constitutional principles. The board was directed to determine ballot positions by lot.


OUTCOME: The court declared the legislative amendment constitutionally invalid and directed the board to determine ballot positions by lot.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Elections -- primary elections -- incumbent cannot constitutionally be favored by statute directing that his name appear first on primary election ballot.

A provision that, in primary elections in 1970 in the City of New York, the name of the incumbent shall appear first on the ballot or the voting machine ( Election Law, § 242-a, subd. 7, as amd. by L. 1970, ch. 196), favors the incumbent and hence is unconstitutional. The Board of Elections is directed to determine all ballot positions by lot, as has heretofore been the practice.

 

1842 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Hospital Television Systems, Inc. v. New York State Tax Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


63 Misc. 2d 705; 311 N.Y.S.2d 568; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1565



June 3, 1970 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer brought a proceeding against respondent New York State Tax Commission pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, seeking a direction that coin receipts from coin-operated television sets that it owned and that were installed in hospitals were not subject to tax under N.Y. Tax Law art. 28. The Commission filed a motion to dismiss the petition on the ground that the petition was time barred.


OVERVIEW: The Commission urged dismissal on the grounds that the taxpayer had failed to exhaust his administrative remedy by applying for a hearing and that the time to apply for such a hearing had expired. The court disagreed. N.Y. Tax Law § 1138 provided that notice of determination of tax liability was to be given to the person liable for payment of the tax and that such determination would irrevocably fix the tax unless the person against whom it was assessed, within 90 days after giving of notice of such determination, applied to the Commission for a hearing. The section then provided that after such hearing, the Commission would give notice of its determination to the taxpayer. Section 1138 also provided that the determination could be reviewed if application was made within four months of the determination. The court found no mandate for an application for a hearing by an allegedly aggrieved taxpayer, and it found no language directing that a condition precedent to the institution of a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 was an application for a hearing. The taxpayer's petition was brought within four months of the determination and was not time barred.


OUTCOME: The court denied the Commission's motion to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Taxation -- sales tax -- petitioner may bring article 78 CPLR proceeding to review determination of respondent tax commission that certain receipts from coin-operated television sets, owned by petitioner and made available to in-hospital patients, are subject to New York State sales tax, even though petitioner had not first applied for administrative hearing to review such determination; article 78 proceeding is timely -- article 78 proceeding cannot be converted into action for declaratory judgment and serve as basis for cross-motion for summary judgment; petitioner's cross-motion for summary judgment is denied.

1. Petitioner may bring an article 78 CPLR proceeding to review a determination of respondent New York State Tax Commission that certain receipts from coin-operated television sets, owned by petitioner and made available to in-hospital patients, are subject to the New York State sales tax (Tax Law, § 1105), even though petitioner had not first applied for an administrative hearing to review such determination. Section 1138 of the Tax Law in providing that a determination by the Tax Commission "shall finally and irrevocably fix the tax unless the person against whom [***2] it is assessed * * * shall apply to the tax commission for a hearing" does not require that an aggrieved taxpayer must first apply for a hearing. To the contrary, section 1138 provides that "The determination of the tax commission shall be reviewable for error, illegality or unconstitutionality or any other reason whatsoever". Since petitioner instituted the article 78 proceeding within four months of the determination sought to be reviewed, it is timely. Respondent's motion to dismiss the article 78 proceeding is denied and it is directed to serve an answer.

2. Since the article 78 proceeding was timely filed it cannot be converted into an action for a declaratory judgment ( CPLR 103, subd. [c]) and serve as a basis for a cross-motion for summary judgment. Petitioner's cross-motion for summary judgment is denied.

 

1843 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Vintage Soc. Wholesalers Corp. v. State Liquor Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


63 Misc. 2d 287; 311 N.Y.S.2d 735; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1568



June 2, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] It is the court's finding that the subject statute is constitutional. Therefore the determination of the State Liquor Authority canceling the petitioner's license was not arbitrary, capricious, or contrary to law and, accordingly, the petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner wholesale wine licensee sought review of the determination by respondent New York Liquor Authority canceling the licensee's wine license because, the licensee alleged, the Authority's decision was arbitrary, capricious, and contrary to law. The licensee alleged that N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law § 104(9) was unconstitutional as it violated a licensee's equal protection rights by requiring only male employee to be fingerprinted.


OVERVIEW: The licensee was issued a license to conduct a wholesale wine business by the New York Liquor Authority. After the licensee's only employee, its sole principal and president, refused to submit his fingerprints as required by N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law § 104(9), the New York Liquor Authority cancelled the licensee's license. The law also required a photograph and a questionnaire from each male employee employed by a licensee. The court dismissed the licensee's petition and held that the statute was constitutional and not violative of the licensee's or other licensees' equal protection rights. The court found that the law was passed to prevent the acts of individuals who, during the prohibition era, had engaged in the "strong arm" solicitation of business in the liquor industry after passage of the Eighteenth Amendment. The court found that while it was possible that women might utilize physical force in attempting to solicit business, it was highly improbable. Indeed, the court ruled, although the law was discriminatory, because it applied only to men, it was not arbitrary, capricious, or contrary to state law.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition for review by the wholesale wine licensee and found that the New York statute requiring only male liquor employees to be fingerprinted was not violative of the licensee's equal protection rights.


HEADNOTES

Intoxicating liquors -- fingerprinting of male employees of licensee -- in proceeding to annul cancellation of wholesale wine license because petitioner's sole employee refused to submit fingerprints, petitioner may challenge constitutionality of law requiring male employees to submit fingerprints, regardless of form of proceeding -- while Alcoholic Beverage Control Law ( § 104, subd. 9) discriminates by applying to males only, statute is not arbitrary -- determination is confirmed.

1. Since petitioner's wholesale wine license was canceled because its male president who was its sole employee refused to submit his fingerprints as required by subdivision 9 of section 104 of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law, a proceeding under article 78 CPLR is proper to set aside such administrative action taken pursuant to what petitioner claims is an invalid, unconstitutional law. Moreover, regardless of the procedural device used,  [***2] the court would not dismiss the proceeding but deem it as one for a declaratory judgment of petitioner's rights under the alleged unconstitutional statute.

2. While the legislation is discriminatory in that it applies only to members of the male sex, it is not arbitrary. There was and is a reasonable basis for the Legislature's distinction between male and female sex in order to prevent the recurrence of evils in the liquor industry.

3. The determination is confirmed.

 

1844 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kriesel


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Onondaga County


63 Misc. 2d 72; 311 N.Y.S.2d 162; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1575



May 28, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] As so modified, the judgment of conviction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of a trial court (New York), which convicted defendant for violation of N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law § 65(1), for selling alcohol to a minor.


OVERVIEW: The record indicated that defendant was convicted for violation § 65(1) because she sold an alcoholic beverage to a 17-year-old after relying on the statement of an accompanying adult that the minor was over 18. Under § 65(1), it was a crime to sell alcohol to any minor, actually or apparently, under the age of 18. On appeal, defendant claimed that the statute was unconstitutional on the ground that the phrase "actually or apparently under the age of 18" was vague and did not clearly define the prohibited acts. In affirming the conviction, the court held that § 65(1) was clear and specific. The statute forbade the sale to any minor actually under the age of 18, and by adding the word "apparently," it clearly meant that the seller had the right to refuse to sell an alcoholic beverage to one who appeared to be less than 18 but was actually over 18. Section 65(1) was constitutional and a valid exercise of the State's police power. The court found sufficient evidence to warrant defendant's conviction beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court reduced the fine imposed on defendant and affirmed the trial court's judgment as modified.


HEADNOTES

Intoxicating liquors -- sale of alcoholic beverage to minor -- subdivision 1 of section 65 of Alcoholic Beverage Control Law is constitutional and valid exercise of State's police power -- evidence warrants conviction of defendant for sale of alcoholic beverage to 17-year-old -- fine is reduced to $ 100; judgment of conviction is affirmed.

1. Subdivision 1 of section 65 of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law which prohibits the sale of alcoholic beverages to any minor, actually or apparently under the age of 18 years, is constitutional and a valid exercise of the State's police power.

2. There is sufficient evidence to warrant the conviction of defendant beyond a reasonable doubt for the sale of an alcoholic beverage to a 17-year-old in reliance upon the statement of an accompanying adult that the minor was over 18 years old. Such a sale is an act malum prohibitum and is not to be excused by ignorance, mistake of fact or honorable intention.

3. The fine of $ 300 imposed on defendant is unreasonably excessive and is reduced to $ 100. Judgment of conviction is affirmed.

 

1845 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Holtzman v. Power


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


64 Misc. 2d 221; 314 N.Y.S.2d 777; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1606



May 20, 1970 



DISPOSITION: The Attorney-General's cross motion is granted and the petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner potential candidate brought a declaratory judgment proceeding seeking to declare null and void a recently enacted amendment to N.Y. Elec. Law § 242-a(7), which required the names of incumbent candidates to be listed first on the 1970 primary New York City ballot, and to enjoin respondent, Board of Elections of the City of New York, from implementing the amendment. The attorney general of the State of New York filed a cross-motion.


OVERVIEW: Instead of bringing an action challenging the amendment to § 242-a(7), the potential candidate brought a proceeding by order to show cause. The relief sought was a declaratory judgment declaring null and void the amendment and enjoining the Board from implementing it. The court dismissed the potential candidate's petition, holding that it lacked jurisdiction over the subject matter because the potential candidate had not served a summons or a complaint. Further, the potential candidate lacked standing to bring the proceeding because she could become a N.Y. Elec. Law § 330(7) "candidate aggrieved" only after she filed her designating petition. Moreover, there was no jurisdiction over the opposing candidates, who were indispensable parties, because they had not been served with process. Finally, on the merits, the court could not say that giving an incumbent first place on the ballot was not founded upon a reasonable distinction or difference in policy. Thus, the questioned advantage was neither invidious nor palpably arbitrary, and the potential candidate was not denied her rights to equal protection within the meaning of the United States or New York Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court granted the attorney general's cross motion and dismissed the potential candidate's petition.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- primary election -- proceeding under Election Law ( § 330) dismissed, on grounds that petitioner was not "candidate", and that opposing candidates were not made parties, and that Election Law ( § 330) does not authorize summary determination of constitutionality of election statute -- however, in order to avoid further proceedings if appellate courts hold that jurisdiction exists, Special Term renders opinion that subdivision 7 of section 242-a of Election Law, giving incumbent candidates first place on 1970 primary election ballots in New York City, is constitutional.

1. When petitioner commenced this proceeding under the Election Law ( § 330) for a judgment declaring that subdivision 7 of section 242-a of the Election Law, which provides that the names of incumbent candidates shall be listed first on the ballots in the 1970 primary elections in New York City, is unconstitutional and enjoining the Board of Elections from thus favoring [***2] the incumbent candidates, petitioner and the other persons enumerated by her in her petition were still collecting signatures on their unfiled designating petitions. Accordingly, none of them was at that time a "candidate aggrieved" (Election Law, § 330). Nor were the opposing incumbent candidates made parties. Moreover, the power of the Supreme Court to determine summarily any question of law or fact as to the "form and contents of official ballots" (Election Law, § 330) does not include a summary power to declare a statute unconstitutional. On these grounds, Special Term dismisses this petition and proceeding.

2. However, in order to avoid further proceedings in the event that the appellate courts find jurisdiction and require further proceedings, Special Term renders a decision on the merits. Special Term is of the opinion that subdivision 7 of section 242-a of the Election Law, even if it favors incumbents, is not palpably arbitrary and does not deny the equal protection of the laws within the meaning of the State and Federal Constitutions, but rather is valid and constitutional.

Meyers v. New York State Div. of Housing & Community Renewal


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


63 Misc. 2d 181; 311 N.Y.S.2d 377; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1605



May 20, 1970 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenants brought an action for declaratory judgment against defendants, a village and the state housing division, attacking the rent decontrol provisions of the Emergency Housing Rent Control Law, 1946 N.Y. Laws 274, § 12(2), and the decontrol of their village. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The tenants attacked the constitutionality of the local option decontrol provision of § 12(2), asked for invalidation of the resolution adopted by the village requesting the division to decontrol all housing accommodations within the village, and sought an injunction preventing the division from terminating rent control in the village. The court found that the legislature properly had authority under N.Y. Const. art. IX, § 2(b)(3) to delegate rent decontrol functions to local governments. The court held that § 12(2) was constitutional because the law, read as a whole, contained sufficient standards by which a local village could decontrol rent. The provision allowed rent decontrol where warranted, which meant when the housing crisis addressed by the rent control laws had disappeared. Therefore, the court denied the tenants' motion for summary judgment. The court also denied defendants' summary judgment motion because a factual dispute remained concerning the propriety of the village's decision to decontrol rent.


OUTCOME: The court denied both motions for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Landlord and tenant -- rent regulation -- decontrol by local resolution -- resolution by village board, requesting State Division of Housing etc., to decontrol all housing accommodations in village (Emergency Housing Rent Control Law, § 12, subd. 2), is presumed to have been constitutionally based on findings required by subdivision 1 of said section 12; trial is required.

A resolution which the Board of Trustees of a village adopted after a public hearing, requesting the New York State Division of Housing and Community Renewal to decontrol all housing accommodations in the village, is presumed to have been validly made "upon a finding that decontrol in such * * * village is warranted" by the fact that "the percentage of vacancies" in the village is now "five percentum or more" or by the facts that, now, in the village, "the availability of adequate rental housing accommodations and other relevant factors are such as to make rent control unnecessary for the purpose of eliminating * * * abnormal increases in rents" (Emergency Housing Rent Control Law [L. 1946, ch. 274, as amd.], § 12, subds. 1, 2; also, § 1, "Declaration and findings"). The statute validly delegates to [***2] local governments (N. Y. Const., art. IX, § 2, par. [b], subpar. [3]) the power to make such findings for rent decontrol. However, on the papers before this court, summary judgment cannot be granted either for or against the validity of this resolution. A trial is necessary.

 

1847 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Leshaw


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


District Court of New York, First District, Suffolk County


63 Misc. 2d 364; 316 N.Y.S.2d 704; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1619



May 15, 1970 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with selling prohibited items on Memorial Day and Independence Day in violation of Town of Islip, N.Y., Ordinance art. 409, § 2. Defendants contended that § 2 was unconstitutional. The matter came before the court for determination upon an agreed statement of facts.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with violating § 2, which prohibited all business and commercial activities on Memorial Day and Independence Day except for the sale of food, drugs, certain vehicular equipment, flowers, souvenirs, and bait. Defendants contended that § 2 was unconstitutional. The court observed that legislative enactments carried a strong presumption of constitutionality. The court further observed that § 2 was very similar to N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 9, a Sabbath Day ordinance, and that Sabbath Day ordinances which prohibited the carrying out of some business but allowed others to be conducted on the Sabbath were constitutional and did not violate one's right to equal protection of the law. N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 86 was the source of a municipality's right to pass ordinances concerning Memorial Day and Independence Day. Section 86 could only be given its intended effect by permitting the prohibition of certain types of business on those holidays. To interpret § 86 more rigorously would make the words "regulate the nature of business" meaningless and the words "and the hours within which various types of commercial and business activities may be conducted" redundant.


OUTCOME: The court found defendants guilty as charged.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- regulation of business on Memorial Day and Independence Day -- ordinance of town prohibiting business and commercial activity on Memorial Day and Independence Day except for stated exceptions is valid under statute providing for "regulation" of business.

Under section 86 of the General Municipal Law, which empowers a town to adopt ordinances "regulating" business activities on Memorial Day and Independence Day, an ordinance of a town "prohibiting" all business and commercial activities on those days except for stated exceptions, is constitutional. Accordingly, defendants are found guilty of selling prohibited items in violation of the ordinance.

 

1848 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Ofenloch v. Gaynor


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


66 Misc. 2d 185; 320 N.Y.S.2d 362; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1624



May 14, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the court orders that the second cause of action herein be deemed an action for declaratory judgment, and that the motions to dismiss be and the same are hereby denied as to the second cause of action and granted as to the first cause of action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff resident taxpayers filed an action seeking to permanently enjoin the issuance of building permits for certain improvements provided for under an agreement between defendant board of cooperative educational services (BOCES) and defendants, a realtor and a construction corporation. Defendants moved to dismiss the complaint pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3211.


OVERVIEW: BOCES entered into an agreement under which defendants were to construct three buildings for use by BOCES. BOCES would then lease the premises. At the end of lease, BOCES had the option to purchase the property and buildings, subject to a referendum of the voters, as prescribed by N.Y. Educ. Law § 1958. The taxpayers filed an action seeking to enjoin the issuance of building permits and challenging the validity of the agreement. The court dismissed the first cause of action, as to the permanent injunction, because the facilities to be operated by BOCES constituted a school, and a town could not prevent the location of a school within its boarders. Further, the taxpayer's challenge to the agreement's validity could not be pursued in the N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 51 form under which it was commenced. However, the court was impelled to exercise its discretion as liberally as possible to preserve the taxpayers' standing. The denial to the taxpayers of their right to pass judgment via a public referendum, which would be required if this was in fact a purchase and not a lease, was a sufficient threatened injury to warrant maintenance of this action as one for a declaratory judgment.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the first cause of action that sought to enjoin the issuance of building permits. The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss as to the second cause of action, which challenged the validity of the agreement.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- Boards of Cooperative Educational Services -- cause of action against town to restrain issuance of building permits for construction of buildings to be used by BOCES is insufficient -- cause of action challenging validity of agreement made between BOCES and realty company to test whether lease is not bona fide but device to obviate referendum of voters is sufficient -- action not maintainable as taxpayer's action but as one for declaratory judgment and plaintiffs have standing to maintain action.

1. A cause of action by resident taxpayers and voters of a town for an injunction against the town to restrain the issuance of building permits for the construction of buildings to be used by the county's Board of Cooperative Educational Services (BOCES) is insufficient. The court is bound by the holding in Matter of Board of Coop. Educ. Serv. of Nassau County v. Gaynor (60 Misc 2d 316, affd. 33 A D 2d [***2] 701, mot. for lv. to app. den. 26 N Y 2d 612) which determined that the facilities to be operated, by BOCES constituted a school within the town's zoning ordinance, and that the town could not prevent the location of a school within its borders.

2. A second cause of action challenges the validity of an agreement made between BOCES and defendant realty company under which the realty company agreed to construct three buildings for use by BOCES at a net annual rental for five years, with an option to renew for an additional five years, and at the end of 10 years, to purchase the property subject to a referendum of the voters. Section 1958 of the Education Law permits BOCES to rent buildings for not to exceed five years and to purchase them only when authorized by the voters. Whether or not plaintiffs can establish at a trial by competent testimony that the value of the land and the cost of construction have in fact been amortized over the term of the lease in the form of rental, and that the lease agreement is not a bona fide rental arrangement but rather a device to obviate a referendum for the expenditure of more than $ 2,000,000 cannot be decided on the papers or on this motion.  [***3] Certainly the economics of the transaction and the discussions during the negotiations would bear examination to determine the intention of the parties as to whether this was a bona fide lease or a constructive sale. A cause of action is stated.

3. The action is brought as a taxpayer's action under section 51 of the General Municipal Law. BOCES is not a municipal corporation and this action cannot be prosecuted in that form. It may however be maintained as an action for declaratory judgment. Plaintiffs as taxpayers and residents have standing to challenge the action of defendant BOCES and the action is appropriate to determine the issues raised by plaintiffs and to test the validity of the challenged lease agreement. The denial to the taxpayers of their right to pass judgment via a public referendum (which would be required if this is in fact a purchase of land and improvements and not a lease) is a sufficient threatened injury to a personal right to warrant maintenance of this action as one for a declaratory judgment.

 

1849 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Van Vort v. Van Vort


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


62 Misc. 2d 981; 310 N.Y.S.2d 641; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1634



May 12, 1970 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband brought an action for divorce on the ground that a decree of separation was made and entered previously in favor of defendant wife, and he alleged compliance with N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 170(5).


OVERVIEW: A separation decree was entered approximately eight years previously in favor of the wife. It provided for visitation for the husband with the couple's children and support payments by the husband. The husband later commenced an action for divorce based upon substantial compliance with the decree. The wife contended that there had been no substantial compliance and that the husband had not come to the court with "clean hands" because he had obtained a unilateral Mexican divorce and had remarried. In awarding the husband a divorce based upon the separation decree, the court held that N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 170(6) was unconcerned with the conduct of the parties. It further held that the husband's failure to visit the children according to the schedule and the fact that he had at one time fallen into arrears with support payments did not prevent the court from finding that he had substantially complied with the separation decree.


OUTCOME: The court awarded a divorce to the husband.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Husband and wife -- divorce -- husband is granted divorce on basis of 1962 decree of separation -- it is no defense that plaintiff obtained Mexican divorce and remarried -- failure of plaintiff to avail himself of rights of visitation does not show failure to comply with separation decree -- plaintiff's having fallen into arrears four years previously and paid lump sum in settlement also does not constitute failure to substantially comply with decree.

1. Plaintiff husband is granted a divorce pursuant to subdivision (5) of section 170 of the Domestic Relations Law on the ground that a decree of separation was granted in favor of defendant wife on April 4, 1962.

2. That plaintiff comes into court without "clean hands" in that he obtained a unilateral Mexican divorce decree subsequent to separation and remarried is not a defense. Under subdivision (5) the misconduct of plaintiff is not a basis for denying a divorce.

3. The failure of plaintiff to avail himself of certain rights of visitation does not show a failure to comply substantially with the decree of separation, nor does the fact that the children might have been returned late on occasion establish failure to comply [***2] substantially.

4. Plaintiff's having fallen into arrears of support payments in 1965 and 1966, and paid, some four years previously, $ 2,800 in settlement of approximately $ 3,600 to $ 4,000 in arrears does not show failure to comply. There is no claim that there are additional arrears or that plaintiff is not now up to date. A defense that plaintiff failed substantially to comply with the decree is dismissed.

 

1850 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Board of Education v. Associated Teachers of Huntington, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


62 Misc. 2d 906; 310 N.Y.S.2d 929; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1657; 74 L.R.R.M. 2979



May 4, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Summary judgment is granted to the plaintiff to the extent of declaring illegal (1) the provisions of section A of article XI (in both agreements) and (2) those separate provisions of section C of article XVIII, above indicated to be illegal.

Summary judgment is granted to the defendant to the extent of declaring legal (1) the provisions of sections E and F of article VIII, (2) the provisions of article XXI, and (3) those separate provisions of section C of article XVIII, above indicated to be legal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff board of education (board) sought a judgment declaring illegal certain provisions of two collective bargaining agreements with defendant teachers association (association) resulting from negotiations pursuant to the Public Employees' Fair Employment Act (Taylor Law), N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law, art. 14. The board also sought to enjoin the association from grieving or arbitrating any matters arising out of the contested provisions.


OVERVIEW: The court treated the board's request and the association's response as cross motions for summary judgment. The court first found that the Taylor Law did not grant public employers the right to bind themselves to terms and conditions of employment not otherwise authorized by law. The court found that the board had authority under the Education Law to reimburse teachers for eyeglasses, dentures, and other devices lost as a result of employment not covered under the Workmen's Compensation Law, and repair or replacement of clothing or personal effects. The court found no authority for provisions providing payment for optional graduate courses. The court found the board authorized to agree to increase a teacher's pay in the final year of service under N.Y. Educ. Law § 3102(3). The court held that the board could not agree to subject matters pertaining to discipline or termination of tenured teachers to a grievance procedure under N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law art. 16, but could do so for non-disciplinary matters relating to the supervision of such teachers.


OUTCOME: The court partially granted summary judgment to each party with respect to specific provisions of the collective bargaining agreement between the association and the board, finding that the board's power bind itself was limited to its existing statutory authority.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- Public Employees' Fair Employment Act -- in action by school board to declare provisions of agreement with teachers' association invalid, court declares invalidity of provision that dismissal or other discipline of tenure teachers must be subject to grievance procedure; however, nondisciplinary evaluations and transfers may validly be agreed to be subject to grievance procedure -- provision for reimbursing teachers for nonrequired courses of study is invalid -- provision for increase of salary for last year prior to retirement is valid -- provisions for reimbursing teachers for eyeglasses, dentures, clothes, etc., which are damaged or destroyed in course of employment,  [***2] are valid.

1. In this action by a school board, the following provisions in the board's agreement with a teachers' association are found to contravene other statutes (cf. Civil Service Law, § 204-a, subd. 1; N. Y. Const., art. XIII, § 14) and therefore are declared to be invalid: (a) a provision for reimbursing teachers for part of their payments for courses of study which are approved in advance by the Principal and by the Superintendent -- but which courses are not required (Education Law, § 3101, subd. 3); and (b) a provision that dismissals or removals or suspensions or other disciplining of tenure teachers shall be subject to a grievance procedure between the board and the teachers' association (Education Law, §§ 3012, 3013); however, the court declares that a provision that the supervision of tenure teachers, including nondisciplinary transfers and evaluations of their performance, shall be subject to grievance procedure, is valid (General Municipal Law, art. 16, § 682, subd. 4; §§ 683, 684).

2. The court declares the following provisions of the agreement to be authorized by statutes and valid: (a) a provision for an increase of salary for the year prior to a teacher's [***3] retirement (Education Law, § 501, subd. 11; § 3102, subd. 3; cf. N. Y. Const., art. VIII, § 1); and (b) provisions that the school board shall reimburse teachers or shall provide for their reimbursement, in situations in which the Workmen's Compensation Law does not provide for compensation, for eyeglasses, dentures, clothing, and other personal effects which are damaged or destroyed or lost without the teacher's negligence in the course of employment (Education Law, § 1604, subd. 27; § 1710; § 1804, subd. 1).

 

1851 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Schwab


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Erie County


62 Misc. 2d 786; 310 N.Y.S.2d 436; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1656



May 4, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The defendant's further motion to reimpanel the second trial jury for purposes of recording a verdict of not guilty under counts one and two of the "B" indictment is denied, the issues raised therein having been rendered moot by this decision.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to reimpanel the second trial jury for purposes of recording a verdict of not guilty under counts one and two of the "B" indictment.


OVERVIEW: Indictments against defendant were returned by the grand jury and he was arraigned thereon. The "A" indictment charged him with two counts of fraudulently presenting false claims for payment to the County Board of Supervisors, and two counts of grand larceny in connection with the payments made under those claims. The "B" indictment charged him with three counts of perjury for allegedly offering false testimony concerning his work that were made during examinations before trial in the county's civil action for breach of contract and on the occasion of his appearance before the grand jury during its subsequent investigations of these matters. The defendant so testified in front of the grand jury after he was made to sign a waiver of immunity from subsequent prosecution. He then filed a motion to reimpanel the jury for purposes of recording a not guilty verdict under the counts in the "B" indictment. The court denied his motion, by holding that, although his privilege against self-incrimination was fully preserved in light of the improper waiver, the privilege did not extend to perjury committed in the very process of making the disclosure that was assertedly compelled.


OUTCOME: The court denied the defendant's motion to reimpanel the second trial jury for purposes of recording a verdict of not guilty under counts one and two of the "B" indictment.


HEADNOTES

Witnesses -- waiver of immunity -- contractor was unconstitutionally compelled to incriminate himself before Grand Jury, because he had to sign waiver of immunity or be disqualified for five years from making any public contracts (General Municipal Law, § 103-b); therefore, his indictments for fraud and grand larceny, and for testifying perjuriously in county's prior civil action, are dismissed -- but he was properly indicted for giving same perjurious testimony to said Grand Jury -- third trial will not place him in double jeopardy -- prosecution's delay of almost six years in moving grand larceny indictment for trial requires dismissal of that indictment.

1. Defendant was a partner in a construction firm which was engaged in the performance of many contracts with the county and other municipalities. In a suit by the county for damages for breach of one such contract, he was examined before trial. Thereafter, he was called before [***2] the Grand Jury to testify concerning his allegedly fraudulent performance of that contract and concerning his allegedly perjurious testimony on said pretrial examination. For the Grand Jury, he signed a waiver of his immunity from prosecution for grand larceny and perjury. Had he refused to sign such waiver, he and his firm would have been disqualified from any and all public contracts for up to five years (General Municipal Law, § 103-b). In view of such compulsion to testify, his constitutional privilege against self incrimination was violated by the Grand Jury, whether or not he asserted his privilege; and therefore, he automatically acquired immunity from prosecution for any substantive crimes which were the subject of his compelled testimony. Accordingly, his indictments by the Grand Jury for fraudulently presenting to the county false claims for payment, and for grand larceny in receiving such payment, and for his perjurious testimony in the civil action, are dismissed.

2. But his indictment for giving perjurious testimony to said Grand Jury is constitutional and triable, even though the testimony which he gave to the Grand Jury was much the same as the testimony which [***3] he had given to the county in the county's civil action.

3. Defendant's first trial resulted, after more than a month, in a mistrial. His second trial, which took almost three months, resulted in a "hung" jury and a declaration of mistrial. Nevertheless, a third trial will not unconstitutionally subject him to double jeopardy.

4. The prosecution's delay, for almost six years without good cause, in moving a grand larceny indictment for trial, requires the dismissal of that indictment (Code Crim. Pro., §§ 8, 668).

 

1852 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Darnet Realty Corp. v. Markley


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Civil Court of the City of New York, Trial Term


63 Misc. 2d 29; 310 N.Y.S.2d 904; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1670



April 28, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition is dismissed, without prejudice to renewal, upon a proper showing of compliance with the statute or ordinance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landlord brought an eviction action against respondent tenant.


OVERVIEW: The landlord offered the tenant a renewal lease, but the tenant failed to sign it by the date of expiration of the original lease. The landlord subsequently brought an eviction action against the tenant as a holdover. The court dismissed the action. The court stated that because the landlord failed to allege any of the enumerated grounds for eviction in the Rent Stabilization Law of 1969, he had not complied with the statutory requirements necessary to be granted an eviction. Under N.Y. Real Prop. Acts. Law § 711, the landlord was required to show compliance with the Rent Stabilization Law of 1969. Among the requirements of that legislation were that the landlord was a member of the association in good standing, otherwise he was relegated to the class of landlords owning controlled rent property. Because the landlord was not alleged to have complied with the statutory requirement, his ability to evict the tenant was limited to those grounds enumerated in the Rent Stabilization Law of 1969. That system was applicable even in a situation where the tenant had an opportunity to sign a proffered renewal lease but failed to do so.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the landlord's eviction action against the tenant as a holdover.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- rent regulation -- eviction of tenant -- during stay period so that review can be had of determination that Rent Stabilization Law of 1969 is unconstitutional, tenant who requested renewal of her expiring lease but who has not signed lease is protected -- petition for eviction of tenant is jurisdictionally defective for failure to plead facts bringing it within either of rent control statutes.

1. The Rent Stabilization Law of 1969 (Local Laws, 1969, No. 16 of City of New York) has been held unconstitutional in 8200 Realty Corp. v. Lindsay (34 A D 2d 79) but a stay was granted for 30 days to permit review by the Court of Appeals. During the stay period, the status of tenants is protected. Accordingly, tenant herein whose lease expired January 31, 1970 and although agreeing to a renewal under such law, has not signed the new lease, is entitled to such protection for the legislative scheme imposes control even if tenant does not sign the proffered lease either under the Rent Stabilization Law or the emergency rent control [***2] law.

2. Under all emergency statutes, the petition must allege that the premises are under the emergency rent control law or under the Rent Stabilization Law and that under either law compliance therewith has been made. Under the Rent Stabilization Law eviction can be had for violation of tenancy, nuisance, subjecting the owner to criminal penalty, illegal use or refusal of access and none of these is alleged in the petition. Under the Real Property Actions and Proceedings Law, while holdover is one of the grounds, that law must be read with the Rent Stabilization Law. This requires that the petition meet the jurisdictional requirements. The petition is jurisdictionally defective for failure to plead facts bringing the petition within either of the control statutes or pleading an exemption. It is dismissed without prejudice.

 

1853 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Garcia


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Allegany County


62 Misc. 2d 666; 309 N.Y.S.2d 721; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1706



April 15, 1970 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to suppress a certain package which defendant stated contained marijuana. Defendant had been indicted for two counts of criminal possession of dangerous drugs in the third degree and also in the sixth degree.


OVERVIEW: A confidential informant told police that a certain individual would be receiving a package with marijuana. The police informed the postal inspector who opened the package, took a sample, and gave it to the police for testing. The sample was found to be marijuana. The postal inspector and the police then obtained a search warrant. The police arrested defendant when he picked up the package. Defendant told the postal clerk that he was the individual the package was addressed to. The postal inspector made the search of the package without a search warrant. The issue before the court was whether the opening of the package by the postal inspector constituted an illegal and/or unconstitutional violation of defendant's rights. The court held that: (1) defendant was a person having a possessory interest in the parcel, and, therefore, he was a person properly claiming to be aggrieved, with standing to bring the motion under N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 813-c; and (2) where the search in its inception was legal and the material contained in the parcel was unlawful, there were no violations of statutes, rules, and regulations or the Fourth Amendment as would require suppression of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to suppress.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- unlawful search and seizure -- mailed package, sent by other than first class mail, was inspected and found to contain drugs; defendant called at post office, stated he was addressee, received package and was indicted for possessing drugs; motion to suppress denied -- having mailed package under law and rules which permit inspection, defendant cannot complain of inspection which was with his consent.

1. A package, sent by other than first class mail, was, upon a tip from an informant, opened and found to contain drugs. The postal inspector and a State policeman obtained a search warrant. When defendant came to the post office and asked for the package in the name of the addressee, and stated that he was the person named, defendant was given the package and ultimately indicted for possessing dangerous drugs. Defendant's motion to suppress the package is denied.

2. Having deposited a parcel in the mail pursuant to the law, rules and regulations which permit its inspection at any time, neither the sender nor, to the extent of his interest therein, defendant, as parcel claimant, can complain of its lawful inspection. Probable cause is not in issue on a finding that [***2] there has been a permissive or consent inspection.

 

1854 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Heslop


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Tompkins County


62 Misc. 2d 620; 309 N.Y.S.2d 474; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1714



April 13, 1970 



DISPOSITION: The conviction of the defendant is reversed, the fine ordered remitted and the traffic information dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from a Court of Special Sessions (New York), in which defendant was convicted of violating N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1227.


OVERVIEW: A state police officer cited defendant, a mail carrier, for violating N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1227, which required that a person operating a privately-owned vehicle in delivering the mail have a sign affixed to the roof of the vehicle reading, "U.S. MAIL." Defendant pled not guilty, but he was convicted and sentenced to pay a conditional fine. Defendant appealed, and the court reversed, holding that § 1227 was too vague and uncertain to be legally enforceable and thus was unconstitutional. The court found that the language of § 1227 was indefinite as to the sign's visibility and provided no standard or guides for affixing a sign except that it had to be on the roof of the vehicle. The court found that the evidence was undisputed that defendant's vehicle bore a sign, which was painted on and across the roof of his vehicle, and that the officer cited defendant because such was only visible from above, and not from in front of or behind, the vehicle. The court concluded that read literally, the requirements of § 1227 could have been met by mounting a sign at any angle to the plane of the vehicle's roof, facing any direction, or even by affixing it flat on the roof, as defendant did.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, in which defendant was convicted of violating a traffic law, and ordered defendant's fine remitted and the traffic information against him dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- mail carrying vehicles -- section 1227 of Vehicle and Traffic Law providing that vehicles carrying mail must have sign on roof reading "U. S. Mail" is unconstitutional.

Section 1227 (now § 1229) of the Vehicle and Traffic Law provides that "Every person operating a privately-owned vehicle in delivering the United States Mail * * * shall affix to the roof of such vehicle a white sign containing the * * * statement: U. S. Mail". Such section is so vague as to be unconstitutional. It provides no standards or guides for affixing the sign except that it be on the roof. The purpose served by the sign is nowhere stated. The requirements of the statute could be met by mounting the sign at any angle to the plane of the roof facing in any direction or affixing it flat on the roof as defendant did. Defendant's conviction is reversed [***2] and the fine remitted.

 

1855 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Di Carlo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Erie County


62 Misc. 2d 638; 309 N.Y.S.2d 791; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1725



April 9, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The judgment appealed from herein must, therefore, be reversed, the informations reinstated and the matter remanded to Buffalo City Court for further proceedings in accordance with this decision.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People appealed from a judgment of the Buffalo City Court (New York), which dismissed informations charging defendants with possession of gambling records on the grounds that N.Y. Penal Law § 225.15(1) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The informations alleged each defendant's possession of written records of horse bets, tally sheets, racing programs, racing forms and ball-point pens, all of which were said to be articles commonly used in the operation of a bookmaking scheme or enterprise. The trial court dismissed the informations on the ground that N.Y. Penal Law § 225.15 was unconstitutional. On appeal the court reversed, holding that the change in the language of from the language of its predecessor was designed solely to facilitate prosecution of a crime which was previously defined, and there was no reason to believe that the legislature had any intention of extending § 225.15(1) to matters beyond those sought to be prohibited its predecessor; and (2) § 225.15(1) was constitutional because, when the statute was restricted in application to possession of such essential and uniquely criminal business records, the section represented an undeniably constitutional exercise of the police power of the State and § 225.25 did not place the burden of proving the fact that uniquely criminal business records were in fact neither used nor intended for use in a bookmaking scheme, upon defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment dismissing the informations charging defendants with possession of gambling records, reinstated the informations, and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- bookmaking -- Penal Law ( § 225.15, subd. 1) making person guilty of misdemeanor for possessing papers and articles in operation of bookmaking enterprise, when read in restricted manner, is constitutional.

Section 225.15 (subd. 1) of the Penal Law provides that a person is guilty of a class A misdemeanor when "with knowledge of the contents thereof, he possesses any writing, paper, instrument or article: 1. Of a kind commonly used in the operation or promotion of a bookmaking scheme or enterprise". Article 225 is concerned not with the bettor, but with the unlawful acceptance of bets from members of the public as a business. Section 225.15 need not be read as a prohibition against innocent possession of racing forms, pads, pencils and other innocuous articles used in bookmaking operations. Its object is the possession of bookmaking records, the records of business wagers, tally sheets and similar items essential and unique to the professional bookmaker's business.  [***2] Said section when so restricted constitutes a constitutional exercise of the police power. A judgment dismissing informations on the ground that the section is unconstitutional is reversed, the informations reinstated and the matter remanded.

 

1856 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ruffino


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Criminal Term, Queens County


62 Misc. 2d 653; 309 N.Y.S.2d 805; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1726



April 9, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Defendants' motion is denied except as above set forth.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a motion for a dismissal of an indictment charging them for the crimes of attempting to commit the crime of murder, conspiring to commit the crime of murder, and possession of a pistol as a felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that eavesdropping warrants were invalid and illegal, that the evidence presented to the grand jury was illegal, and that an order amending the warrants to include subsequent overheard conversations constituting evidence of crimes not named in the original warrants was improperly and unconstitutionally made. Defendants also sought inspection of the grand jury minutes and an order directing the production of the original eavesdropping orders and the papers upon which they were granted. The court denied the motion, except as to the request for copies of the original eavesdropping warrants. The court held that a legally intercepted telephone call was not rendered constitutionally defective because of the failure to obtain an amending order as promptly as possible, as such was a mere irregularity which did not affect the legality of the interception or the prosecutor's right to offer the conversation in evidence. The court found that defendants' substantive rights were not affected, as the wiretap was discontinued immediately upon the interception of the communication at issue. The court concluded that there was probable cause to justify the issuing of the warrants.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motion to dismiss the indictment, except as to that portion requesting copies of the original eavesdropping warrants for inspection by defendants, which portion was granted.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- wiretap -- ex parte orders authorized wiretapping for narcotics crimes; while thus listening, police heard plan to murder; police immediately discontinued wiretap (U. S. Const., 4th Amdt.), and arrested defendants, one of whom had loaded pistol in hand; on evidence which included this overheard conversation, Grand Jury properly indicted defendants for attempted murder; subsequently, Justice who had issued wiretap orders amended them so as to include conversations as to murders; immaterial whether such amended order was obtained promptly; motion to dismiss indictment is denied -- District Attorney shall produce court orders, so that defendants may compare them with copies which were served on defendants -- but, even if District Attorney consents to defendants' motion to inspect Grand Jury minutes, court denies such motion.

1. The provisions of the Code of Criminal Procedure (§ 813-a) governing ex parte orders for "interception" of "telephonic communications" were repealed and new provisions governing ex parte "eavesdropping warrants" were enacted (Code Crim Pro., §§ 814 to 825; L. 1968, ch. 546, eff. June [***2] 5, 1968), and these were repealed and newer provisions were enacted (§§ 814 to 825; L. 1969, ch. 1147, eff. June 25, 1969). On May 12, 1969, an eavesdropping warrant was properly issued to tap a certain telephone for information as to crimes dealing with narcotics (Code Crim. Pro., former § 816) and this warrant was properly extended on May 31 to June 19. On June 4, 1969 telephone conversations with the defendants as to a planned murder by shooting were thus intercepted by the police. As a result, on June 4 in the vicinity where the planned murder was to be committed, the police arrested the defendants, one of whom had a loaded pistol in his hand. The police immediately discontinued this wiretap. On June 16, on evidence which included the overheard conversations of June 4, the Grand Jury properly indicted the defendants for attempted murder and conspiracy to murder and felonious possession of a pistol. On September 18, 1969, the Justice who had issued the eavesdropping orders properly amended the orders so as to include crimes based on the conversations which had been overheard on June 4. Whether or not the amended order was obtained "as promptly as practicable" or "as soon [***3] as practicable" (Code Crim. Pro., former § 822, subd. 1; present § 825, subd. 4) is immaterial, since the police discontinued their wiretapping after they overheard the conversations about the planned murder (U. S. Const., 4th Amdt.). Therefore, defendants' motion to dismiss the indictment is denied.
