The court dismissed the writ and remanded the inmate to the custody of the warden, holding that the use of the special jury did not violate his rights to a fair trial, to due process, or to equal protection. The court noted that at no time prior to judgment did the inmate object to the composition of the grand or special juries with respect to the exclusion of individuals opposed to capital punishment.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the inmate's writ alleging that the trial court had violated his constitutional rights and remanded him to the custody of the warden.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- exclusion of jurors opposed to capital punishment -- trial and conviction of relator by blue ribbon jury from which jurors opposed to capital punishment were excluded did not violate his constitutional rights; no showing requiring hearing was made by relator to support claim that Judiciary Law ( § 597) was misapplied by County Clerk -- questioning of jurors as to newspaper article by court, prosecutor and relator's counsel, but outside presence of relator, did not violate his rights.

1. Relator was convicted of murder in the second degree after a jury trial. Relator claims that section 597 of the Judiciary Law as applied in New York County deprived him of his constitutional rights because it excluded jurors opposed to capital punishment and caused an unrepresentative jury and substantially increased the risk of conviction. Relator proposes to produce at a hearing the County Clerk, his records, and jurors from the 1964 New York County Special Jury panels from which his special jury was drawn. The testimony of such jurors as to their views in 1964 towards [***2] capital punishment carries no weight and the examination of the County Clerk's records is in the nature of a fishing expedition which should not be permitted. The argument that the Grand Jury and the special jury on his trial were prosecution prone has been rejected and the use of a special jury did not violate relator's rights to a fair trial, to due process or to equal protection of the laws. While relator now attacks the constitutionality of section 597, at no time prior to judgment did he object to the composition of grand or special juries, and never objected to the exclusion of jurors opposed to capital punishment. No showing has been made which requires a hearing to support the claim of a misapplication of section 597 by the County Clerk. Moreover, relator's constitutional rights were not violated by the application of this section, nor did it prevent the rendition of a fair verdict on the issue of his guilt nor increase his risk of conviction.

2. During the trial a newspaper article appeared in a newspaper which defendant's trial counsel brought to the court's attention. Relator's absence from the jury room while his counsel, the prosecutor and the Judge were questioning [***3] the jury about such newspaper article, did not affect any substantial right of relator and did not invalidate the subsequent judgment of conviction. Section 427 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, which provides that "After the jury have retired for deliberation" and request instructions, the instructions must be given in defendant's presence is inapplicable since the jury had not retired for deliberation. Section 356 of the code, which requires that at the trial of a felony defendant must be personally present, is also inapplicable. No witnesses were being questioned and no instructions were being given to the jury.

 

1880 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Woodhouse, Drake & Carey, Ltd. v. Anderson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


61 Misc. 2d 951; 307 N.Y.S.2d 113; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1979; 7 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 214



January 14, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, plaintiff's motion is granted and defendant's cross motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, claiming status as a holder in due course of a promissory note executed by defendant, sued defendant and moved for summary judgment. Defendant moved for leave to serve an amended answer.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought suit as a holder in due course of a note executed and delivered by defendant to cover a deficit in an account for which defendant was responsible and moved for summary judgment. Defendant moved for leave to amend his answer. The court denied defendant's motion because it was sought as a prejudicial tactic for avoiding or delaying summary judgment. The court then dispensed with each of defendant's assertions. Defendant was liable to a holder in due course even if, as he claimed, he were an accommodation indorser. Plaintiff was a holder in due course under the Uniform Commercial Code and therefore an unsupported claim for lack of consideration failed. The note was not usurious because it imposed interest at the maximum legal rate. The legislature in giving clearly defined powers to the banking board to set interest rates for a limited period of time had made a valid and limited delegation of power which was not unconstitutional. Accordingly, plaintiff's motion for summary judgment was granted.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's cross-motion for leave to serve an amended answer, granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgment, and awarded plaintiff the relief demanded in the complaint.


HEADNOTES

Bills, notes and checks -- promissory note -- interest -- accommodation maker -- raising of lawful maximum interest rate to 7 1/2% is constitutional (3 NYCRR 4.1) -- promissory note, payable at 8 1/2% or at maximum legal rate, is payable at latter rate and hence is not usurious -- accommodation maker or indorser is liable to holder in due course -- plaintiff is holder in due course even though it took note in payment of antecedent debt, and even though unqualified indorsement to plaintiff occurred only after prior transfer to plaintiff for value -- summary judgment for plaintiff -- defendant's cross motion to amend his answer is obvious tactic to delay summary judgment and hence is denied.

1. Section 5-501 of the General Obligations Law and section 14-a of the Banking Law and the Regulation of the Banking Board raising the lawful maximum interest rate to 7 1/2% (3 NYCRR 4.1) are valid and constitutional.

2. A promissory note, which states that interest is payable at 8 1/2% or at the maximum legal rate, is payable at the latter definitely ascertainable maximum rate and no more (Uniform Commercial [***2] Code, § 3-104, subd. [1], par. [b]; § 3-106) and hence is not usurious.

3. Defendant asserts that he executed the note without any consideration and only in order to cover a deficit in an account for which he was responsible to his employer. Even if this is true, defendant was an accommodation maker or indorser and, as such, liable to a holder in due course.

4. Plaintiff is a holder in due course, even though it took the note in payment of an antecedent debt, and even though the unqualified indorsement to plaintiff occurred only after a prior transfer to plaintiff for value, but before maturity (Uniform Commercial Code, §§ 3-201, 3-302, 3-303, 3-304).

5. Accordingly, plaintiff is granted summary judgment on the note, and defendant's cross motion for leave to amend his answer so as to plead usury, etc., as above set forth, is denied.

6. Although the sufficiency and merits of a proposed amended pleading are generally left to be determined at the trial or upon a proper motion, a motion to amend should be denied when it is made as an obvious tactic to avoid or delay summary judgment.

 

1881 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Glen v. Rockefeller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


61 Misc. 2d 942; 307 N.Y.S.2d 46; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1991



January 12, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the application is denied and the petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners moved for an injunction pendente lite seeking to enjoin and restrain respondents, governor and transit authority (New York), from collecting and enforcing a transit fare in excess of 20 cents pending the holding of a public hearing on any proposed increase in fare.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners sought to enjoin and restrain respondents, governor and transit authority, from collecting and enforcing a transit fare in excess of 20 cents, pending the holding of a public hearing on the subject of any proposed increase in such fare. The court first noted that the governor and the comptroller were not proper parties with the state and the governor having immunity from suit without evidence of a legislative waiver. The court also noted that the governor and the state had no jurisdiction over the fare increase and were not proper parties as well. The court also held that, while the fare increase hit the poor hardest, it was applied equally across the citizenry. The court found that petitioners had no standing to challenge fare increase and therefore the application for injunctive relief was denied and the petition dismissed.


OUTCOME: Application for an injunction pendente lite to enjoin the respondents, governor and transit authority, from collecting and enforcing a transit fare in excess of 20 cents, was denied and the petition dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Public authorities -- New York City Transit Authority -- fares may be raised by New York City Transit Authority without any public hearing.

An action by citizens to restrain the New York City Transit Authority from raising transit fares above their present level of 20 cents unless it first holds a public hearing thereon is dismissed. "Notwithstanding the provisions of any other law", the New York City Transit Authority has the power to adjust its rates of fare so as to maintain a self-sustaining operation (Public Authorities Law, § 1205, subd. 1). This power is legislative and hence it is not judicially reviewable. Although, in contrast, the Metropolitan Transportation Authority is required to hold a public hearing before raising rates on its own facilities or on those of a "subsidiary corporation" Public Authorities Law, § 1266, subd. 3), the New York City Transit Authority is not a "subsidiary" in this respect. Although the legislative purpose is to implement "a unified mass transportation policy" (Public Authorities Law, § 1264; L. 1967, ch. 717, § 60), and although the same persons comprise [***2] the boards of both authorities, it is not unusual for key officials to wear "two hats" and to function differently under each hat. Constitutional principles of due process of law and equal protection of the laws do not require a public hearing in such case.

 

1882 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Zeluck v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


62 Misc. 2d 274; 307 N.Y.S.2d 329; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2007; 73 L.R.R.M. 2265



January 6, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion to dismiss is therefore granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor, the Attorney-General of the State of New York, sought to dismiss the petition which sought to enjoin respondent education board from making payroll deductions against certain teachers pursuant to a determination by the board's school superintendent under N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 210 that they had engaged in a strike. The petitioner was the teachers' union.


OVERVIEW: The school superintendent determined that payroll deductions against the striking teachers were proper pursuant § 210. The union sought to enjoin the board from making the deductions. The attorney-general intervened to dismiss the union's petition. The court granted the attorney-general's motion to dismiss the union's petition for injunction. The court found that § 210 did not infringe upon the union members' right of free association and speech. The court held that the ability to strike was not essential to the right of association and it was subordinate to the right of the State to prohibit the activity. The court held that the fact that the prohibition was against all strikes by public employees without classification among various public employee groups did not affect the constitutionality since it was within the State's power to determine that all strikes by public employees were harmful without distinguishing between them as to degree. The court held that the determination of the legislature that the school board had the power to be both negotiator and ultimate arbiter of disputes arising out of negotiation was not unreasonable because dispute procedures existed.


OUTCOME: The court granted the attorney-general's motion to dismiss the union's petition for injunction against the board's deduction from striking teachers' pays.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- Taylor Law -- deduction of two days' pay from public employee for each day he was on strike (Civil Service Law, § 210) is valid and constitutional.

Section 210 (Taylor Law) of the Civil Service Law, prohibiting strikes by public employees, and authorizing a public employer to deduct two days' pay for each day that such an employee violates the prohibition, is valid and constitutional. The court will not enjoin a Board of Education from making such deductions from the salaries of those teachers who were determined, by the local Superintendent of Schools after due notice, to have been on strike. Such determination is reviewable by means of an article 78 proceeding. Such determination does not violate constitutional requirements of due process, equal protection, free speech or free association.

 

1883 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Posner v. Rockefeller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


62 Misc. 2d 28; 307 N.Y.S.2d 959; 1970 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2011



January 3, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, for the reasons stated herein, the petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, as members of the State assembly and taxpayers, commenced a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 seeking a judgment that would direct respondents, Governor and state officials, not to expend further money in accordance with State budget appropriation bills. Upon remand from the Special Term, Albany County (New York) following the denial of respondents' motion for change of venue, respondents filed a motion to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners sought a judgment that would prohibit respondents from expending additional money in accordance with the State budget appropriation bills. Petitioners contended that certain parts of the appropriation bills were unconstitutional when measured against the requirements of N.Y. Const. art. VII concerning the itemization of expenditures. The court determined that petitioners, as taxpayers, had no standing to attack the constitutionality of the bills because they were not personally aggrieved by the enactment. Petitioners did have standing to attack the constitutionality of the bills as members of the State assembly when they were unable to perform their duties under N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 4. However, petitioners' official standing to attack the constitutionality of the bills ended upon the enactment of the bills because their constitutional duties were terminated when the bills were enacted. The court concluded that petitioners had no standing at the time they initiated the proceeding and thereby granted respondents' motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court granted respondents' motion to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- State budget -- citizens and taxpayers lack standing to attack constitutionality of State budget submitted by Governor -- as Assemblymen, petitioners had duty to perform but, since budget bills became law prior to commencement of proceeding, their duty was ended and they lack standing to bring proceeding -- moreover, bills were submitted in January, 1969 and commencement of proceeding six months later was untimely.

1. Citizens and taxpayers have no standing to attack the constitutionality of budgets for State expenditures prepared by the Governor for submission to the Legislature since they do not allege that they are personally aggrieved by the budgets.

2. As Assemblymen petitioners claim that, because of the form in which the appropriation bills were submitted, they were unable to perform the duties enjoined upon them by section 4 of article VII of the State Constitution. Since this proceeding was not commenced until after enactment of these appropriation bills, and petitioners' constitutional duty was at an end, they no longer had standing in their official capacity to bring [***2] the proceeding.

3. Moreover, insofar as petitioners, as Assemblymen, challenge the form in which the appropriation bills were submitted by the Governor, the proceeding must be dismissed as untimely. The original bills were introduced on January 21, 1969 on which date they became final and binding. The proceeding not having been commenced until July 1, 1969, petitioners are barred from relief.

 

1884 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Board of Education v. Parsons


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Wayne County


61 Misc. 2d 838; 306 N.Y.S.2d 833; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 946



December 31, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the petition herein is dismissed and the motion for summary judgment on the merits in favor of the respondent is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, school district and taxpayers, sought review the 1970 assessment made by respondent assessor on the nuclear power plant under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 and N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 7. The assessor filed a cross-motion for an order pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3211, 3212 dismissing the petitions herein and for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The school district and the taxpayers alleged that the nuclear power plant was underassessed. They applied for review under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 and N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 7 claiming that such property was assessed at a lower percentage of true or full value than other properties in the town. The assessor filed a motion to dismiss. The court dismiss the petitions and held that there was no remedy in law that could be given in such proceeding because the tax rolls passed from the custody of the assessor and the court was, therefore, without power to order their correction. Thus, the petition under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 failed to state a cause of action. Further, the court held that the school district was not a taxpayer liable for the payment of taxes on real property and the taxpayers did not claim overvaluation seeking a decrease in their assessment. Thus, they had no standing as an aggrieved person under N.Y. Real Prop. Law § 7.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petitions filed by the school district and the taxpayers to review the tax assessments made by the assessor on the nuclear power plant.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- assessments -- proceedings to review alleged underassessment of another's property dismissed ( CPLR art. 78; Real Property Tax Law, art. 7).

Neither article 78 of the CPLR nor article 7 of the Real Property Tax Law is available to attack the alleged underassessment of another's property. Such proceedings are dismissed.

 

1885 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. East Island News Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


District Court of New York, First District, Suffolk County


61 Misc. 2d 923; 307 N.Y.S.2d 336; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 947



December 31, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For all of the foregoing reasons, the motion for an order controverting the warrant and dismissing the information is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought a ruling on their motions seeking an order controverting a search warrant, their motions to suppress evidence obtained seized pursuant to the warrant, and their motions to dismiss the complaints charging them with obscenity, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 235.05(1) and N.Y. Penal Law § 235.10(2).


OVERVIEW: Upon an application for a search warrant, a judge from the Supreme Court of New York reviewed 18 books and made a determination that they were obscene under the definition of N.Y. Penal Law § 235.00(1). The judge issued the search warrant, books were seized, and defendants were charged with obscenity in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 235.05(1) and N.Y. Penal Law § 235.10(2). Defendants filed motions to controvert the warrant, motions for suppression of evidence seized, and motions to dismiss the complaints against them. The court denied the motions, holding that while the titles to be seized did not appear on the face of the warrant, they were incorporated in the warrant by reference to the accompanying affidavit. The court held that the warrant specified with particularity what books could be seized. The court held because the issuing judge made a prior determination that the material was obscene, defendants could not complain that the items seized are not obscene and constitutionally protected. The court that because the search warrant was valid and properly issued, defendants were not entitled to suppression of the evidence or dismissal of the charges against them.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motions.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- search warrants -- Supreme Court Justice was given application for search warrant and 18 books alleged to be obscene; Justice kept and read books and issued search warrant; adversary hearing prior to issuance of search warrant was not required -- titles of books appear in affidavit but not on search warrant but are incorporated into warrant -- defendants cannot claim, before trial, that books are not obscene -- affidavit in support of warrant met requirements -- People v. Richmond County News (9 N Y 2d 578) not controlling as to present obscenity statute.

1. In a criminal prosecution against defendants charging obscenity in violation of subdivision 1 of section 235.05 and subdivision 2 of section 235.10 of the Penal Law, a search warrant had been obtained on an application with which 18 books had been delivered. The search warrant was issued after the Justice of the Supreme Court read the books. On this motion to controvert the search warrant, an adversary hearing prior to the issuance of the search warrant was not required. All that [***2] was required was prior judicial scrutiny and there was such scrutiny here.

2. While the titles to be seized do not appear on the face of the search warrant, they are incorporated in the warrant by reference to the affidavit. The officers were authorized to seize 18 specific titles and no more. There was no delegation to the officers of any authority to decide for themselves what could be seized.

3. Since the Supreme Court Justice determined that the items seized were obscene, defendants cannot before trial claim that the seized books are not obscene and constitutionally protected.

4. The affidavit in support of the warrant met the enunciated requirements. The reliability of the information supplied by informants was corroborated by detailed investigation made by the police officer.

5. People v. Richmond County News (9 N Y 2d 578) interpreted the former obscenity statute and does not define the limits of expression permissible under the State Constitution with respect to the present Penal Law ( § 235.00, subd. 1).

 

1886 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Lawson v. Mantell


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


62 Misc. 2d 307; 306 N.Y.S.2d 317; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 951



December 30, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion of the plaintiffs is accordingly denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff purchasers filed a motion for a preliminary injunction against defendant seller in the seller's action in replevin under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 71 to recover the merchandise sold to the purchasers who defaulted in payment.


OVERVIEW: The purchasers bought goods from the seller under a contract of conditional sale providing installment payment, with the seller reserving a security interest in the merchandise. Upon default in payment the seller elected to declare the entire balance due immediately. The purchasers asserted that the statute had to be struck down as unconstitutional because its provisions violated the rights to due process and equal protection afforded by U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court determined that the statute required that an action be commenced and that the replevin papers be served personally upon a defendant. The court explained that even then the chattel was not immediately awarded to plaintiff but was retained by the sheriff for a period of three days and defendant was allowed an opportunity to reclaim the same during that period. The court noted that the statute provided the purchasers with more liberal treatment that the contract. The court concluded that in civil matters the state could not be constitutionally required to provide for the economic inequality of parties. The court found nothing unequal in a statute that required one party to do nothing more than the other.


OUTCOME: The court denied the purchasers' motion for a preliminary injunction.


HEADNOTES

Replevin -- constitutional validity of replevin statute -- in action for declaration of invalidity of replevin statute ( CPLR art. 71), plaintiffs have not shown clear legal right to temporary injunction to restrain seller of goods under conditional sales contract from pursuing his remedy -- article 71 provides due process of law.

1. In an action for a declaration that the replevin statute, CPLR article 71, is unconstitutional, commenced by purchasers of goods under a conditional sales contract upon which they defaulted, the seller, defendant, then exercising his contractual right to declare the entire balance due immediately, plaintiffs have failed to establish a clear legal right to a temporary injunction so as to restrain defendant from proceeding with his remedy. The replevin remedy is ancient and there is a strong presumption of its constitutionality.

2. Article 71 of the CPLR provides due process of law by requiring personal service of process, if possible, before the chattel is seized and, even when seized, it is retained for three days to give the purchasers an opportunity to reclaim. Moreover, there is nothing [***2] unequal in a statute which requires plaintiff and defendant to each provide a bond.

 

1887 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Taddeo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Onondaga County


62 Misc. 2d 833; 310 N.Y.S.2d 424; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 955



December 24, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landlords appealed to the decision of the City Court of Syracuse, Criminal Division (New York), which found the landlords in violation of provisions of the Syracuse, New York, Housing Code. The landlords were each fined.


OVERVIEW: The landlords were convicted of violations of the Syracuse, New York, Housing Code. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions. The court held that the landlords had standing to challenge the violations. The court held that the pertinent sections of the statute were a valid exercise of the legislative power and were constitutionally enacted. The housing inspector obtained permission from the tenant to search the premises and did not need the landlords' permission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the landlords' convictions for violations of a city housing code.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- housing code inspections -- judgment convicting property owners of violations of city's Housing Code affirmed -- code is presumably constitutional -- tenant properly admitted city inspectors into premises.

The tenant in residence of defendants' building admitted city inspectors into the premises, and the inspectors found numerous violations of the city's Housing Code, such as inadequate exits, no fire protection, lack of repairs, etc.; and subsequently one of the two defendants went into the premises with the inspectors and was shown the violations. Thereafter, the defendants made no repairs, and hence this criminal prosecution was commenced against them, for violations of the city's Housing Code, and the defendants were properly convicted. The code is presumably valid and constitutional. The code provision which makes it an additional violation for an owner to refuse admittance to city inspectors is not involved in this case, since no such additional violation is charged. The code's lack of a provision for a search warrant is not involved, since the inspectors were properly admitted into these premises. Judgment convicting the defendants is affirmed.

 

1888 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Calicchio


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Westchester County


62 Misc. 2d 144; 306 N.Y.S.2d 566; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 957



December 23, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] With respect to the Grand Jury minutes, the motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to suppress all evidence pertaining to the alleged crimes of gambling in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 986.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stated that the indictments were based upon investigations of treasury agents made pursuing alleged violations for willfully failing to register and to pay an occupational tax for engaging in the business of accepting wagers as required by 26 U.S.C.S. §§ 4411-4412. The federal charges were dismissed or a nolle prosequi was filed and defendant was indicted and charged with the crime of violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 986. The court determined that federal officers were not disqualified from testifying in a state prosecution for violation of state gambling laws and evidence properly obtained by them could be used in the state prosecution. The court denied defendant's motion to suppress because the ability of the federal government to prosecute defendant for failure to follow the procedures presented by §§ 4411-4412 based upon federal investigations into violations of said statutes was not an element of a violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 986 based upon the same investigation. The court also denied defendant's motion for leave to inspect the grand jury minutes because the supporting affidavit failed to show that the indictment was not based upon sufficient evidence.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motions to suppress and for leave to inspect the grand jury minutes.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- gambling -- use of evidence acquired during Federal investigation -- motion by defendant, indicted for violating section 986 of Penal Law on basis of alleged gambling, to suppress evidence against him upon ground that it was acquired by Federal agents investigating his alleged failure to register and pay occupational tax, as required by sections 4411 and 4412 of title 26 of United States Code, is denied -- while United States Supreme Court has held that privilege against self incrimination is defense against prosecution for failure to comply with said Federal statutory provisions, it has not held said provisions unconstitutional -- ability of Federal Government to prosecute for failure to comply with said provisions is not element of violation of section 986 of Penal Law based upon same investigation.

1. A defendant indicted for violating section 986 of the Penal Law on the basis of his alleged commission of various acts of gambling, moves to suppress the evidence against him upon the ground that it was acquired by Federal Treasury Agents investigating an alleged failure by him to register and pay [***2] an occupational tax for engaging in the business of accepting wagers, as required by sections 4411 and 4412 of title 26 of the United States Code. The motion is denied.

2. While the United States Supreme Court has held that persons who assert their constitutional privilege against self incrimination as to said Federal statutory provisions may not be criminally punished for failure to comply therewith, it has not held the provisions unconstitutional. Moreover, it has held that the privilege against self incrimination does not require dismissal of an indictment charging a gambler with violating section 1001 of title 18 of the United States Code by filing false information in a report required by said section 4412 since, even though he would have been able to assert the privilege as a defense against a prosecution for failure to file a section 4412 report, the validity of the government demand for information is not an element of a section 1001 violation. Here, the ability of the Federal Government to prosecute for failure to comply with sections 4411 and 4412 based upon Federal investigations into violations thereof is not an element of a violation of section 986 of the Penal Law [***3] based upon the same investigation.

 

1889 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Wales v. Gallan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, Richmond County


61 Misc. 2d 681; 306 N.Y.S.2d 614; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 963



December 22, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion of the Commissioner of Social Services to join as copetitioner is granted, in view of the sworn allegation of information and belief that petitioner and the child are now public charges.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent alleged father sought a ruling on his motion to dismiss a paternity suit filed against him by petitioner mother under N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 517 and N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act. § 522. The Commissioner of Social Services sought a ruling on its motion to join the suit as co-petitioner.


OVERVIEW: Two years and seven months after her child was born out of wedlock, the mother filed a paternity action against the alleged father. He filed a motion to dismiss the action on the ground that the statute of limitations for such actions had expired. The Commissioner filed a motion to join as a co-petitioner. The court denied the motion to dismiss and granted the motion to join. The court held that the different statute of limitations contained in N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 517 and N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 522 were unconstitutional as violative of equal protection. The court held that the differentiation between public welfare officials and a child's mother as to statutes of limitations did not serve the purpose of protecting an alleged father from a stale claim. The court held that differentiation was entirely irrational and arbitrary. The court held that the 10-year statute of limitations should have been applied because it was the more beneficial provision. Thus, under that limitations period, the mother's paternity suit was not time barred. The court allowed the Commissioner to join as a co-petitioner in light of his allegation that the mother and the child had become public charges.


OUTCOME: The court denied the alleged father's motion to dismiss the paternity suit. The court granted the Commissioner's motion to join as co-petitioner.


HEADNOTES

Children born out of wedlock -- paternity proceedings -- Statute of Limitations -- although mother filed paternity petition 2 years and 7 months after birth of child, and hence 7 months too late, public welfare official was granted permission to join as copetitioner alleging that mother and child are public charges (Family Ct. Act, §§ 517, 522) -- Statute of Limitations on paternity petition by public welfare official is 10 years; limitation of 2 years on petition by mother unconstitutionally denies her equal protection.

1. A paternity proceeding must be commenced by the mother of the child within 2 years after the birth, unless the alleged father has acknowledged his paternity in writing or by furnishing support; however, a public welfare official may institute such a proceeding within 10 years after the birth if the mother or the child is, or is likely to become, a public charge (Family Ct. Act. §§ 517, 522). This inequality in the applicable Statute of Limitations contravenes [***2] the constitutional guarantees of equal protection of the laws.

2. In this case, the mother instituted this paternity proceeding 2 years and 7 months after the birth; and, when she admitted that the alleged father had not furnished support or acknowledged paternity, the local public welfare official moved to join as copetitioner, alleging that the mother and child are now public charges. Such motion is granted. At the hearing, the alleged father can dispute the allegation that the mother and child are public charges.

 

1890 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


City School Dist. v. Zeluck


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


63 Misc. 2d 613; 312 N.Y.S.2d 984; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 969; 73 L.R.R.M. 2264



December 19, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school district brought a proceeding by order to show cause that sought to punish defendant employees for criminal contempt for the alleged willful disobedience to an order of the court, a temporary restraining order enjoining them from striking and causing and inducing other employees to strike or engage in picketing. The employees filed a cross-motion to vacate the order to show cause or the execution.


OVERVIEW: The basis of the employees' cross-motion to vacate the order to show cause or the execution thereof was on jurisdictional grounds and the claimed unconstitutionality of law permitting the contempt sanction. The employees contended that the petition and order to show cause were ineffective for noncompliance with N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 211 and N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 201(4). The constitutional questions were not reached because the jurisdictional defects in the proceeding warranted the court's vacating the order. The court did not have jurisdiction because the application for the contempt finding was not made by the chief legal officer of the city in which the school district sat as required by N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 211.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order to show cause that sought to punish the employees for criminal contempt for the alleged willful disobedience to an order of the court.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Schools -- enforcement of Public Employees Fair Employment Act -- proceeding to punish employees for contempt was not commenced on application of "chief legal officer" ( Civil Service Law § 211), defined as corporation counsel of city, where applicant was attorney for school district; order to show cause is vacated.

 Section 211 of the Civil Service Law, part of the Taylor Law, provides that, if an order of the court restraining a violation is not complied with, the "chief legal officer" shall apply to the Supreme Court to punish such violation. The "chief legal officer" is defined ( Civil Service Law, § 201, subd. 4) as "the corporation counsel of the city in which such government or public employer has its principal office". An order to show cause to punish by contempt a violation of an order, obtained on the application of the attorney for plaintiff school district, is defective and must be vacated.

 

1891 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Arricale v. Power


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


61 Misc. 2d 653; 306 N.Y.S.2d 334; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 970



December 19, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate sought an order pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 directing respondent board to issue to him a certificate of election to the office of councilman.


OVERVIEW: The candidate was a member of the Liberal Party and sought an order directing the board to issue to him a certificate of election to the office of councilman. The democratic candidate received the largest number of votes and the Republican and Conservative Party candidate received the second largest number of votes from his parties' voters. The candidate argued that as one of the two remaining candidates receiving the largest number of votes, he was entitled to the remaining seat. The board and intervenor-candidate argued that the intervenor-candidate's combined vote on the Republican and conservative lines made him the candidate with the second largest vote. The court determined that there was nothing in the legislative history or the city's charter provision that precluded a combination of two minorities into a larger minority for political and electoral purposes. Therefore, the court determined that all the votes cast for a candidate for councilman, on whatever line, were required to be counted and totaled pursuant to the city's charter and the election law. Accordingly, the candidate's petition was dismissed and the stay was vacated.


OUTCOME: The proceeding was dismissed and the stay contained in the order to show cause was vacated.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Elections -- candidate of two parties -- in election for Councilman-at-Large in Borough of Bronx, Charter providing that each elector must vote for one councilman and that two receiving largest number of votes in each borough shall be elected, petitioner candidate of Liberal Party who received 70,054 votes was not elected over candidate of Republican Party who received 40,074 votes and as candidate of Conservative Party received additional 31,272 votes for total of 71,303 votes; votes for intervenor in both parties must be counted.

Section 22 of the New York City Charter states that two Councilmen-at-Large shall be elected from each borough, that no party shall nominate more than one candidate for Councilman-at-Large and that (subd. d) "Each elector shall have the right to vote for not more than one candidate at large and the two candidates receiving the largest number of votes in each borough shall be elected". At the general election on November 4, 1969, petitioner was the candidate of the Liberal Party in the Borough of The Bronx and received 70,054 votes. Intervenor was the candidate of the Republican Party and received 40,074 votes. Intervenor was also the candidate [***2] of the Conservative Party and received 31,272 votes. The candidate of the Democratic Party received a majority of the votes cast and she was elected as the first Councilman-at-Large. Petitioner contends that his party received the second highest number of votes and that he was elected as the second Councilman-at-Large, despite the fact that intervenor had a total of 71,303 votes as the candidate of the Republican and Conservative Parties. Although section 22 was intended to provide minority parties with representation on the City Council, it did not intend to exclude the votes received by intervenor as candidate of the second party in computing his total for otherwise those who voted for him in one of the parties would be disenfranchised. Intervenor was elected.

 

1892 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Eight Sherwood Corp. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, New York County


67 Misc. 2d 246; 324 N.Y.S.2d 253; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 973



December 18, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***2] Accordingly, the application is denied and the petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner assignee filed an application seeking review of a determination of respondent city, which sustained an assessment against the assignee for the purchase of certain realty at a foreclosure sale.


OVERVIEW: The assignee purchased certain realty at a foreclosure sale from a seller who was appointed by the district court to represent the interests of the mortgagee, the United States of America. The seller deeded the property to the assignee pursuant to the assignment. Thereafter, the assignee filed a real property transfer tax report stating that no tax was due because the transaction was exempt because the grantor was acting on behalf of the United States of America. The city audited the return and assessed the assignee the sum of $ 9,030.53 with interest. A hearing was held and the original assessment was sustained. The assignee filed an action pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 and argued that the assessment was double taxation since he was required to pay the transfer tax again when the property was resold. Further, the assignee challenged the constitutionality of N.Y. Tax Law § 1230. The court determined that the imposition of the transfer tax upon the assignee was not the equivalent to double taxation since the same was not being taxed twice. Further, the court held that the assignee presumably knew the law and assumed the tax liability ordinarily owed by the grantor.


OUTCOME: The application was denied and the petition was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- New York City's tax on real property transfers -- grantee at sale on foreclosure of mortgage held by United States of America is not exempt from New York City's tax on deeds.

The judgment in a mortgage foreclosure action by the United States of America directed that the property be sold by a Master who had been appointed by the United States District Court to represent the interests of said mortgagee. The Master sold the property to a private corporation, which assigned its bid to another private corporation, so the Master executed a deed to the latter corporation. Said grantee must pay the New York City tax on deeds. The United States of America is properly exempted from the New York City tax on deeds "where it is the purchaser" (Tax Law, § 1230, subd. [b], as amd. by L. 1965, ch. 575); and the tax properly falls on the nonexempt "grantee" (Administrative Code of City of New York, § II46-6.0, subd. a, par. 2; § II46-4.0). This is not unconstitutional, nor is it double taxation. If and when this grantee sells the property, it will have to pay a tax as a "grantor", but that tax will [***3] be on a different transaction.

 

1893 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Patterson v. Daquet


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Civil Court of the City of New York, Kings County


62 Misc. 2d 106; 308 N.Y.S.2d 173; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 976



December 17, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landlords brought an eviction action against respondent tenant upon expiration of a lease, contending that a municipal rent stabilization law was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Rent Stabilization Law of 1969 (RSL), New York City, N.Y., Local Law 16, authorized voluntary self-regulation of the housing industry by an association of real property owners under the supervision of the New York City Housing and Development Administration (HDA). However, the HDA reserved the right to refuse registration under the RSL unless landlords enacted a code approved by the HDA. The court found in favor of the landlords and against the tenant in eviction proceedings because the RSL unconstitutionally delegated to a private agency the right to make its own rules and regulations having the force of law administered via the opinions, whims, arguments, dreams, and nightmares of the HDA lawyers as reflected in their transient daily, weekly or monthly by-laws.


OUTCOME: The court entered a decision in favor of the landlords and against the tenant, and held that the rent stabilization law was unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Landlord and tenant -- rent regulation -- "Rent Stabilization Law of 1969" -- "Rent Stabilization Law of 1969" (Local Laws, 1969, No. 16 of City of New York) providing for voluntary regulation of rents in housing constructed after 1947 is unconstitutional.

The "Rent Stabilization Law of 1969" (Local Laws, 1969, No. 16 of City of New York) providing for voluntary self-regulation of the housing industry by an association of real property owners under the supervision of the New York City Housing and Development Administration, which requires each association to adopt a code for the regulation of rent increases in housing constructed after February 1, 1947 is unconstitutional.

 

1894 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re John Children


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, New York Citywide Child Abuse Term


61 Misc. 2d 347; 306 N.Y.S.2d 797; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 995



December 12, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent parents challenged the constitutionality of article 10 of the New York Family Court Act as it presumptively mandated the removal of children from the custody of a parent who was adjudged to be addicted to narcotics.


OVERVIEW: The parents argued that art; 10 of the New York Family Court Act was unconstitutional because it presumptively mandated the removal of abused children from parental custody. Under N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 1012 an abused child was a child under 16 years of age who had serious physical or mental injury inflicted upon him who was in the custody of a parent or other person who had been adjudicated a narcotic addict. The court held a portion of art. 10 of the New York Family Court Act invalid. The court stated that the portion of art. 10 dealing with automatic stays on appeal was invalid. In so far as N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 1112 was mandatory it was invalid. This section addressed the staying of orders where the effect of the order was to discharge the child to the custody of the alleged abusive parent. The court said that the statute would have unconstitutionally vested in a petitioner who brought false or baseless charges against a parent the judicial power to overrule a family court judge. The court believed the statute to otherwise be reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court invalidated a portion of a statute which dealt with automatic stays on appeal of orders in child abuse case, but found the statute otherwise reasonable.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Infants -- removal from custody of narcotic-addicted parents -- after hearing, Family court may order removal and placement of children of narcotic-addicted parents (Family Ct. Act, §§ 1012, 1022) -- statute as construed is constitutional -- jury trial not required -- hospital records admissible -- "person who has been adjudicated a narcotic addict" (Family Ct. Act, § 1012) means "who is adjudicated a narcotic addict" by Family Court -- court suggests that various sections of statute be amended -- section 1112 of Family Court Act, mandatorily staying child abuse order while appeal is pending, is unconstitutional.

1. Article 10 (§§ 1011-1025) of the Family Court Act defines an "abused child" as one under age 16 "who has had serious physical or mental injury inflicted upon him by other than accidental means or who is in the care and custody of a parent or other person who has been adjudicated a narcotic addict" (§ 1012); and it provides that "After a hearing * * *, if the court shall determine that such allegations are established, the court shall enter an order directing the removal of such child from his home until such order is modified, and providing for his placement as [***2] the court shall determine" (§ 1022). This means that the court "shall" make such an order unless the presumption that the child needs to be removed from the custody of the narcotic-addicted parent is rebutted. The Legislature intended that the provisions of article 3 of the Family Court Act as to hearings, placements, etc., as well as the provisions of article 8 as to orders of protection, etc., should be applicable. The Legislature also intended that the Family Court should use the definition of "narcotic addict" which is set forth in the Mental Hygiene Law (art. 9, § 201, subd. 2): -- "a person who is * * * dependent upon opium, heroin, morphine or any derivative or synthetic drug of that group or who by reason of the repeated use of any such drug is in imminent danger of becoming dependent upon opium, heroin," etc. As thus construed, section 1022 of the Family Court Act affords due process and equal protection and is constitutional and valid.

2. A jury trial is not required by statute or Constitution for a determination by the Family Court that a person is a narcotic addict.

3. In a child abuse proceeding, hospital records showing a parent's narcotic addiction, as well as [***3] the hospital records of the symptoms and treatment of a baby born to such a narcotic-addicted mother, are admissible in evidence (Family Ct. Act, § 1018; Social Services Law, § 383-a, subd. 1-b; CPLR 4518, subd. [a]).

4. The words in section 1012 of the Family Court Act -- "a parent or other person who has been adjudicated a narcotic addict" -- mean a person who is adjudicated a narcotic addict by the Family Court in the child abuse proceeding; that is, the section does not require that there be a prior adjudication by the Supreme Court or Family Court or any other court.

5. The court suggests that the Legislature should clarify said section 1012 of the Family Court Act by amending "who has been adjudicated" to read "who is adjudicated".

6. The court further suggests that the Legislature should amend said section 1012 of the Family Court Act by making it applicable to any child -- and particularly a female child -- under age 18 (cf. Family Ct. Act, art. 3, § 312, definition of "neglected child").

7. The court further suggests that the Legislature should likewise amend the definition of "person in need of supervision" in article 7 of the Family Court Act so as to make it [***4] applicable to children -- and particularly a male child -- under age 18.

8. Section 1112 (of art. 11) of the Family Court Act provides that, pending the determination of an appeal from an intermediate or final order or decision in a child abuse proceeding, "such order or decision shall be stayed where the effect of such order or decision would be to discharge the child." The quoted portion of this section contravenes due process and the constitutional powers of the Family Court and therefore is invalid.

 

1895 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Keough


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Monroe County


61 Misc. 2d 762; 305 N.Y.S.2d 961; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1008



December 10, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a demurrer with a trial court (New York) that challenged their indictments and alleged that the facts within the indictment did not constitute a crime under N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law §§ 316(d), (f).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were accused of violating § 316 based on their alleged unlawful printing and public distribution of a publication that contained photographs that defiled and case contempt upon the flag of the United States. Defendants demurred to the indictments and alleged that the facts stated in the indictment did not constitute a crime and that the facts, if true, constituted a legal justification for the acts charged that barred prosecution. The court disallowed the demurrers and held that the indictment was sufficient because it stated that defendants violated a valid statute and the alleged facts constituted a crime.


OUTCOME: The court disallowed defendants' demurrer to the indictments.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- defilement of flag of United States -- indictment charging defendants with defiling flag of United States in violation of General Business Law ( § 136, subds. d, f) is valid; demurrer disallowed.

An indictment charges defendants with a violation of subdivisions d and f of section 136 of the General Business Law in that defendants unlawfully printed and distributed a publication containing photographs which defiled and cast contempt upon the flag of the United States and in that defendants, at the same time and place, unlawfully caused to be publicly displayed an emblem and flag contained in photographs in a publication in such a manner as to cast contempt upon the flag of the United States. Defendants' demurrer to the indictment is disallowed. It is sufficient. It states the violation of a valid statute and the facts stated constitute a crime.

 

1896 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Babylon v. Conte


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


61 Misc. 2d 626; 305 N.Y.S.2d 553; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1024



December 3, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion, therefore, is in all respects granted and the cross motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town sought a preliminary injunction restraining defendant owners from maintaining, operating or permitting the operation of a place of public assembly as a cabaret, bar or lounge, dance hall or discotheque establishment without a license as required by Babylon, N.Y., Unified Code of Ordinances ch. VII, § 705. The owners' cross motion sought to vacate a temporary restraining order as violative of their constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The owners had a license to operate their club, which was suspended by the town building inspector and not renewed because the owners permitted "topless dancing." Section 705 specifically authorized license revocation where such topless dancing was permitted. The owners filed a cross motion seeking to vacate the temporary restraining order already issued, arguing that such order violated their constitutional rights. The court held that: 1) the ordinance was presumed constitutional absent proof of its invalidity beyond a reasonable doubt; 2) a lower court of limited jurisdiction had no authority to determine the constitutionality of the ordinance; and 3) such determination had to be made by a court of competent jurisdiction in a declaratory judgment action. The court further held that, in a previous action involving the same litigants and substantially the same issues, a court of competent jurisdiction had recognized the validity of the ordinance, and granted the town summary judgment enjoining the same acts, which were the subject of the town's motion for injunctive relief. Therefore, the court held there were no valid grounds to deny the temporary injunction.


OUTCOME: The court granted the town's motion and denied the owners' cross-motion.


HEADNOTES

Licenses -- topless dancing prohibited -- District Court of county has no jurisdiction to adjudge ordinance unconstitutional (cf. CPLR 3001); moreover, Supreme Court enjoined defendants against allowing topless dancing in their licensed entertainment establishment; accordingly, in present action in Supreme Court, defendants are preliminarily restrained from operating their establishment.

Pursuant to a town ordinance requiring cabarets, bars, dance halls and discotheque establishments to be licensed, and prohibiting so-called "topless" dancing therein, and authorizing the town's Building Inspector to revoke the license of any such establishment which violates the ordinance, defendants' license was suspended. Thereafter the District Court of the county granted to said defendants a judgment declaring the ordinance unconstitutional; however, only the Supreme Court has jurisdiction to grant such a declaratory adjudication ( CPLR 3001); and the Supreme Court did thereafter grant to the town a summary judgment enjoining said defendants from thus violating their license. Accordingly, in the present [***2] action in the Supreme Court, the town is granted a preliminary injunction restraining said defendants from operating their establishment.

 

1897 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Day


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Herkimer County


61 Misc. 2d 786; 306 N.Y.S.2d 610; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1029



December 2, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motions of the defendants herein are hereby granted, and the right to trial by jury is granted in each case.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, who were found eligible to be treated as youthful offenders, demanded a jury trial. The demand and motion was opposed by the district attorney and decision at that time was reserved.


OVERVIEW: Defendants had been charged with several counts of burglaries and larcenies. The consents to be investigated contained a waiver of a jury trial. Without such a consent and a waiver, treatment as youthful offenders would have been denied because such an investigation could not be conducted without defendants' consent. Such waivers had not been considered the voluntary knowing act of the minors who were considered youthful offenders because the waiver was surplusage. The court determined that defendants were accused of serious crimes which, if convicted, might have involved confinement in the State institution for a considerable period of time. The court explained that while some of the criminal disability of conviction may have been eliminated and moderated once defendants were treated as youthful offenders, they still faced imprisonment for a serious crime, so they were entitled to all of the protections that the law allowed. The court noted that the mandate for a jury trial contained in U.S. Const. amend. VI applied to all serious crimes. The court concluded that a person declared eligible for treatment as a youthful offender was entitled to a trial by jury.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motions for a trial by jury.


HEADNOTES

Infants -- youthful offenders -- despite waivers of jury trials, youthful offenders are entitled to jury trials.

Persons who are declared eligible for youthful offender treatment are entitled to jury trials, despite their previously executed waivers of jury trials.

 

1898 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Falcone v. Zingerline


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Oneida County


61 Misc. 2d 885; 306 N.Y.S.2d 785; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1036



November 28, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the petitioner's application to permanently enjoin the respondent Examining Board of Plumbers and the City of Rome from the collection of the $ 10 annual renewal fee for registration of plumbers is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner plumber instituted a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding against respondents, the Commissioner of Public Works of the City of Rome and the Examining Board of Plumbers of the City of Rome, protesting the imposition by respondents of a $ 10 recertification fee for his master plumber's license.


OVERVIEW: Respondents imposed a recertification fee when the plumber attempted to renew his master plumber's license. The court denied the plumber's application to permanently enjoin respondents from the collection of the annual renewal fee. The court found that by enacting N.Y. Gen. City Law art. 4, which provided state-wide legislation in the field of plumbing, the State did not intend to pre-empt the field of plumbing. The court found that § 4(4) granted the power to the board to charge the fee and the city enacted Rome City, N.Y., Code § 10-76 pursuant to this authority. The court held that the imposition of the fee, which was not prohibited by the state law, was a valid exercise of the municipality's powers granted to the city to act in relation to its own property, affairs or government, under N. Y. Const. art. IX, § 2(b)(2) and state statute. The court found that the annual renewal was implicitly mandated N.Y. Gen. City Law § 50, which provided that all licenses issued by the board expired and the licenses could be renewed. The court found that the fee had a reasonable relationship to the board's expenses for issuing the renewals and was not an unconstitutional revenue-producing tax.


OUTCOME: The court denied the plumber's application to permanently enjoin respondents from the collection of the annual renewal fee.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- licenses -- city's Examining Board of Plumbers validly and constitutionally requires $ 10 annual fee for renewals of plumbers' licenses.

The Examining Board of Plumbers of the City of Rome passed a resolution which validly and constitutionally requires a $ 10 annual fee for renewing and recertifying a master plumber's license (Rome City Code, § 10-76; General City Law, § 44, subd. 4; § 45-b; § 50; N. Y. Const., art. IX, § 2, subd. [b], par. [2]). The $ 10 bears a reasonable relation to the board's expenses of processing such annual renewals.

 

1899 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Teachers Asso., Cent. High School Dist. v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


61 Misc. 2d 492; 305 N.Y.S.2d 724; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1055; 72 L.R.R.M. 2858



November 20, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The respondent may have judgment dismissing the petition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner teacher's association sought confirmation of an award in an arbitration between the association and respondent school board.


OVERVIEW: The association filed a petition for confirmation of an arbitrator's award, which included a provision for compensation for unused sick leave when an employee left for reasons other than retirement, involuntary separation, or after a request for resignation. The board argued that the payment of unused sick leave would be an ultra vires act, and, therefore, illegal. The court dismissed the petition. The court held that N.Y. Educ. Law § 1709, which granted the board the power to adopt rules regarding absences with and without pay did not give the board authority to pay for unused sick leave. The court held that payment for unused sick leave would amount to a gift of public funds, in violation of N.Y. Const. art. VIII, § 1. The court held that the award was contrary to public policy.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the association's petition for confirmation of an arbitration award against the board.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- teachers -- collective negotiation agreements -- school district cannot agree to pay for unused personal sick leave; arbitration award directing school district to pay such agreed sum of money to deceased teacher's estate is invalid and unenforceable.

In an agreement between a school district and a teachers' association for collective negotiation and arbitration (Civil Service Law, art. 14), a provision that, if a teacher voluntarily left the employ of the school district, he should be granted "an increase in current salary equivalent to current pay for accumulated unused personal sick leave", which, in the case of 15 years of service would be equal to 20% of accumulated personal sick leave, and that, if a teacher died while in the school district's employ, the same benefit should be paid to his estate or other designated beneficiary, is contrary to public policy. (N. Y. Const., art. VIII, § 1; General Municipal Law, § 92, subd. 1; Education Law, § 1709, subd. 16; Opinions of State Comptroller; Opinion of Counsel for State Educ. Dept.) Accordingly, an arbitration award, directing the school district [***2] to pay to the estate of a deceased teacher a sum of money in lieu of days of personal sick leave accumulated prior to her death, is invalid and unenforceable.

 

1900 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Scott v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


61 Misc. 2d 333; 305 N.Y.S.2d 601; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1063



November 18, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, minor's guardian, brought an action against respondent school district to enjoin the school district from enforcing its dress code that prohibited girls from wearing slacks to school.


OVERVIEW: When the minor wore slacks to school, she missed classes because she was placed in detention. The minor's guardian alleged that the regulations were unreasonable and unlawful because they violated standards set by the Commissioner of Education, the equal protection clause of the United States Constitution, and the minor's rights of free speech and expression under N.Y. Const. art. I, § 8 and the U.S. Const. amend. I, XIV. The minor's guardian alleged that the regulations were unconstitutionally vague and bore no reasonable relation to health, welfare, or the education process. The court held that dress code was valid only to the extent necessary to protect the safety of the wearer, male or female, or to control disturbances or distractions that interfered with the education of other students. The court held that the dress code prohibition against girls wearing slacks to school was null and void. The proscription against girls wearing slacks to school bore no reasonable relationship to health, welfare, or the prevention of disturbances or distractions that would interfere with the educational process. The slacks policy exceeded the school district's authority.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment annulling the paragraph of the school district's code of regulations that prohibited girls from wearing slacks to school.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- dress regulations -- regulation adopted by school board, prohibiting girls from wearing slacks except when permitted by principal, is adjudged void.

The Board of Education of a school district adopted "Dress Regulations for the Secondary School" which, in part, flatly prohibited "girls wearing slacks" except when "permitted by the principal between December 1 and March 31 on petition by the student council when warranted by cold or inclement weather". This flat prohibition is adjudged null and void by Special Term of the Supreme Court. (Education Law, § 1709, subds. 2, 8-a, 8-b, 33.) The board submitted the proposed dress regulations to a referendum of the students and their parents, and such submission was commendable; however, such referendum cannot give to the board authority which it does not lawfully have. It was not necessary for petitioner and her mother to appeal to the State Commissioner of Education before instituting this proceeding for judicial review of the board's unlawful act.

 

1901 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Rose v. Barraud


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


61 Misc. 2d 377; 305 N.Y.S.2d 721; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1094



November 7, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, individual objectors to the incorporation of a town, sought to set aside the decision of respondent town supervisor that the petition to incorporate complied with N.Y. Village Law art. 3.


OVERVIEW: The objectors claimed that the map attached to the petition to incorporate was improper in scale and did not comply with N.Y. Village Law § 3-302(1)(c)(1). They also made a broad allegation of unconstitutionality of the statute or its application. The argued that the supervisor should have refused approval to the incorporation because the area lacked contiguity, was gerrymandered, contained excessive commercial and industrial areas, did not contain the whole of the community in the sociological sense, removed excessive tax base from the unincorporated area of the town, and deliberately left without its boundary property which was not subject to real estate tax but which served the community. All of the parties conceded that affixed to the petition was a full description by metes and bounds of the area sought to be incorporated. The court denied the objectors' petition. Section 3-302(1)(c)(1) permitted the description to be made by a metes and bounds description. There was no constitutional right to the continued maintenance of the tax base or any municipal organization. Therefore, there was no statutory or common-law authority to support the objectors' contentions.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition of the objectors.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- incorporation of village -- since petition to incorporate territory as village contained sufficient metes-and-bounds description, immaterial that map, which was drawn on scale of 1 inch = 1,000 feet, bore erroneous legend "1 inch = 500 feet" -- statute does not empower town Supervisor to determine objections that proposed territory is gerrymandered and that it would remove excessive taxable realty from rest of town; statute is constitutional.

1. A petition by residents of an unincorporated area, to incorporate the area as a village, must, among other things, describe the area or territory by metes and bounds or by existing boundaries or by a map (Village Law, § 3-302, subd. 1, par. c, subpar. [1]). The petition in this case contained a sufficient description by metes and bounds; hence it was immaterial that the annexed map, which was drawn on a scale of 1 inch to 1,000 feet, bore a legend "1 inch = 500 feet".

2. The petition was properly approved as to form by the Supervisor of the town (Village Law, §§ 3-306, 3-308, 3-310). The cited sections validly and constitutionally omit any authority in the Supervisor to determine such substantive objections [***2] as that the proposed territory is gerrymandered, that it lacks contiguity, that it does not contain the whole of the community for which it is proposed to be named, that it contains excessive commercial and industrial areas, that it removes an excessive amount of taxable realty from the unincorporated part of the town, and that it leaves outside of the limits of the proposed village the nontaxable fire stations and schools and churches which serve the whole community.

 

1902 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


East Neck Estates, Ltd. v. Luchsinger


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


61 Misc. 2d 619; 305 N.Y.S.2d 922; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1105



November 3, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowner challenged the power of respondent town planning board to require the dedication of a certain strip of shorefront to the town as a condition for the approval of a proposed residential subdivision.


OVERVIEW: The subdivision in issue was a rectangular tract along the shoreline. Thirty building plots were contemplated. A strip of the land along the water was unsuitable for home construction. The board, concerned with the rapidly diminishing availability of public shorefront and aware of the unique suitability of a beach front for recreational purposes, required that the landowner dedicate to the town a strip of land 80 feet wide from the high-water line across the entire frontage. The landowner declined. N.Y. Town Law § 277(1) did not explicitly require dedication of the park area to the town. The board had the power to require a sum of money in lieu of land. The landowner contended that the value of the land was so disproportionate to the value of the whole tract that confiscation resulted. The court found that the value of the tract at the time of sale would have been decreased significantly if the 80-foot strip were in public ownership. The court held that the board's demand was confiscatory. The proceeding was remitted to the board for further action. Even assuming that the board did have the power to require dedication, standards of due process and reasonableness were required.


OUTCOME: The proceeding was remitted to the board for action consistent with the court's opinion, which stated that the standards of due process and reasonableness were required.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- Planning Board's requirements of subdivider -- Planning Board's requirement, that subdivider of $ 208,000 tract dedicate $ 92,000 worth of beach front to town, is confiscatory; matter is remitted to Planning Board.

A corporation bought for $ 208,000 a 23-acre tract fronting for about 557 feet on the southerly side of Long Island Sound in Suffolk County. The town's Planning Board required, as a condition of approving the corporation's residential subdivision plat, that the corporation dedicate to the town for recreational purpose ( Town Law, § 277, subd. 1; § 278, subd. 1; § 280-a), the entire beach front, 80 feet wide. Such a strip is worth about $ 92,000. This is a confiscatory requirement. There are other, more reasonable ways under the cited statutes for making the shore front available for recreational purposes. The matter is remitted to the Planning Board accordingly.

 

1903 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Becher


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Surrogate's Court of New York, New York County


61 Misc. 2d 46; 304 N.Y.S.2d 628; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1107



October 31, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the application to withdraw the funds is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner alien beneficiary brought an application against for an order against respondent that would allow him to withdraw certain funds that he had inherited from the residuary of a decedent's estate that were being held on deposit for his benefit.


OVERVIEW: Funds that the alien beneficiary, who was a resident of East Germany, inherited from the residuary of the decedent's estate were held on deposit for his benefit. The alien beneficiary sought an order against respondent that would allow him to withdraw the funds. The court granted the application. The court found that N.Y. Surr. Ct. Proc. Act Law § 2218(1)(a) applied to the case because East Germany was a country to which checks or warrants drawn against funds of the United States could not be transmitted. The court held that the alien beneficiary had sustained the burden of proof of showing that he would have the benefit, use, and control of the money.


OUTCOME: The court granted the application for an order against respondent that would allow the alien beneficiary to withdraw the funds.


HEADNOTES

Executors and administrators -- funds due to foreign national -- funds to which resident of East Germany was entitled by intestacy were properly paid into court under SCPA 2218 -- on beneficiary's application to withdraw funds, he must establish that he would have use and benefit of funds -- this must be proven even if he appears in person -- beneficiary sustained burden of proof and his application to withdraw is granted.

1. Since East Germany is a country "to which checks or warrants drawn against funds of the United States may not be transmitted", funds to which a resident of East Germany was entitled by intestacy were properly paid into court under paragraph (a) of subdivision 1 of SCPA 2218 which is applicable.

2. On said resident's application in person to the court to withdraw the funds, the standard to be applied is that set forth in subdivision 2 of said section, i.e., whether the beneficiary would have the benefit or use or control of the money.

3. The standard must be applied even if the beneficiary appears in person. It is the domicile or residence of the alien legatee which is determinative.

 [***2] 4. The beneficiary sustained the burden of proving that he would have the benefit, use and control of the money. In East Germany he can use the money with a purchasing power roughly comparable to its purchasing power in this country. His application to withdraw the funds is granted.

 

1904 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Altman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


District Court of New York, Second District, Nassau County


61 Misc. 2d 4; 304 N.Y.S.2d 534; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1124



October 23, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with violating a town ordinance that prohibited seaplanes from taking off or landing upon any portion of the town's channel system except in emergency situations.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted landing his aircraft in violation of the town ordinance on two occasions, but argued that the ordinance was not enforceable. The court rejected defendant's arguments and found him guilty. Defendant first argued that local governments were preempted from the right to govern the use of airways and seaplane ways by the laws of the United States and by the administrative action of the Federal Aviation Agency. The court rejected this argument because defendant failed to establish that the federal government preempted the States in the particular area affected by this ordinance. Further, the court found that this ordinance was in harmony with the federal law. The court also rejected defendant's claim that the ordinance was an unconstitutional burden upon the interstate commerce clause of the United States Constitution.
