In reaching this conclusion, the court distinguished a prior decision from another state that struck down a state statute that provided for the right to bring wrongful death actions by legitimate, and not illegitimate, children. The court noted that, unlike the prior case, there was no New York statute that deprived the objectants of their inherent rights. Moreover, the court noted that the prior decision could not alter the impact and effect of the law of England which governed the right to share in the present case, and precluded the objectants from qualifying as distributees.


OUTCOME: The court denied the objectants' motion to set aside a decree declaring that they were not entitled to share as distributees in the estate of the decedent.


HEADNOTES

Descent and distribution -- legitimacy -- objectants, held not entitled to share in estate because of illegitimacy of their progenitors, not deprived of equal protection of laws under Levy v. Louisiana (391 U.S. 68) since no New York statute is involved -- denial of costs and disbursements was proper since services of attorneys for objectants did not benefit estate.

1. Objectants were held not entitled to share in this estate as distributees because of the illegitimacy of their progenitors (57 Misc 2d 982). The decision in Levy v. Louisiana (391 U.S. 68) does not change the result. There is no New York statute here which deprives objectants of the equal protection of the law. The Levy decision does not alter the impact and effect of the law of England, where decedent resided, and which governed the right to share and was controlling.

2. The denial of costs and disbursements to objectants was proper. Objectants were unsuccessful in proving their kinship to decedent. The criterion for the award of costs and disbursements is whether the services of the attorneys for objectants benefited the estate and [***2] not whether the services rendered aided the court. The services did not benefit the estate.

 

1948 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Patrolmen's Benevolent Asso. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


59 Misc. 2d 556; 299 N.Y.S.2d 986; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1574



April 30, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The cross motion for summary judgment is granted. The main motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a patrolmen's union and its members, filed an action claiming breach of a collective bargaining agreement by defendants, City of New York and associated officials, and moved for an order declaring 1969 N.Y. Laws ch. 177 unconstitutional and enjoining defendants from dividing patrolmen into more than three platoons and requiring excessive hours of employment. Defendants filed a cross-motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs claimed that defendants were committed to the three-platoon system under the collective bargaining agreement and that 1969 N.Y. Laws ch. 177, which contained special provisions applying to police assignments within the City of New York, unconstitutionally denied equal protection of the laws and as applied to the agreement impaired the obligation of contract. The court determined that no triable issue was raised by plaintiffs' claim that equal protection of the law was denied because, as shown by statistical charts furnished by defendants, the City of New York stood in a different situation from other municipalities within the State of New York with respect to the potential for violence and other emergencies. The court also ruled that plaintiffs failed to establish that any commitment to the three-platoon system existed in the agreement and that all prior negotiations merged in the agreement. The court further determined that the enactment of 1969 N.Y. Laws 177 under the Home Rule Law did not violate the constitutional prohibition against impairment of contract.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' cross-motion for summary judgment and denied plaintiffs' motion.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- police -- amendatory statute, abolishing, as to New York City police force, requirement for three shifts, and authorizing city's Police Commissioner to "distribute the available police force according to the relative need for its services", is constitutional.

In the hours between 6:00 p.m. and 2:00 a.m. in the City of New York, the incidence of crimes of personal violence and the incidence of calls for the police are respectively 47.1% and 44.6% of the daily total; yet, because of the three-shift system, which is called the three-platoon system (L. 1911, ch. 360; L. 1966, ch. 1005), less than 35% of the police force is on duty during those hours. Moreover, widespread emergencies may occur at any hour. Accordingly, on home rule request, the cited statutes were amended by chapter 177 of the Laws of 1969, so as to omit, as to the New York City police force, the requirement for three shifts, and so as to authorize the city's Police Commissioner to "distribute the available police force according to the relative need for its services." Under this amendment, the Police Commissioner [***2] has at present instituted a four-platoon system. This amendment does not deprive the police of the equal protection of the laws or of the prior statutes, nor does it impair the existing collective bargaining contract between the city and the Patrolmen's Benevolent Association. The city is granted summary judgment dismissing this action by the Patrolmen's Benevolent Association for a declaratory judgment and injunction.

 

1949 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Carl Ahlers, Inc. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, New York County


59 Misc. 2d 634; 300 N.Y.S.2d 428; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1595



April 24, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wholesale egg dealers questioned whether the City of New York could have forbade to interstate commerce liquid and frozen eggs which met the federal standard of identity, unless said egg products were inspected and legended by the service authorized pursuant to 7 U.S.C.S. § 1622(h),which specifically stated that no person was required to use the service authorized by the subsection.


OVERVIEW: The New York City Health Code mandated continuous inspection and legending of liquid and frozen eggs in accordance with the regulations promulgated by the United States Secretary of Agriculture. The egg dealers contended the health code regulations interfered with, burdened, and discriminated against interstate commerce because Congress, by providing a standard of identity for liquid and frozen eggs and offering a service, for continuous inspection and legending of egg products, which was voluntary, not mandatory, pre-empted the field. The court held that the regulations were unconstitutional and void insofar as they violated the egg dealers' rights and privileges in interstate commerce, but were constitutional and valid as to their activities in intrastate commerce. The regulations were inconsistent with the requirements of the federal law, for they forbade to interstate commerce what the federal government authorized. The city mandated a further requirement and burdened the use of a service that the federal authority specifically stated was not to have been mandated. Therefore, the regulations did not supplement the federal prescription; they infringed upon it.


OUTCOME: The court held that the city's regulations regarding legending of certain egg products was unconstitutional as to interstate commerce, but constitutional as to intrastate commerce.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- regulation of broken out eggs -- labeling requirement of New York City Health Code as to broken out eggs is inconsistent with Federal law and void as to regulation of sale in interstate commerce of broken out eggs but constitutional as to regulation of sale in intrastate commerce -- no denial of equal protection by regulation of broken out eggs but no other egg products.

1. Section 81.48 of the New York City Health Code provides that no broken out eggs shall be brought into and sold in the city unless pasteurized to remove salmonella micro-organisms in accordance with regulations of the United States Secretary of Agriculture. Section 81.49 provides that the container of liquid or frozen eggs shall bear a label, containing the date when and place where the eggs were broken out, and other items. The United States Secretary of Agriculture provides a service for voluntary, continuous inspection of egg products and for placing a legend on the products indicating that they have been inspected. Subdivision (h) of section 1622 of title 7 of the United States Code provides that "no person shall be required to use the service". Sections 81.48 and 81.49 of [***2] the New York City Health Code are inconsistent with Federal law in that they require the use of a labeling service which the Federal law says no one "shall be required to use", and are unconstitutional insofar as interstate commerce is concerned. They are constitutional as to plaintiffs' activities in intrastate commerce.

2. Defendant city did not violate the equal protection clause by regulating liquid and frozen eggs and not regulating other egg products.

 

1950 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Mandelbaum


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Surrogate's Court of New York, Nassau County


59 Misc. 2d 456; 299 N.Y.S.2d 363; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1599



April 23, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the appeal is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant executrix sought review of a pro forma order fixing the estate tax on the grounds that appellee tax commission allegedly failed to allow a full insurance exemption pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law § 958.


OVERVIEW: Appellant executrix sought review from a pro forma order fixing the estate tax on the grounds that appellee tax commission failed to allow a full insurance exemption. The last section of N.Y. Tax Law § 958 directed that the amount of the insurance exemption should be reduced by the amount of the marital deduction. Appellant executrix contended that the legislature intended it to mean only those insurance proceeds, which were necessary to satisfy the marital deduction. Consequently, appellant executrix argued she should be allowed a full insurance exemption pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law § 983 because the insurance funds were not necessary in satisfying the martial deduction. The court found the statute allowed insurance exemptions, provided that the insurance exemption coupled with the marital deduction did not exceed $ 100,000. Accordingly, appellant executrix's appeal was denied.


OUTCOME: Appeal denied because the statute allowed an insurance exemption when the insurance exemption coupled with the marital deduction did not exceed $ 100,000 and appellant executrix failed to demonstrate that the statute violated the U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- estate tax -- spouse's insurance exemption plus marital deduction cannot exceed $ 100,000 (Tax Law, § 958, subd. [b], par. [3]) -- statute constitutional.

1. In an adjusted gross estate of approximately $ 186,000, the marital deduction was approximately $ 93,000, and the wife received the latter amount in full. In addition, she received insurance proceeds amounting to $ 57,297.62. So much of said insurance as, coupled with said marital deduction, exceeds $ 100,000, is subject to estate tax (Tax Law, § 958, subd. [b], par. [3]). The last sentence of said paragraph (3) is not to the contrary.

2. The executrix has failed to meet the burden of demonstrating that the statute violates the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution.

 

1951 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ditniak


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Justice Court of New York, Town of Ulster, Ulster County


59 Misc. 2d 264; 299 N.Y.S.2d 593; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1607



April 21, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the informations herein are dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with violating N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 21, § 103.1, when they failed to comply with New York Thruway Authority regulations which closed all service areas on the New York Thruway System to charter buses for a period of time. At trial, defendants challenged the validity of the regulation under the Equal Protection Clause.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were issued uniform traffic tickets by the New York State Police on the Thruway for failing to comply with sign which read "Closed to Charter Buses -- Midnight Friday to Midnight Sunday." Charter buses and their passengers were denied the use of restaurant, rest rooms, and parking facilities. The court noted that the Authority regulation in question did not operate uniformly on all members of the class; i.e., buses. It discriminated against a part of the class. This hostile legislation discriminated against charter buses in contrast with private cars, regular route buses, trucks and buses belonging to private corporations or associations that transport their own members. Therefore, equal protection of the laws was denied. The court held that the regulation was unconstitutional under the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution and N.Y. Const. art. I, § 11. The regulation barring charter buses was an abuse of administrative discretion in that it was too broad and that the classification was arbitrary, unfair, and discriminatory.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the informations filed against defendants.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- Thruway regulation -- Thruway regulation forbidding charter buses from using service areas and restrooms and restaurants on summer weekends is discriminatory and unconstitutional; hence, informations dismissed.

A resolution and a regulation of the New York State Thruway Authority, which have the effect of closing, as to charter buses and their numerous passengers, all service areas and restrooms and restaurants and parking facilities between New York City and Albany on weekends during the period from Memorial Day through Labor Day, constitute an arbitrary abuse of administrative discretion and an unconstitutional discrimination against the members of part of a class. Therefore, informations charging that the defendants violated the regulation are dismissed by the Justice Court.

 

1952 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Syracuse v. Penny


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Onondaga County


59 Misc. 2d 818; 300 N.Y.S.2d 679; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1637



April 14, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff City of Syracuse filed a motion for a preliminary injunction pending trial in its action for a permanent injunction to restrain defendant contractor from performing any electrical work in the city on the grounds that the contractor was not licensed to do the work.


OVERVIEW: The contractor had completed several electrical jobs in the city after three times failing the examination provided for under the city's electric code. The city filed an action for a permanent injunction to restrain the contractor from performing any electrical work in the city without a license. The city then filed a motion for a preliminary injunction pending trial. The court granted the city's motion, holding that the city's establishment of a board of examiners under the electrical code was a lawful delegation of power pursuant to N.Y. Gen. City Law § 20(27)(e). Also, the city was entitled to maintain an action to compel compliance with or to restrain by injunction the violation of the licensing ordinance pursuant to N.Y. Gen. City Law § 20(22). Further, the city merely adopted the National Electrical Code and incorporated it into the city's electrical code, which it was entitled to do. Additionally, the city had the authority under its general police power to set forth requirements as to qualifications of persons permitted to engage in electrical work in the city because such work affected the public welfare, health, and safety.


OUTCOME: The court granted the city's motion for a preliminary injunction in its action for a permanent injunction to restrain the contractor from performing any electrical work in the city in the absence of obtaining a license to do the work.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Licenses -- electrician's license -- city's electric code validly and constitutionally requires electricians to be examined and licensed by board of examiners; unlicensed electrician is enjoined from practicing.

The Electric Code of the City of Syracuse validly and constitutionally provides for the examination and licensing of electricians by a Master Electrician's Board of Examiners, and that "The latest National Electrical Code, copy of which is marked Exhibit 'A' and annexed hereto, as hereinafter modified, is hereby adopted as part of the electric code of the City of Syracuse"; and the General City Law ( § 20, subd. 22; § 20, subd. 27, pars. [a] to [e]) provides that a violation of an ordinance may be enjoined by a city. The code does not unconstitutionally delegate legislative powers; and of course the city always has the power to delete from applicability any provisions of the National Electrical Code which may be found to conflict with the laws of the State of New York or with the ordinances of the City of Syracuse. Accordingly, the city is granted a preliminary injunction against the performance of any electrical work by a person who has three times failed to [***2] pass the examinations and who nevertheless persists in installing inferior or hazardous electrical wiring at various locations in the city.

 

1953 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Tamburro v. Trama


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Westchester County


59 Misc. 2d 488; 299 N.Y.S.2d 528; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1654



April 9, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed a motion, seeking an order directing the sheriff to enter defendant's home and remove furniture.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued defendant to repossess furniture under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 71. When a sheriff's deputy tried to seize the furniture, defendant refused to allow the deputy in. Plaintiff filed a motion seeking an order directing the sheriff to enter defendant's home and remove the furniture. The court held that even though there was a bona fide dispute over the ownership of the furniture, N.Y. C.P.L.R. 7103 entitled plaintiff to claim the furniture from the sheriff by executing an undertaking as required by N.Y. C.P.L.R. 7102(e). The court held that under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 7102, the sheriff was to retain custody for three days and then to deliver the furniture unless defendant filed an exception to plaintiff's surety, a notice of motion for an impounding order, or the necessary papers to reclaim the chattel under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 7102(f).


OUTCOME: The court granted plaintiff's motion.


HEADNOTES

Replevin -- pauper -- requirement that defendant post bond in order to keep her furniture pending trial ( CPLR 7102) does not unconstitutionally discriminate against pauper.

A defendant in a replevin action who wishes to retain possession of the chattels -- her furniture, in this case -- until her dispute with plaintiff as to ownership is determined by trial, must post an undertaking, as against plaintiff's undertaking and requisition to the Sheriff to seize the furniture ( CPLR 7102, subd. [f]). This statutory requirement does not invidiously and unconstitutionally discriminate against a defendant who is receiving public assistance and has no funds wherewith to furnish an undertaking. The Sheriff will be directed to enter her apartment and remove the furniture.

 

1954 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Firestone v. First Dist. Dental Soc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, New York County


59 Misc. 2d 362; 299 N.Y.S.2d 551; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1657



April 7, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, which reversed a summary judgment in favor of plaintiff dentist, the court heard the merits of the dentist's action against defendant, a district dental society. The dentist sought a judgment to declare that certain provisions of the society's code of ethics and regulations were invalid and to enjoin the society from enforcing said provisions.


OVERVIEW: The dentist was a member of the society, and, as required by the code of ethics, the dentist submitted his manuscript on dental care to the society for approval prior to his reading the manuscript for a radio broadcast. The society denied approval, finding that the article contained statements "not in good taste" and that the publication was not in the best interests of dentistry. The dentist alleged that the requirements were an improper prior restraint of his freedom of expression under the First and Fourteenth Amendments. The court agreed and found the provisions invalid. The court found that the society's activities constituted "state action" because it was clear that the State Dental Society, of which the society was a component, functioned as an agent of the State. Because no provision for judicial review was made in advance of final restraint, the system clearly offended the constitutional guarantee of freedom of expression on matters of public interest. Although it was not necessary to show economic loss, the court found that the loss of membership in the society would have had adverse economic consequences for the dentist and would deprive him of substantial rights.


OUTCOME: The court entered a judgment declaring that provisions of the society's code of ethics and regulations were invalid. The court further enjoined the society from taking disciplinary action against the dentist based upon the invalid provisions.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Physicians and surgeons -- dentists -- dental society cannot suspend or expel or discipline member for his failure to obtain its prior approval of his manuscript or radio broadcast -- this decision does not preclude society from taking disciplinary steps if member makes speech or broadcast which offends code of ethics in other respects.

Plaintiff is a licensed and practicing dentist and a member of a dental society. The society's constitution and by-laws provide for the suspension or expulsion of any member who publishes or broadcasts any manuscript or talk on dental matters to the lay public without first obtaining the approval of the society. Through its committee on ethics, the society has refused to approve plaintiff's proposed radio broadcast, on the ground that his manuscript therefor does not uphold the dignity and best interest of the profession; and the committee has threatened disciplinary action against him if he publishes or utters such a manuscript. He would suffer economic loss if suspended or expelled from the society. In view of the statutory powers of dental societies (Education Law, § 6602 et seq.), and in view of the lack of any provision for a judicial [***2] determination in advance, this constitutes State repression of freedom of speech (U. S. Const., 1st and 14th Amdts.). It is immaterial that plaintiff may not have exhausted all his nonjudicial remedies under the society's constitution and by-laws in an attempt to obtain such unconstitutionally required approval of his proposed speech. Nor did his application for membership, in which he agreed to abide by the society's code of ethics, constitute a waiver of the constitutionally guaranteed freedom of speech. Accordingly, the code of ethics is declared invalid insofar as it requires approval of a manuscript or proposed broadcast, and the society is enjoined from disciplining plaintiff for failing to obtain such advance approval. Of course, this does not preclude the society from taking disciplinary steps under its constitution and by-laws against plaintiff or any member, on a charge that a particular publication or broadcast by such member has offended the code of ethics for reasons other than his failure to obtain advance approval.

 

1955 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


De Crow v. Hotel Syracuse Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Onondaga County


59 Misc. 2d 383; 298 N.Y.S.2d 859; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1658



April 4, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] In view of the above it is academic even to discuss the plaintiff's motion for a protective order since the action by this decision is dismissed and judgment granted therefor to the defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a female visitor to a hotel, filed a motion for a protective order under N.Y. C.P.L.R. § 3103 to prevent unreasonable annoyance. Defendant hotel filed a cross-motion for summary judgment pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. § 3212 to dismiss the visitor's complaint to recover under N.Y. Civ. Rights Law § 40 for mental anguish and public embarrassment.


OVERVIEW: The visitor went to a lounge owned and operated by the hotel. She was unable obtain an intoxicating drink without an escort at the bar, although she would have been served at a table near the bar. The visitor argued that she was discriminated against on the basis of her gender. The court ruled that N.Y. Civ. Rights Law § 40 and N.Y. Civ. Rights Law § 40-c made it clear that the legislature has made it discriminatory to deny any person his civil rights because of race, creed, color or national origin. There was no mention in either statute of the word "sex". Thus, the visitor had no redress under the statutes. Further, N.Y. Civ. Rights Law § 40-e did not apply because under the facts adduced at the examination before trial, it was clear that on neither occasion did the hotel refuse to receive or entertain the visitor. Rather, it simply conditioned their reception and entertainment of her by requiring that she be escorted to the bar or be seated at a table removed therefrom.


OUTCOME: The court granted the hotel's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the visitor's complaint.


HEADNOTES

Civil rights -- women -- refusal to serve woman at hotel bar does not discriminate against her "race, creed, color or national origin" (Civil Rights Law, § 40 et seq.); action for penalties dismissed.

The refusal by a hotel to serve intoxicating liquor to an unescorted woman at its bar does not discriminate against her "race, creed, color or national origin", and the hotel's offer to serve her at a table near the bar does not mean that the hotel "refuses, without just cause or excuse, to receive and entertain any guest" (Civil Rights Law, §§ 40, 40-c, 40-d, 40-e, 41). Her action to recover the penalties provided in said sections is dismissed.

 

1956 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Fisher v. Board of Supervisors


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Ontario County


59 Misc. 2d 953; 301 N.Y.S.2d 310; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1671



March 28, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought an order from the court (New York) declaring, among other things, that the districting and apportionment of the members of defendant Ontario County Board of Supervisors was void and unconstitutional. Plaintiffs requested that the court direct permanent redistricting or reapportionment to insure compliance with the equal protection provisions of law, and for temporary relief pending the adoption of a final constitutional plan.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs claimed that the apportionment of the Board was inequitable and void. The court agreed. The court found that the facts clearly demonstrated that the apportionment of the Board violated the "one man, one vote" required by the decisions of the United States Supreme Court. The court found that a casual examination of the figures cited was sufficient to demonstrate, in view of the fact that each supervisor had one vote, that the disparities in population as between the various municipalities involved, rendered it impossible to reconcile present districting with constitutional requirements of population based representation. Accordingly, the court concluded that no triable issue of fact existed. The court held that N.Y. County Law § 150, and other applicable statutes, insofar as their application required the present apportionment of the Board, were invalid and unconstitutional. The apportionment violated and offended the equal protection clauses of U. S. Const. amend. XIV, and N. Y. Const. art. I, § 11.


OUTCOME: The court granted plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment and directed the Board to adopt and submit a temporary plan of reapportionment, pending the effectuation of a permanent plan, that would meet the constitutional standard of "one man, one vote."


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- apportionment of Board of Supervisors -- plan for weighted voting by present members of Board of Supervisors of Ontario County having been rejected by referendum, court directs said board to submit constitutional plan of reapportionment to court within 60 days.

The 21 Supervisors who constitute the Board of Supervisors of Ontario County are elected as follows: 1 from each of the 16 towns, 2 from the City of Canandaigua, and 3 from the City of Geneva. Each Supervisor represents a different number of people, ranging approximately from as few as 558 persons to as many as 6,242 persons. This inequality of representation is unconstitutional. A standing committee of the Board of Supervisors has been studying this problem for three years; and at one time the board proposed, by a local law, a scheme for proportionately weighting the voting power of each of the 21 Supervisors on the board; but that scheme was defeated by a referendum. Now the court directs the Board of Supervisors to submit to the court, within 35 days, a constitutionally valid, temporary plan of reapportionment, and, within 60 days, a permanent, constitutionally valid plan of reapportionment.

 

1957 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Oakwood Island Yacht Club, Inc. v. New Rochelle


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


59 Misc. 2d 355; 298 N.Y.S.2d 807; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1688



March 20, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Plaintiffs' motion for partial summary judgment is granted to the extent that an order may be entered herein directing the entry of judgment declaring the said ordinances to be unconstitutional and invalid, and declaring that the plaintiffs are entitled to have defendant's Bureau of Buildings entertain and consider plaintiffs' application for a building permit upon its merits.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a property owner and a prospective buyer, filed a motion for partial summary judgment in their suit in which they sought a judgment declaring that New Rochelle, N.Y., Ordinance No. 208 (ordinance), as adopted by defendant City of New Rochelle, which barred the owner from building on its property, was unconstitutional and void.


OVERVIEW: Under the existing City zoning ordinance, the owner's property was at all times zoned for use for garden type apartment houses. The owner and the buyer applied to the City's Bureau of Buildings for a permit to construct a garden type apartment house. The Bureau refused to review the building plans or to issue a building permit because the City had adopted the ordinance. The ordinance prohibited all construction work or the issuance of building permits for the property for a period of six months while the City awaited approval of their application for state funds to condemn the land for park and recreation purposes; another ordinance extended the period for another six months. The court agreed with the owner and the buyer and ruled that the ordinance was invalid because it unconstitutionally deprived the owner and the buyer of their property without due process of law. There was no authority for adopting an ordinance to prevent a property owner from building upon his property because a city in the future may seek to obtain it by condemnation. The City's defense that the property did not have the required street access had no bearing on the issue of the ordinance's constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court granted the owner's motion for partial summary judgment and entered an order directing the entry of judgment declaring the City's ordinance to be unconstitutional and invalid and declaring that the owner was entitled to have the City's Bureau of Buildings entertain and consider the owner's application for a building permit upon its merits.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- ordinance barring construction -- ordinance of city which prevents owners of land for six-month period from constructing permitted type of building while city seeks funds to condemn land is unconstitutional and invalid.

An ordinance which prevents owners of land from obtaining a permit for constructing a building on their land, a permitted use, for a six-month period while the city applied for funds to condemn such land for park and recreation purposes unconstitutionally deprives plaintiffs of their property without due process of law and is invalid, and plaintiffs are entitled to have defendant's Bureau of Buildings entertain and consider plaintiffs' application for a building permit.

 

1958 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Zientara v. Zientara


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


59 Misc. 2d 344; 299 N.Y.S.2d 253; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1692



March 19, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For all of the reasons hereinabove stated, I hold that the present action cannot be maintained and the complaint is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife filed an action for an absolute divorce against defendant husband pursuant to N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 170(5).


OVERVIEW: The wife based her divorce action on the ground that the parties had lived apart for a period of two years under a decree of separation. The wife was the innocent party in the prior separation action, which had occurred prior to the original enactment of § 170(5) in 1966. Except for an opposition to a demand for alimony and counsel fees, the husband had not resisted the action. The court held that § 170(5) could not be applied retroactively because under the application of general rules of statutory construction, the legislature that enacted the provision did not intend retroactive application of § 170(5).


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the wife's action.


HEADNOTES

Husband and wife -- divorce -- subdivision (5) of section 170 of Domestic Relations Law, enacted in 1966, providing as ground for divorce that parties lived apart for two years under decree of separation, cannot be retroactively applied and complaint for divorce based on separation decree entered in 1959 is dismissed.

Subdivision (5) of section 170 of the Domestic Relations Law, enacted in 1966 to take effect on September 1, 1967, which specifies, as a ground for divorce, that the parties had been living apart for a period of two years under a decree of separation, cannot be retroactively applied to a decree of separation entered on November 27, 1959. The statute is not remedial and so cannot be applied retroactively. The complaint herein seeking a divorce is dismissed.

 

1959 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Greenburgh v. Board of Supervisors


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


59 Misc. 2d 152; 298 N.Y.S.2d 615; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1701



March 13, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs and intervenors, two towns and others, filed an application for further action in the reapportionment of a county legislative body in an action filed against respondents, a county board of supervisors, other towns in the county, and the Secretary of State of the State of New York.


OVERVIEW: The court issued an interim decision that permitted consideration by the county board of proposed laws to reapportion the board into 17, single-member districts. The board rejected both proposed laws. The matter came before the court for a final determination. A nonpartisan organization adopted the proposed law as its plan for reapportionment for consideration by the court. The court also had two other reapportionment plans that were before it in its interim decision. One plan was based on the state assembly district boundaries within the county. The second plan used a combination of one-member, two-member, and three-member districts. The court held that: (1) the assembly district plan was rejected because no party advocated its adoption and because it fragmented municipalities within the county to a greater extent than the other proposals; (2) the multiple member district plan was rejected because some of the districts were not compact or contiguous; and (3) the single member district plan was adopted because it was more desirable than the multiple-member district plan in the variance of populations within the districts and the use of existing municipal boundaries.


OUTCOME: The court adopted a reapportionment plan for the county legislative body. The court provided procedures for the implementation of the plan and the election of the county legislative body.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- apportionment of Board of Supervisors -- successive proposals of Westchester County Board of Supervisors for reapportionment of its members' representation of voters having been either disapproved by court or rejected by referenda, court now approves plan of league of voters for division of county into 17 districts each of which shall elect one County Legislator.

The Westchester County Board of Supervisors having proposed one plan after another to reapportion constitutionally its members' presently unequal representation of the people, and the court having adjudged that some of the plans failed to meet the constitutional requirement of one person-one vote, and the people having rejected the other plans one after another by successive referenda, the court has now taken further testimony and has approved, with modifications, a proposal by the League of Women Voters for the division of the county into 17 districts which are nearly equal in population and which, insofar as practicable, do not unnecessarily split municipalities. In each of these 17 districts the voters shall elect one County Legislator in 1969, to take office on January 1, 1970 and to serve [***2] for two years. This new County Board shall replace the existing Board of Supervisors (County Law, § 150-a). The qualifications of candidates shall be as provided in the Public Officers Law ( § 3). The salaries of such County Legislators shall be as fixed by the Westchester County Administrative Code (art. III, § 15), unless altered by appropriate legislation. They shall be county officers, and no provision of any city charter concerning city supervisors shall apply to them. Vacancies in the office of County Legislator shall be filled by such County Board until the next general election. All provisions of the Westchester County Charter and the Westchester County Administrative Code which now apply to the Board of Supervisors shall apply to this County Board and its members, except for any provisions thereof which may be inconsistent with this decision of the court. The court will retain jurisdiction for all purposes.

 

1960 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ricci


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Oneida County


59 Misc. 2d 259; 298 N.Y.S.2d 637; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1711



March 11, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Denied. ( People v. Perrell, 47 Misc 2d 1024, 1025.)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who had been indicted on drug charges, sought a bill of particulars, a list of witnesses, discovery and inspection, production of the statements of witnesses; sought to dismiss the indictment on the ground that certain statutes were unconstitutional; and sought to inspect the grand jury minutes and dismiss the indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with acting together and in concert with others on three counts involving dangerous drugs. The court held that the N.Y. Penal Law §§ 220.30 and 220.10 were not unconstitutional. The court denied the motion to dismiss the indictment. Defendant was not entitled to relief on his motion to inspect the grand jury minutes because there was sufficient legal evidence before the grand jury to warrant the presentment. Defendant was not entitled to a list of the witnesses that the prosecution intended to use at the trial. He was not entitled to the original notes of the arresting officers and any and all statements made by him.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motions.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- dangerous drugs -- statutes making possession or sale of dangerous drug criminal, constitutional -- although drugs were sold to undercover police agents, defense of entrapment is not ground for inspection of Grand Jury minutes -- bill of particulars is granted of approximate times and places of alleged possessions and sales; all other items are denied -- list of People's witnesses denied -- defendant is not entitled in advance to statements of witnesses or to notes made by arresting officers -- District Attorney shall state whether he intends to use any admission or confession made by defendant; if so, defendant may have pretrial hearing as to voluntariness -- defendant is not entitled to examine and copy records and chemical reports concerning drug.

1. Defendant has been properly indicted for criminally possessing and selling, in the third degree, a hallucinogenic drug, namely, lysergic acid diethylamide (Penal Law, §§ 220.00, 220.10, 220.30). The statutes are constitutional.

2. Concededly, the sales were made to undercover police agents; however, entrapment is an affirmative defense and hence is [***2] not a ground for asking for an inspection of the Grand Jury minutes. Nor is the buyer an accomplice of the seller; that is, his testimony need not be corroborated. In any event, the court has read the Grand Jury minutes and finds that there was sufficient legal evidence to sustain the indictment.

3. On defendant's motion for a bill of particulars, the court in its discretion will grant the following item only: the approximate times of day or night when, and the approximate places where, the alleged criminal possessions and sales occurred. Other items, such as the chemical composition and amounts and weights of the drugs, are not essential to a third degree criminal possession or sale; nor is the consideration for the alleged sale essential, since the statute defines a sale as including a giving or disposing of to another. And, of course, the defendant is not entitled to evidentiary items, such as how he actually possessed and sold the drugs.

4. Defendant is not entitled to a list of the witnesses who will be used by the prosecution at the trial.

5. Defendant is not entitled, in advance of trial, to any statements made by witnesses and to the notes made by the arresting officers.

 [***3] 6. The District Attorney is directed to disclose whether he intends to rely upon any admission or confession which defendant made while in custody; and if so, the defendant will be entitled to a pretrial hearing as to the voluntariness of the admission or confession.

7. The court denies defendant's motion for an order to examine, copy, or make photographic or photostatic copies of any and all charts, records and chemical reports concerning the drug allegedly possessed and sold by defendant.

 

1961 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Shapiro v. Shapiro


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


59 Misc. 2d 412; 298 N.Y.S.2d 785; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1721



March 7, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The court having concluded that subdivision (5) of section 170 cannot be retrospectively applied in an action brought by the party adjudged guilty in a decree of separation entered prior to the effective date of said statutory provision, defendant's motion is granted and the complaint herein is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant wife moved to dismiss the action for divorce brought by plaintiff husband pursuant to N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 170(5).


OVERVIEW: A judgment of separation on which the action was based was granted to the wife in another county in 1964. The husband was adjudged guilty of cruel and inhuman treatment and nonsupport. That judgment antedated the adoption of a new divorce law. The wife sought dismissal of the husband's divorce action on the ground that § 170(5) could not have been retroactively applied to an action brought by a party that was guilty in a decree of judgment or separation prior to September 1, 1966. The court held that: (1) absent consent of both parties pursuant to § 170(6), the option to initiate proceedings that culminated in divorce laid exclusively with the innocent spouse; and (2) the option in § 170(5) could have been retroactively applied to a decree of separation in cases brought prior to its adoption by innocent spouses, but the option was to be applied prospectively only in actions that were instituted by a guilty spouse because that construction was wholly consonant with well-settled rules of statutory construction.


OUTCOME: The court granted the wife's motion and dismissed the husband's complaint.


HEADNOTES

Husband and wife -- divorce -- spouse against whom judgment of separation was rendered in 1964 cannot maintain suit for divorce on ground that he and she have thus lived apart for two years since 1966 and he has performed all terms of said judgment (Domestic Relations Law, § 170, subd. [5]); said subdivision was not meant to benefit guilty party retroactively.

The Domestic Relations Law ( § 170, subd. [5]; L. 1966, ch. 254, § 15) now provides that a divorce action may be maintained on the ground that, since September 1, 1966, the parties have lived apart for two years since the granting of a judgment of separation and the party now seeking the divorce has substantially performed all the terms of the judgment of separation. This subdivision was not intended to apply retroactively to the benefit of the guilty spouse against whom a judgment of separation on the ground [***2] of cruelty and nonsupport was rendered in 1964. His action for a divorce is dismissed.

 

1962 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lake Ronkonkoma Theater Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


District Court of New York, First District, Suffolk County


59 Misc. 2d 438; 299 N.Y.S.2d 545; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1723



March 6, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Defendants' motion to suppress is therefore denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a theater corporation and an individual, were charged by a criminal information with violating N.Y. Penal Law § 235.05(2) by acting in concert to present a motion picture that was allegedly obscene. Defendants brought a motion to suppress the use of the film against defendants.


OVERVIEW: The officers paid admission to the theater and viewed the film. They then arrested defendants and seized the rolls of film. Defendants alleged that the seizure was unconstitutional because there was no judicial inquiry and prior adversary hearing. After viewing the film and hearing testimony of the officers, the court found that the officers had "absolute" probable cause to arrest and that the search and seizure incidental to the arrest were permissible. The court further found that the New York obscenity statutes, N.Y. Penal Law § 235.00 et seq., incorporated the wording of prior decisions of the United States Supreme Court in order to formulate proper guidelines and standards for police officers. Thus, the laws were was clear and unambiguous, and they needed no prior judicial determination as to what was obscene.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motion to suppress.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- obscenity -- court finds that police, after viewing motion picture performance twice, had probable cause to arrest defendants without warrant and seize film; motion to suppress such seized evidence denied.

At a regular paid performance in defendants' motion picture theatre, the police twice viewed a motion picture which they had probable cause to believe to be obscene (Penal Law, § 235.00; § 235.05, subd. 2), and thereupon, without any warrant, they properly arrested the defendants (Code Crim. Pro., § 177, subd. 1) and, as an incident of this proper arrest, they properly seized the rolls of film. The court, after viewing the film and hearing counsel, denies defendants' motion to suppress the seized evidence.

 

1963 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Abelson v. Abelson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


59 Misc. 2d 172; 298 N.Y.S.2d 381; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1736



February 26, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The defendant's motion for an allowance of counsel fees is granted to the extent of awarding her an interim allowance of $ 1,000 to be paid by the plaintiff one half within 30 days after service of a copy of the order entered hereon with notice of entry, and the balance within 90 days thereafter, with leave to apply for a further allowance to the trial court, or to special term should developments in this action warrant such additional allowance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband brought an action for an absolute divorce upon the ground that he and defendant wife had lived apart pursuant to a judgment of separation. The husband filed a motion to dismiss five of the six affirmative defenses pleaded by the wife. The wife filed a motion for an allowance of counsel fees.


OVERVIEW: The court granted dismissal of the three proffered defenses that related to the husband's alleged adultery because fault grounds were irrelevant to maintain an action for divorce based on N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 170(5). The dismissal was also based on the court's finding that there were no issues to try with respect to those defenses because the separation judgment contained no directions that involved them. The court denied the husband's motion to dismiss the defense that invoked the doctrine of clean hands because it was for the trial court determine whether the cumulative effect of the husband's conduct warranted the application of the equitable doctrine. The court also denied dismissal of the defense that claimed that the wife would be deprived of constitutionally protected rights if § 170(5) was given a retroactive application because neither the legislative intent nor the statutory language required such application. The court granted the wife's motion for counsel fees.


OUTCOME: The court granted the husband's motion to dismiss three of the affirmative defenses pleaded by the wife, but denied the motion as to the other challenged defenses. The court granted the wife's motion for an allowance of counsel fees to the extent of awarding her an interim allowance, with leave to apply for a further allowance.


HEADNOTES

Husband and wife -- divorce -- divorce may now be had even by party against whom judgment of separation was rendered, provided only that they have since lived apart for two years and he has performed all terms of judgment of separation ( Domestic Relations Law, § 170, subd. [5]) -- however, under asserted defense that plaintiff comes into court with unclean hands, trial court may determine, upon all evidence, whether husband's conduct in obtaining void Mexican divorce and marrying another woman in another State now bars him from aid of court of equity -- this judgment of separation was obtained long before enactment of divorce reform law; court suggests that trial court may grant this divorce but may expressly leave wife's property  [***2] rights unimpaired -- triable defense, that husband has not paid alimony as directed by separation judgment -- defendant wife is granted interim allowance of $ 1,000 for counsel fee.

1. The Domestic Relations Law ( § 170, subd. [5], as added by L. 1966, ch. 254, and as amd. by L. 1968, ch. 700) now provides that either party may have a divorce on the grounds that they have lived apart for two years pursuant to a judgment of separation and that the one now seeking the divorce has substantially performed all the terms of the judgment of separation. Under this subdivision (5) it is immaterial that the judgment of separation was rendered against the one who now seeks the divorce.

2. Nor is it a defense to such a divorce action that, ever since the separation judgment was rendered in 1961, the husband -- who is the one now seeking a divorce -- has been living in open adultery with another woman. Nor is it a defense that he procured a void Mexican divorce in 1962 and then married said other woman in Connecticut, and that his divorced wife (the defendant in this divorce action) obtained a judgment in 1963 declaring said Mexican divorce to be void.

3. However, it is an equitable defense [***3] to any divorce action that the plaintiff comes into court with unclean hands; and, for this purpose, the trial court may hear all the evidence as to this plaintiff's above-alleged conduct and may determine, upon all the evidence, whether plaintiff's conduct has been such as to bar him from seeking the aid of a court of equity.

4. This divorce action was commenced by the husband on September 12, 1968 on the basis of a separation judgment which the wife won in 1961. The court suggests that the questions as to whether subdivision (5) of section 170 of the Domestic Relations Law (as added by L. 1966, ch. 254, and as amd. by L. 1968, ch. 700) is intended to apply retroactively to the many separation judgments won by wives prior to September 1, 1967, and as to whether said subdivision (5) can constitutionally be thus applied retroactively, do not necessarily arise, since the trial court may grant a divorce decree to such a husband but may expressly leave unimpaired the wife's property rights, such as her right to elect to take against the husband's testamentary dispositions.

5. Of course, it is a triable defense to this divorce action that the husband has not paid alimony as directed [***4] by the judgment of separation.

6. Defendant wife is granted an interim allowance of $ 1,000 for counsel fee.

 

1964 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Berback v. Mangum


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Monroe County


59 Misc. 2d 41; 297 N.Y.S.2d 853; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1741



February 25, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petitioners are granted the relief asked for in toto, encompassing (1) lack of jurisdiction; (2) annulling the determination after investigation; (3) dismissing the complaint; and (4) injunction as to holding any hearing or taking any further steps in this proceeding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner home owners brought an application to annul and vacate a determination made by respondent, the New York State Division of Human Rights, which denied the owners' claim of exemption to the New York Human Rights Law, pursuant to N.Y. Exec. Law § 296(5)(a), finding that the exemption violated the U.S. and New York Constitutions. The owners also requested the dismissal of a housing discrimination complaint and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The owners claimed that they met the exemption set forth in § 296(5)(a) because their home was a two-family home and they occupied one apartment of the home. A complainant alleged that the owners refused to rent to her because of her race and color. The Division contended that the exemption violated the equal protection clauses of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § I and of the N.Y. Const. art. I, § 11. Further, the Division claimed that 42 U.S.C.S. § 1982 was enacted pursuant to the authority of U.S. Const. amend. XIII, § 2. The court found that the U.S. Fair Housing Law of 1968, 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 3601-3619, authorized similar exemptions to that of N.Y. Exec. Law § 296(5)(a). The court found careful federal and state legislative intent to warrant holding § 296(5)(a) constitutional. The exemption in the respective statutes included the legal assumption that a man's house was regarded as his castle. Because § 296(5)(a) was found to be constitutional, the owners were entitled to their requested relief.


OUTCOME: The court granted the relief requested by the owners, vacating a determination made by the Division, dismissing the discrimination complaint, and enjoining any hearing or the taking of any further steps in the action against the owners.


HEADNOTES

Civil rights -- housing -- owners of two-family dwelling who reside in one of its two apartments lawfully refused to rent other apartment to person who thereupon complained to State Division of Human Rights that she was refused because of her race and color; said division is restrained from taking any further steps (Executive Law, § 296, subd. 5, par. [a]).

In a two-family dwelling in which the owner resides, an apartment or other housing accommodation is validly and constitutionally exempted (by the unnumbered sentence at the end of Executive Law, § 296, subd. 5, par. [a]) from the open-renting requirements of said paragraph. Accordingly, the owners of such a two-family dwelling lawfully refused to rent the vacant apartment to a person who thereupon complained to the New York State Division of Human Rights that she had been refused because of her race and color. The owners of the dwelling [***2] are granted an injunction annulling the division's initial determination of the complaint, and restraining the division from holding a hearing or taking any further steps in the proceeding against said owners. (Cf. U. S. Const., 14th Amdt.; N. Y. Const., art. I, § 11; U. S. Code, tit. 42, § 1982.)

 

1965 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Gleason v. Gleason


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


59 Misc. 2d 96; 298 N.Y.S.2d 375; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1756



February 19, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] That branch of plaintiff's cross motion which seeks to strike paragraph "1" of defendant's answer is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a wife, filed a motion to dismiss the complaint for divorce of plaintiff, a husband, on the grounds of her affirmative defenses that the parties were living apart pursuant to a separation agreement and not pursuant to a separation decree in a prior proceeding which barred the divorce action pursuant to the 1968 amendment to N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 170(6), and that N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 170(5) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The husband filed a cross-motion to strike the wife's defenses as insufficient in law and to strike a paragraph of the wife's answer where she denied the husband's allegation that he had fully complied with the terms of the separation decree. The husband instituted the action pursuant to § 170(5) on the ground that the parties had been separated pursuant to a decree of separation for more than two years prior to the commencement of the action. The wife had commenced the earlier separation action, and a decree was granted to the wife on the ground of abandonment immediately after the parties had entered into the separation agreement, which was incorporated into that decree. The court held that: (1) the present martial status of the parties was determined by the decree rather than the agreement because the agreement provided by its terms that it was of no effect until the decree was entered; (2) there was no showing that § 170 was patently unconstitutional; and (3) the husband could maintain his action because § 170(5) had been held constitutionally valid in its retroactive application to "old" decrees of separation entered before its enactment.


OUTCOME: The court denied the wife's motion to dismiss the husband's complaint and granted the husband's motion to strike the wife's affirmative defenses. The court denied the husband's motion to strike a paragraph of the wife's answer that concerned the husband's allegation of his compliance with the separation decree.


HEADNOTES

Husband and wife -- divorce -- in action for divorce on ground that parties are separated pursuant to 1954 decree of separation, defense that parties live apart under separation agreement is insufficient -- Domestic Relations Law ( § 170, subd. [5]) insofar as it applies retroactively to "old" separation decrees is constitutional -- no constitutional prohibition against State permitting divorce on grounds unrelated to fault -- court at nisi prius should not declare law unconstitutional unless unconstitutionality is patent -- issue as to whether plaintiff complied with decree of separation is not decided on pleadings.

1. In an action for divorce based on subdivision (5) of section 170 of Domestic Relations Law on the ground that the parties had been separated, pursuant to a decree of separation dated in 1954, for more than two years prior to the commencement of this action, a defense that the parties are living apart pursuant to an agreement of separation rather than a court decree is insufficient. The agreement specifically provides that it was to have no effect [***2] until entry of the decree. The decree governs their status.

2. Subdivision (5) of section 170 is constitutionally valid in its retroactive application to "old" decrees, and this action may be maintained. The claim that the new section unconstitutionally interferes with the wife's "vested" rights arising out of the marital res is rejected. There is no vested right to inherit and there is no vested right that a spouse has arising either out of contract or out of the marital status to remain married to his or her partner. No decree or agreement may be construed as to bar a party from seeking a divorce where the grounds exist and the court has jurisdiction. Granting a divorce would not diminish plaintiff's obligations under the agreement. In addition the court may make such additional provisions for the wife's support as would be fair under the circumstances.

3. There is no constitutional prohibition to a State permitting a divorce on grounds unrelated to fault. That plaintiff was the "guilty" party in the action for separation does not prevent him from maintaining this action.

4. Moreover, a court at nisi prius should not declare an act of the Legislature invalid unless [***3] its unconstitutionality is patent, and there is no such showing here.

5. Since full compliance with the terms of the separation decree by plaintiff is one of the jurisdictional requisites to maintaining the action, the issue as to whether plaintiff has fully performed pursuant to the terms of the decree, raised by defendant in her answer, will not be disposed of on the pleadings.

 

1966 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Marthann Realty Co. v. Meade


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


59 Misc. 2d 274; 298 N.Y.S.2d 368; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1771



February 14, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, town and park district, filed a motion to dismiss petitioner citizens' N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 challenge to a condemnation map for parking facilities.


OVERVIEW: The town board adopted a resolution that approved a condemnation map proposed by the park district for parking facilities near the Manhasset Station of the Long Island Rail Road. The citizens separately brought article 78 proceedings to annul the resolution, to enjoin further steps in the condemnation, to have declared unconstitutional a section of an act, and to attack the taking itself as being without public purpose, arbitrary, capricious and in bad faith. The town and the park district did not answer the petition; instead, they filed a motion to dismiss, contending that it was inappropriate to review a legislative enactment by an article 78 proceeding. The court denied the motion to dismiss and directed respondents to file answers in both proceedings. The town board's approval was its final action in the matter. As a matter of public policy, it was unwise to postpone all questions until the park district had completed its condemnation proceeding. Substantial public expense and effort were involved in a condemnation projection and substantial prejudice hung over threatened property owners until a proceeding was complete.


OUTCOME: The court denied respondents' motion to dismiss the citizens' challenge to a condemnation proceeding and directed respondents to file answers.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- Park District -- article 78 proceedings may be brought to review authorization by Town Board to Park District to institute condemnation proceeding, and to review constitutionality of statute insofar as town's tax credit may be pledged for payment of bonds of Park District.

A Town Board called a public hearing on a proposal by a Park District of the town to acquire land and construct improvements thereon; and, after the public hearing, the Town Board adopted the Park District's proposed condemnation map for parking facilities near a railroad station, and delegated all further proceedings to the Park District. These resolutions and the record do not clearly indicate whether the parking facilities will be for the use of the Park District residents only, and whether the tax assessments therefor will be levied on the Park District residents only; and there are conflicting contentions as to the reasonableness of the estimated costs of acquisition and improvement and as to whether this parking facility will be economically self-sufficient. Accordingly, several property owners properly bring these article 78 proceedings ( CPLR 7803, subds. 2, 3) to restrain [***2] any further steps, on the ground that the proposed condemnation is arbitrary and has no public purpose and is in bad faith, and to declare unconstitutional section 319.9 of the Nassau County Civil Divisions Act (L. 1939, ch. 273, as amd.) insofar as it permits the taxing credit of the whole town to be pledged for payment of bonds of a Park District for an improvement which is to be used by Park District residents only. The validity of the delegation of authority by the Town Board ( Town Law, § 216; Nassau County Civil Divisions Act, § 319.6) is in issue, hence the question of whether the action of the Park District is legislative is moot in this context. It would be prejudicial and unwise to postpone any judicial review until the condemnation is completed. Therefore, the motions to dismiss these article 78 proceedings are denied.

 

1967 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Peru v. State


Claim No. 47204


Court of Claims of New York


59 Misc. 2d 49; 297 N.Y.S.2d 779; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1784



February 7, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The claim is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant town filed an action seeking to recover for property appropriated by defendant, the State of New York, pursuant to the New York Conservation Law.


OVERVIEW: The State acquired the property, containing a roadway and a dock for access to Lake Champlain, under the New York Park and Recreation Land Acquisition Bond Act. The town filed a complaint alleging that it was the owner of the property and seeking damages for its appropriation. Based on deeds of owners whose property abutted the relocated town road, the minutes of the town meetings, the public use of the area as a road and dock, and the town's maintenance and repair of the road and dock, the court found that the town established its title to the property. The court found that the State made exactly the same use of the road and dock area as was made by the town. The court held that N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 3 applied only to the property of a municipal corporation held in a public or governmental capacity. Because the property was a public roadway and the dock was built, at least partially on state land, the property was held by the town in its governmental capacity. The town was not legally entitled to receive compensation under § 3 because the property was held in a governmental capacity and was not put to a substantially different use from that use made prior to the appropriation.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the town's claim.


HEADNOTES

Eminent domain -- property of municipal corporation -- town is not entitled to compensation for town road and town dock which were appropriated for same uses as theretofore (General Municipal Law, § 3).

A town is not entitled to compensation for the State's appropriation of a dock on Lake Champlain and of a road leading to the dock, both of which were owned by the town in its governmental capacity, since the appropriation was made under the Conservation Law for substantially the same public uses as before the appropriation (General Municipal Law, § 3).

 

1968 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Rye, New York, Non-Partisan Civic Asso. v. Metropolitan Transp. Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


58 Misc. 2d 932; 297 N.Y.S.2d 388; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1798



February 3, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Defendants' motion to dismiss is denied. Plaintiffs' cross motion is granted as to the second cause of action and denied, but without prejudice, as to the first cause of action. The intervenor's cross motion for summary judgment is granted as to the second cause of action pleaded in its complaint and is denied, but without prejudice, as to the remaining causes of action pleaded by it.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Metropolitan Transportation Authority (MTA), the Chairman of the MTA, and the Commissioner of the Department of Transportation, filed a motion for summary judgment in the action of plaintiffs, a city, villages, and others, seeking a declaration that 1967 N.Y. Laws 717, § 92 was unconstitutional. Plaintiffs and intervenor town file cross-motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Section 92 was enacted as part of a general law. It authorized the MTA, upon approval of the State Superintendent of Public Works, to design, construct , maintain, operate, improve, and reconstruct a bridge crossing Long Island Sound. Plaintiffs filed a complaint alleging that § 92 was unconstitutional because it violated N.Y. Const. art. X, § 5 and art. III, § 15. The court rejected defendants' argument that because the MTA was created by a special act of the legislature, the subsequent amendment and enlargement of its powers so as to include the construction of bridges, could validly be accomplished legislatively without a further special act of the legislature. The declarations and findings found in 1965 N.Y. Laws 324, which created the MTA, indicated that the legislature did not contemplate that the MTA would be authorized to construct highways or bridges for mass transportation of persons driving their own cars or other vehicles. The expansion of the MTA's powers and purposes to include improvement of mass transportation was of such a substantial nature as to require a special act of the legislature. Therefore, 1967 N.Y. Laws 717, § 92 violated N.Y. Const. art. X, § 5.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motion to dismiss. The court granted plaintiffs' cross motion as to the second cause of action and denied, without prejudice, the motion as to the first cause of action. The court granted the town's cross motion for summary judgment as to the second cause of action pleaded in its complaint and denied, without prejudice, the motion as to the remaining causes of action pleaded by it.


HEADNOTES

Statutes -- general or special act -- powers of Metropolitan Transportation Authority, created by special act of Legislature, could not constitutionally be enlarged by general act, because of section 5 of article X of New York Constitution, to include design and construction of bridge across Long Island Sound for vehicular traffic; general act is void -- intervenor town may not raise issue not raised by plaintiffs.

1. The Metropolitan Transportation Authority was created by special act of the Legislature (L. 1965, ch. 324) for the purpose of insuring the continuation of essential commuter services. Chapter 717 of the Laws of 1967 which dealt with many subjects other than MTA, and which is not a special act of the Legislature, authorized the MTA, in section 92 thereof, to design, construct [***2] and operate a highway bridge crossing Long Island Sound. Section 92 is unconstitutional under section 5 of article X of the New York Constitution which provides that "No public corporation * * * possessing both the power to contract indebtedness and the power to collect rentals, charges, rates or fees * * * shall hereafter be created except by special act of the legislature". Such provision does not permit the Legislature, after an authority has been created by a special act, to alter its powers and purposes by a general act. It was never contemplated in the original creation of MTA that it would be given authority to regulate mass transportation by private automobile and to build highways and bridges. Authorizing it to do so must be accomplished by a special act of the Legislature.

2. An intervenor town may not attack the validity of section 93 of chapter 717, an issue not raised by plaintiffs. Such issue is not properly before the court.

 

1969 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Adelman v. Adelman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


58 Misc. 2d 803; 296 N.Y.S.2d 999; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1802



January 31, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant wife brought a motion to dismiss plaintiff husband's action for divorce, which he filed pursuant to N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 170(5) on the grounds that they had lived apart pursuant to a separation decree for at least two years after the granting of the separation decree and that the husband had substantially complied with the terms of the decree.


OVERVIEW: The husband brought an action for divorce against the wife pursuant to § 170(5). The couple had been separated pursuant to a separation decree, which was entered over two years prior to the divorce action being brought by the husband. Section 170(5) was not in effect at the time of the separation decree but was in effect before the divorce action was brought. The wife brought a motion to dismiss the action, contending that retroactive application of § 170(5) deprived her of certain property rights and was thus unconstitutional, and that the legislature did not intend retroactive application of the statute. The court dismissed the wife's motion, ruling that the wife's property rights were not violated because her right to inherit from her husband was merely contingent and would only be a vested right if her husband were dead. In addition, the evidence showed that the legislature intended the statute to be retroactive because it allowed persons who were separated to be extricated from a perpetual state of marital limbo by granting a divorce based upon a prior separation decree.


OUTCOME: The court denied the wife's motion to dismiss the husband's action for divorce.


HEADNOTES

Husband and wife -- divorce -- wife obtained judgment of separation prior to September, 1, 1966, and husband has complied with its terms, and two years have elapsed, hence he may maintain suit for divorce -- Domestic Relations Law ( § 170, subd. [5]) is constitutionally retroactive.

A wife obtained a judgment of separation in July, 1966, and the husband allegedly has complied with its terms, and two years have elapsed, and therefore he may institute an action against her for divorce (Domestic Relations Law, § 170, subd. [5], as amd. by L. 1968, ch. 700). Said subdivision (5), unlike subdivision (6), now applies to judgments of separation which were entered even prior to September 1, 1966, and even though such judgment of separation was rendered against the party who thereafter sues for divorce. The retroactive application of the cited subdivision does not unconstitutionally impair the obligation of contract, or deprive the wife of any vested rights of inheritance or social security benefits, or deny to her the equal protection of the laws. Her motion to dismiss the divorce complaint is denied.

 

1970 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Board of Education v. Allen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


58 Misc. 2d 762; 296 N.Y.S.2d 890; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1805



January 30, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly and for the reasons herein stated, the petition must be, and hereby is dismissed. The stay heretofore granted is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city board of education filed a petition for an order to show cause against respondent, the state commissioner of education, in which intervenors, a minor student through his father, intervened. The board argued that an order of the commissioner was a direction for the cross-bussing of elementary school students that was arbitrary and unconstitutional and that the commissioner did not have the power to promulgate the order.


OVERVIEW: A city was bisected by railroad tracks. The population on the north side of the city was predominantly white, and on the south side, it was predominantly nonwhite. The commissioner promulgated an order aimed at full integration of the city's public schools. The order required that elementary school students be bussed out of their neighborhoods to go to school. The board filed an action against the commissioner, and the student intervened. The court issued a stay of the commissioner's order, but it then dismissed the petition and vacated the stay, holding that the commissioner's action was not purely arbitrary. Accordingly, under N.Y. Educ. Law § 310, the order had to be upheld. The commissioner had the power to substitute his judgment for that of the board even if the action of the board was not arbitrary because the decision of the commissioner in regard to racial balance was conclusive. The commissioner's determination had an educational purpose, so there was no constitutional impairment to his order for cross-bussing even though the order placed a serious financial burden on the city's taxpayers.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the board's petition, and it vacated the stay of the commissioner's order.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- racial imbalance -- courts cannot review decision of State Commissioner of Education requiring school board to integrate all elementary schools.

On one side of the railroad tracks, the population of a certain city is predominantly white, and on the other side it is predominantly nonwhite. The State Commissioner of Education has determined that the children of all racial and ethnic strains in the community must be given a comingled equality of educational opportunity at the grade school level, and he has therefore finally determined an appeal before him by directing the city's board of education to assign all pupils in grades one through three to the elementary schools in one half of the district, and all pupils in grades four through six to the elementary schools in the other half of the district; and, as part of his decision, he has indicated several means by which the district may be able to meet its expenses of cross-bussing and its related financial problems. Directives of the Commissioner may be enforced by, among other [***2] measures, withholding funds and removing school board members (Education Law, §§ 306, 1706). The Commissioner's directive in this case is an educational one and hence the courts cannot review it (Education Law, § 310). Accordingly, this judicial review petition ( CPLR, art. 78) is dismissed.

 

1971 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Oriental Boulevard Co. v. Heller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County
