58 Misc. 2d 920; 297 N.Y.S.2d 431; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1813



January 27, 1969 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, property owners and a real estate board, filed an action against defendants, the Commissioner of the Department of Air Pollution Control of the City of New York and others, seeking a judgment that would declare New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code ch. 41 (1966), as amended in 1968, known as Local Law No. 14, to be unconstitutional and to enjoin its enforcement.


OVERVIEW: The property owners and real estate board challenged the requirements of Local Law No. 14 for upgrading of incinerators and oil burners in multiple dwelling buildings. They sought a judgment declaring the law unconstitutional and enjoining its enforcement. The court granted the Commissioner's motion to dismiss the action as to the real estate board on the ground that there was no justiciable controversy between the real estate board and the Commissioner. The court held that the law was reasonably related to the legislative interest of protecting the public welfare. The property owners failed to show that the classification, as to dates of compliance with the law, was discriminatory or a denial of their equal protection rights. The law did not violate due process notice and opportunity requirements and did not deprive the property owners of any vested right. The court enjoined enforcement of the law pending a determination of the constitutionality of the provisions of the law that prescribed the dates for compliance and the penalties and punishment for violations of the law, which were triable issues. The court declared that the law was constitutional in all other respects.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the real estate board's complaint and granted an injunction pendente lite enjoining enforcement of the challenged law.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- reduction of air pollutants -- action challenging constitutional validity of law providing for reduction of air pollutants applies only to amended local law of 1968 not original enactment of 1966 -- no justiciable controversy exists as to plaintiff Real Estate Board, membership corporation, and its complaint is dismissed -- amended law is constitutional -- triable issue presented as to time-for-compliance requirements of law and as to penalties -- plaintiffs are granted injunction pendente lite -- defendants are granted summary judgment declaring law constitutional except as to provisions requiring trial.

1. Local Law No. 14 of the Laws of 1966 of the City of New York as amended by Local Law No. 14 of the Laws of 1968 deals with the reduction of air pollutants and provides for the upgrading of incinerators in multiple dwellings. In this action the challenge posed with respect to the constitutionality of said local law as originally enacted in 1966 is academic since a justiciable controversy is presented only as to the amended local law.

2. Plaintiff Real Estate Board, a membership corporation, cannot challenge the constitutionality of said local law [***2] since its rights are not injuriously affected thereby. No justiciable controversy exists between it and defendants. Its complaint is dismissed.

3. The amended local law is constitutional.

4. A triable issue is presented as to the argument that it would require more than the time prescribed in the law for property owners to comply with the requirements as to upgrading of equipment. Were that so, the law would be unconstitutionally oppressive.

5. The constitutional validity of the provisions imposing penalties and other punishment on violators of the law cannot be adequately assayed without a consideration of the reasonableness of the prescribed time limitations for compliance with the law. This is an issue which must also be tried.

6. Plaintiffs are granted an injunction pendente lite enjoining enforcement of the law.

7. Defendants are granted summary judgment declaring the law constitutional as to all provisions except those which prescribe the dates for effecting compliance with the law and those which prescribe penalties and punishment for violations of the law.

 

1972 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Bergerman v. Lindsay


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


58 Misc. 2d 1013; 297 N.Y.S.2d 421; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1829



January 21, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, plaintiff's application for injunctive relief is denied and summary judgment is granted in favor of defendants dismissing the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter was before the court on the motions of plaintiff, the chairman of a citizen's group, for summary judgment and judgment on the pleadings in his action under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3212 seeking to restrain defendants, the mayor and the members of the Board of Estimate of the City of New York, New York, from passing upon and approving, disapproving, or changing proposed budgets of the city, and from exercising any other alleged legislative powers.


OVERVIEW: Despite the fact that there was a great disparity in population among the city's five boroughs, New York City, N.Y., Charter §§ 61 and 62 gave each borough the same vote in the Board. The chairman filed a complaint alleging that New York City, N.Y., Charter §§ 119, 120, 121, 124, 128, 221, 222, 223 and 224, which related to city budget and allied fiscal matters, violated the United States Constitution because it denied to each citizen and voter an equal vote. The court found that the "one man - one vote" principle only applied to legislatures or the general governing body of a local government unit. After reviewing the background of the board, the court found that the rule was inapplicable because it was not a legislature, general governing body, nor a political unit vested with general governmental powers. The Board had a specified but strictly limited range of powers concerning the approval and adoption of certain fiscal policies, and the major part of the legislative and governmental powers of the city lied elsewhere. The function of the Board was to act as the caretaker of the city's property and trustee of the retirement system of the city's employees.


OUTCOME: The court denied the chairman's application for injunctive relief and granted defendants' motion for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- reapportionment -- under New York City Charter of 1963, Board of Estimate is not city's general legislative or governing body, and hence constitutional principle of one person-one vote does not apply to those of its members who are Presidents of boroughs of unequal population.

Under the New York City Charter of 1963 (§ 8, subd. a; §§ 3, 21, 27, 38, 61, 62, 119-121, 124, 128, 221-224, 228; § 813, subd. [i]; § 1102, subd. b), the City Council and the Mayor are the general legislative and general governing bodies of the city, and the Board of Estimate of the city merely participates with them in the adoption and approval of expense budgets and capital budgets and fiscal policies. Accordingly, the constitutional principle of one person-one vote does not apply to the Board of Estimate, and therefore it is immaterial that five of its members are the respective Presidents of the five boroughs of the city and that the five boroughs are unequal in population. Summary judgment is granted dismissing a complaint [***2] which seeks to restrain the Board from allegedly unconstitutionally approving or disapproving or changing the budgets of the city.

 

1973 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Toomey v. Neenan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial and Special Term, Ontario County


59 Misc. 2d 787; 300 N.Y.S.2d 388; 1969 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1871



January 6, 1969 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion for preliminary injunction is denied and the complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner commenced an action against defendants, a town and some of its officers, to restrain the enforcement against him of an ordinance prohibiting the dumping in the town of junk, garbage, and refuse from sources located outside the town.


OVERVIEW: The landowner was under contract to haul pomace from a company that processed apples and apple juice. He hauled the pomace to his property and plowed it under as fertilizer. The town threatened to enforce its ordinance, so the landowner sued. He also sought a preliminary injunction pending the outcome of his action. In the meantime, he was arrested for violating the ordinance, and prosecution commenced. He then sought an order restraining or prohibiting a criminal prosecution pending the resolution of his civil action. The court noted that the suit did not challenge the ordinance on constitutional grounds, but rather sought a declaration whether certain facts, i.e., the dumping or plowing under of pomace, constituted a violation of the ordinance in question. The court found that all of the associated issues were factual in nature and held that they were better left for determination in the already commenced criminal prosecution since no question of law was raised for determination in the civil action regarding the regularity or validity of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court denied the landowner's motion for a preliminary injunction and dismissed his complaint.


HEADNOTES

Injunctions -- criminal prosecution -- action to enjoin criminal prosecution for violation of local law, not on ground that law is invalid or unconstitutional, but on ground that facts do not apply to this case, dismissed.

Plaintiff has been arrested under a town's local law which prohibits, under penalty of $ 500 fine and/or one year's imprisonment, dumping of garbage, junk and refuse from sources outside the town. Plaintiff alleges that he has a contract with a company which processes apples and apple juice to haul the resulting pomace to his property, where he plows it under as fertilizer. The town asserts that the pomace is garbage and that he is not plowing much of it under. Plaintiff does not assert that the local law is invalid or unconstitutional. Under these circumstances, plaintiff's civil action for an injunction against the town's enforcement of its local law is dismissed and of course his motion for a preliminary injunction is denied. The issues are factual and they will be determined in the pending criminal action.

 

1974 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re D.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, Juvenile Term, Queens County


58 Misc. 2d 1093; 296 N.Y.S.2d 825; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 942



December 31, 1968 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner security guard alleged that respondent juvenile should be declared a juvenile delinquent on the ground that she violated N.Y. Penal Law § 140.00(5) by trespassing on the premises of a department store after she had been lawfully ordered not to return to its premises.


OVERVIEW: The security guard testified that she saw the juvenile and two companions opening the pocketbooks of female customers. The store owner directed the juvenile to stay out of the store. When the juvenile entered the department store only three months later, the security guard alleged that the juvenile had violated N.Y. Penal Law § 140.10, the criminal trespass statute. The court found that the juvenile was a juvenile delinquent because she had violated § 140.10 by returning to the store. The court found that §140.10 was constitutional and did not violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV because it did not target individuals of a particular race, creed, color, or national origin. The court found that N.Y. Penal Law § 140.00(5) made clear that intent to commit a crime was not a necessary element of a violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 140.10 and that its purpose was served by allowing department stores the right to keep out of its premises individuals who had previously been involved in acts leading to convictions of or findings against such individual.


OUTCOME: The court found that the juvenile was a juvenile delinquent.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Infants -- juvenile delinquency -- article 140 and section 140.10 of Penal Law dealing with criminal trespass are constitutional -- 15-year-old girl who in July, 1968 was directed not to return to department store and who was found in store opening pocketbooks of female customers on September 19, 1968 violated section 140.10 and is adjudged juvenile delinquent; criminal trespass occurred regardless of intent; lapse of time between warning and re-entry was not unreasonable.

1. Article 140 and particularly section 140.10 of the Penal Law which renders a person guilty of criminal trespass in the second degree "when he knowingly enters or remains unlawfully in a building" are constitutional. Subdivision 5 of section 140.00 of the Penal Law provides that a person "enters or remains unlawfully" upon premises when he is not licensed to do so and a person who "regardless of his intent" enters or remains upon premises open to the public does so with license "unless he defies a lawful order not to enter or remain, personally communicated to him by * * * authorized person". Article 140 does not give any owner the right to keep a person out of premises on the basis of an individual's [***2] race, color, creed or national origin and so the article does not infringe upon section 40 of the Civil Rights Law or section 296 of the Executive Law.

2. A 15-year-old girl who had been directed in July, 1968 orally by a department store's security director to stay out of the store and not to come back and who was seen in the store on September 19, 1968 opening the pocketbooks of female customers violated section 140.10 of the Penal Law and is a juvenile delinquent. No unreasonable lapse of time existed between the date of the warning to stay out and the date of her knowing re-entry into the store. Under the article the criminal trespass occurs "regardless of his intent".

 

1975 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Hogan v. Rosenberg


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


58 Misc. 2d 585; 296 N.Y.S.2d 584; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 945



December 30, 1968 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the application is denied and the petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, petitioner district attorney sought to enjoin and prohibit respondents, the judges of the Criminal Court of the City of New York (New York), from conducting a jury trial in the cases pending against respondent young adults on charges of possession of burglar's tools, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law §140.35, and criminal trespass in the third and first degree, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law §§140.05, 140.15.


OVERVIEW: The young adults were granted a jury trial on Class A misdemeanor and other charges against them. The district attorney filed a petition to prohibit the jury trial, alleging that N.Y. City Crim. Ct. Act § 40, which governed the pending proceedings, expressly precluded a trial by jury. The court addressed the constitutional issues regarding the reformatory sentence provisions of N.Y. Penal Law § 75 et seq., and held that crimes punishable by no more than six months in prison did not require a jury trial, while those persons who faced punishment of two years in jail would be, if convicted, guilty of a "serious" crime and thus entitled to the constitutional guarantee of a trial by jury. Offenses punishable by incarceration of no more than one year were not "serious" crimes and did not require a jury trial. The young adults faced the possibility of up to four years of imprisonment, which mandated the right to trial. Therefore, N.Y. City Crim. Ct. Act § 40, to the extent it denied a jury trial to young adults who faced reformatory sentence pursuant to the provisions of N.Y. Penal Law § 75 et seq., was unconstitutional and void.


OUTCOME: The court denied the application and dismissed the district attorney's petition.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- right to jury trial -- "young adults", over age 16 and under age 21, may be given reformatory sentences of up to four years, and therefore they can be constitutionally tried by jury trial only (Penal Law, § 75.00 et seq.; cf. N. Y. City Crim. Ct. Act, § 40).

An adult who is charged with crimes for which the maximum term of imprisonment is one year may constitutionally be tried without a jury; but a "young adult" (that is, one who is over age 16 and under age 21 at the time of sentence) who has not been given the benefit of a "youthful offender" proceeding may be given a "reformatory sentence" of up to three years or four years; and therefore, a "young adult" can be constitutionally tried by a jury trial only. (U. S. Const., 6th and 14th Amdts.; Penal Law, § 75.00 et seq.; N. Y. City Crim. Ct. Act, § 40; cf. Code Crim. Pro., § 913-e et seq.; Duncan v. Louisiana, 391 U.S. 145, followed.)

 

1976 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Church v. Church


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


58 Misc. 2d 753; 296 N.Y.S.2d 716; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 948



December 28, 1968 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband sought a divorce from defendant wife pursuant to N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 170(5).


OVERVIEW: On March 8, 1963, a separation decree was entered in an action in which the husband was determined to have been the "guilty" party. Thereafter, the husband sought a judgment of divorce pursuant to § 170(5). The court dismissed his complaint. Section 170(5) provided that an action for divorce could be maintained on the ground that the parties had lived apart pursuant to a decree or judgment of separation for a period of two years if the plaintiff submitted proof that he or she had substantially performed all the terms and conditions of that decree or judgment. The court noted that the husband had established an apparent cause of action under § 170(5). However, it concluded that a "guilty" spouse was not entitled to relief under that provision. In that regard, the court found that giving retrospective effect to § 170(5), which took effect on September 1, 1967, would divest and impair the innocent spouse's vested rights of marital status, property, social security, and inheritance. While § 170(5) did not expressly limit relief to innocent spouses, the court found that granting such relief to a "guilty" spouse would offend public policy.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the husband's complaint seeking a divorce from the wife. No costs were awarded.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Husband and wife -- divorce -- "guilty" husband in decree of separation has no cause of action for divorce (Domestic Relations Law, § 170, subd. [5]) based thereon and his complaint is dismissed.

Subdivision (5) of section 170 of the Domestic Relations Law, which provides that an action for divorce may be maintained on the ground that the husband and wife have lived apart pursuant to a decree or judgment of separation for a period of two years after the granting of the judgment and satisfactory proof has been submitted by plaintiff that he or she has substantially performed all the terms and conditions of such decree or judgment, reasonably construed, does not warrant the grant of a decree of divorce to the "guilty" spouse under a decree of separation entered prior to September 1, 1967. Accordingly, the complaint in an action for divorce commenced by a husband who was defendant in the prior judgment of separation entered on March 8, 1963, is dismissed even though the wife has not contested the husband's cause of action.

 

1977 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Martin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, Ulster County


58 Misc. 2d 459; 296 N.Y.S.2d 453; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 966



December 18, 1968 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] There being no failure on the part of the respondent to provide fair and reasonable support for his minor daughter the petition insofar as it seeks support for her is likewise dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner wife, a California resident, filed an action against respondent husband, pursuant to the Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code tit. 10a, part 3, §§ 1650-1690, to obtain an order requiring the husband to support his dependents The action was received by the court in New York as the responding state pursuant to the New York Uniform Support of Dependents Law, N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law art. 3-A.


OVERVIEW: The parties were divorced in Mexico. The Mexican divorce incorporated a separation agreement that required the husband to pay child support and alimony. The wife alleged that the husband failed to make the required support payments. The court stated that in a reciprocal support proceeding of N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 446(c), which conferred jurisdiction upon the family court to entertain applications to enforce the support provisions of foreign divorce decrees, did not apply. The court could only invoke that statute if the wife commenced proceedings in New York. The court also held that the wife was not entitled to relief under the New York Uniform Support of Dependents Law, which made a husband liable for support of his wife, N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law, § 32(1), because that section excluded any liability of a divorced husband for the support of his former wife. Consequently, the proceeding, insofar as it sought support for the wife, was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the wife's petition.


HEADNOTES

Husband and wife -- Uniform Support of Dependents Law -- wife who was divorced by Mexican decree which incorporated support provisions of separation agreement is no longer "his wife" and cannot maintain proceeding to require him to pay to her in California "a fair and reasonable sum" (Domestic Relations Law, art. 3-A [Uniform Support of Dependents Law], § 32 -- said law has not been impliedly modified by Family Court Act ( § 466, subd. [c]) -- New York law, not California law, governs this proceeding -- nor can he be required to support his adult daughter (Domestic Relations Law, § 31, subd. 3; Family Ct. Act, § 413) -- $ 200 per month, which he is now paying, is "a fair and reasonable sum" for his younger daughter -- accordingly, this petition by divorced wife is dismissed.

1. Husband and wife were divorced by a Mexican decree which incorporated by reference their separation agreement requiring him to pay her, for the support of herself and their two daughters, $ 500 a month plus [***2] 20% of any subsequent salary increases. This divorced wife now resides in California. She is no longer "his wife", and therefore she cannot maintain a proceeding under our Uniform Support of Dependents Law to require him to pay "a fair and reasonable sum" for her support (Domestic Relations Law, art. 3-A, § 32, subd. 1). This is not to say that she cannot, if she comes here, maintain a proceeding under our Family Court Act ( § 466, subd. [c]; cf. § 422, subd. [b]) "to modify the order or decree" of the Mexican court. But the Legislature has not indicated any intent to repeal so much of article 3-A of the Domestic Relations Law as would permit the court to interpolate into it the provisions of section 466 of the Family Court Act; nor does the constitutional principle of equal protection of the laws require such an interpolation.

2. Any relief which may be awarded in New York to this divorced wife must be governed by New York law, and not by the California Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act which appears to include "any duty of support imposed * * * by any * * * decree or judgment".

3. As for the two daughters, one is now over 21 years old and hence her father [***3] owes her no duty of support (Family Ct. Act, § 413; Domestic Relations Law, art. 3-A, § 31, subd. 3).

4. As for the younger of the two daughters, respondent father has been paying $ 200 a month; and the court finds, from the evidence as to respondent's income and "means", that this is "a fair and reasonable sum" (Domestic Relations Law, art. 3-A, § 32).

5. Accordingly, the petition is dismissed.

 

1978 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


La Pan v. County of Albany


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


58 Misc. 2d 657; 296 N.Y.S.2d 416; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 978



December 16, 1968 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Therefore, in the exercise of discretion, the motion is granted, without costs, to the extent of having the husband's original notice of claim corrected to supply the omission of his wife's claim for loss of consortium, and to the further extent of permitting an amended complaint to be served upon the municipality on or before January 15, 1969.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant injury victim filed a motion to permit his wife to annex a loss of consortium claim to his notice of claim served on respondent municipality pursuant to N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 50-e after an accident.


OVERVIEW: The victim was involved in an accident, and he sustained serious injuries as a result. The victim alleged that the accident was caused by the municipality's negligence. He filed a notice of claim against the municipality pursuant to § 50-e(1) in a timely manner. After the victim filed his notice of claim, there was a landmark decision that recognized a cause of action for loss of consortium. The victim then filed a motion to permit the wife to annex a claim for loss of consortium to his notice of claim against the municipality. The court granted the motion, holding that § 50-e(5) permitted the correction of a notice of claim in the case of mistakes, omissions, irregularities, and defects made in good faith. The court reasoned that the victim's original notice of claim was timely filed and adequate in content to apprise the municipality of the accident giving rise to the claims. Thus, the court concluded that allowing the wife to annex her consortium claim did not prejudice the municipality.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to permit the victim's wife to annex her consortium claim to the victim's notice of claim against the municipality.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- notice of tort claim -- permission is granted to correct filed notice of negligence claim against municipality, by adding wife's claim for damages for loss of consortium, and to serve amended complaint accordingly.

On July 2, 1968 the Court of Appeals overruled a long existing principle of law and ruled that the wife of an injured man has a cause of action for damages for loss of consortium ( Millington v. Southeastern Elevator Co., 22 N Y 2d 498). Prior to that date, an injured man had filed a notice of negligence claim against a county. His wife's cause of action against the county for damages for loss of consortium arose on the date of the accident. More than 90 days have elapsed, but her claim has not yet been barred by the Statute of Limitations. The husband's filed claim has sufficiently [***2] apprised the county of the accident. The court, in the exercise of discretion, grants permission (a) to correct the husband's filed notice of claim by supplying the omission of the wife's claim for loss of consortium, and (b) to serve an amended complaint on the county accordingly (General Municipal Law, § 50-e, subd. 6).

 

1979 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


American Institute for Imported Steel, Inc. v. County of Erie


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


58 Misc. 2d 1059; 297 N.Y.S.2d 602; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 986



December 13, 1968 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons hereinbefore set forth, it is the opinion of this court that petitioners have failed to sustain the burden of proving the allegations set forth in their petition and that the relief sought therein must therefore be denied and the said petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner bidders filed an action asking that the court review the actions of respondent Commissioner of Public Works for the County of Erie (commissioner). The bidders sought to have the commissioner's addendum and resolutions declared unconstitutional and to order that the commissioner advertise for bids for its project without the addendum.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner sought bids for a public project based upon certain specifications. An addendum to the specifications required that the bidders adhere to the resolution adopted by the county legislature, which limited the source of structural steel used on the project. The bidders argued that the commissioner's action was in violation of N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 103 and that the action of the commissioner was an unwarranted interference with the powers of the federal government to regulate commerce. In denying the petition of the bidders, the court held that the "Buy American" resolution and the contract specifications that followed were not violative of N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 103. The court also determined that it could not assume to pass judgment upon the wisdom of the county legislature's enactment or whether its allegedly offensive resolution was extremely parochial. Accordingly, the court determined that the bidders failed to sustain their burden of proving the allegations set forth in their petition.


OUTCOME: The court denied the bidders' petition to have the Commissioner's addendum and resolution declared unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- contracts -- resolution of Erie County Legislature validly and constitutionally provides that all county public improvement contracts which require steel shall require steel made in United States; injunction denied.

A resolution of the Erie County Legislature, providing that all county public improvement contracts which require steel shall require steel made in the United States unless the product is unavailable here because of labor conditions, and a provision or specification to that effect in a county agency's advertisement for bids for the construction of a building, are lawful and constitutional. They do not violate the 1947 international treaty entitled "General Agreement on Tariffs and Trades", since that treaty excepts "procurement by governmental agencies of products purchased for governmental purposes" (61 U.S. Stat. A19). They do not violate section 103 of the General [***2] Municipal Law which requires that contracts be awarded to the "lowest responsible bidder"; indeed, it appears that such a provision usually appears in State contracts in spite of section 174 of the State Finance Law which requires that State contracts be awarded to the "lowest responsible bidder". Nor does such provision violate the commerce and duties and supremacy clauses of the United States Constitution (art. I, § 8, cl. 3; art. I, § 10, par. 2; art. VI, par. 2); indeed, the United States Government has enacted a similar contract requirement (U. S. Code, tit. 41, § 10b). Accordingly, the court dismisses this petition which seeks to enjoin such an advertisement for bids.

 

1980 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. K.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Criminal Term, Kings County


58 Misc. 2d 526; 296 N.Y.S.2d 404; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1008



December 6, 1968 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motions are denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, two juveniles, were indicted for felonies. They executed a consent for a prepleading investigation and waived a trial by jury. Thereafter, through counsel, they filed a demand for a jury and later made the same demand by notice of motion. Defendants contended that they were entitled to a trial by jury on a youthful offender information, that they did not waive their right, and that even if they did, they made a timely repudiation.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue before the court was whether N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. §§ 913-g(3) and 913-h, which set forth that a trial on a youthful offender information had to be without a jury, violated defendants' constitutional rights. Denying defendants' motions for jury trial, the court refused to declare void and unconstitutional a statute that was so beneficial in its application and held that such a declaration, if it were to be done at all, should be done at the appellate rather than the trial level. The court found no mandate of a jury trial in the Matter of Gault, which held that juvenile court proceedings had to meet constitutional standards of due process as to notice, right to counsel, privilege against self incrimination, and the right to confront and cross-examine sworn witnesses. The court concluded that the mandate that all defendants in serious criminal prosecutions have the right to be tried by a jury did not apply to youthful offender proceedings, which were not criminal prosecutions and did not result in criminal disability.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motions for a jury trial.


HEADNOTES

Infants -- youthful offenders -- youthful offender treatment is not right but privilege -- requirement that trial be without jury (Code Crim. Pro., § 913-g, subd. 3; § 913-h) is constitutional.

1. The according of youthful offender treatment to a youth is not a right but a privilege.

2. Subdivision 3 of section 913-g and section 913-h of the Code of Criminal Procedure, dealing with youthful offenders and providing that a trial, if one is to be had, be without a jury is constitutional. ( Nieves v. United States, 280 F. Supp. 994, not followed.) A jury trial is not essential in affording due process and fair treatment to juveniles.

 

1981 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Kinney Car Corp. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


58 Misc. 2d 365; 295 N.Y.S.2d 288; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1035



November 21, 1968 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons indicated, this motion for a temporary injunction is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff car rental agencies (agencies) sought a preliminary injunction against defendants, city, mayor, police commissioner, traffic commissioner, and the director of the city traffic court, to enjoin them from enforcing an amendment to the New York City, N.Y., 1968 Local Laws No. 57, pending trial on the constitutionality of the amendment.


OVERVIEW: The amendment made car rental agencies liable for the unpaid parking fines of their customers. The agencies contended that it compelled them to pay fines for violations not committed by them in violation of state and federal due process and singled out car owners who rented cars in violation of state and federal equal protection. They also asserted that the city council had no authority to impose parking fines on car owners who did not commit the violations. The court denied the agencies' motion for a preliminary injunction. The agencies could protect themselves by requiring lessees to deposit money in anticipation of unpaid fines. They would suffer no irreparable hardship by the time elapsing prior to the trial. The amendment limited an agency's liability to the fines. Also, pretrial discovery would be necessary to support the claim that the amendment violated equal protection. The fact that lessors of cars were only a small percentage of all car owners did not necessarily establish that the amendment was invalid in singling them out for liability for parking violations committed by others. The city's power was not limited to imposing penalties only on those who parked the cars.


OUTCOME: The court denied the agencies' motion for a temporary injunction pending trial against defendants' enforcement of the amendment.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- parking -- local law subjecting lessors of motor vehicles to fines for illegal parking by lessees is not clearly unconstitutional; application for preliminary injunction denied.

Local Law No. 57 of the 1968 Local Laws of the City of New York provides that lessors of motor vehicles shall be jointly and severally liable with the lessees of such vehicles for parking violations committed by lessees, but that such liability shall be limited to the payment of any duly imposed fines, and that any fine thus paid by a lessor may be recovered by the lessor from the lessee; and further, that the lessor shall not be liable for a fine if said lessor has filed the registration plate number of the leased vehicle and the lessor's address with the New York City Criminal Court's Traffic Summons Control Bureau and if a notice of issuance of the summons is not mailed to the lessor at such address within 90 days. This local law does not contravene the Vehicle and Traffic Law (cf. § 388; § 1642, subd. [a], pars. 2, 20), or clearly violate the due process and equal protection provisions of [***2] the State or Federal Constitution, or impose irreparable hardship on the business of leasing automobiles and trucks; and therefore, enforcement will not be temporarily restrained.

 

1982 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Real Properties Along Peconic River


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


58 Misc. 2d 409; 295 N.Y.S.2d 992; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1062



November 13, 1968 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Except as modified by this decision, the objections filed by claimants above named are overruled and the tentative decree, as so modified, is confirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a condemnation proceeding, claimant landowners filed objections to the court's tentative decree, questioning the amount of the awards made to the landowners for the loss of use of their land upon a taking by defendant county.


OVERVIEW: Two of the landowners questioned the amount of awards made to them, contending that the awards were inadequate. The other two landowners did not contest the amount of the awards as rendered, but contended that, because of a rise in the general interest rate, the constitutional mandate of "just compensation" for property taken under eminent domain included an allowance of interest in excess of the statutory limitation of four percent prescribed by § 13 of the Suffolk County Improvement Act, 1933 N.Y. Laws ch. 566. The court modified in part and affirmed, holding that: (1) the award to one landowner was inadequate because the landowner's parcel was more favorably situated in comparison to another parcel, but the unit value per acre of the award for each parcel was substantially the same; (2) the trial court did not err computing the interest payable to the landowners because in the legal interest rate of four percent referred to in § 13 was fixed by N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 3-a and was the proper legal rate of interest in a condemnation proceeding; and (3) the provisions of § 3-a, as it related to the rate of interest in condemnation matters, was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court modified the award for one parcel by increasing the award for one of the parcels; except as modified, the court overruled the objections filed by the landowners and confirmed the tentative decree, as so modified.


HEADNOTES

Eminent domain -- interest on award -- interest rate on condemnation award in Suffolk County is still only 4%.

The interest rate on a condemnation award in Suffolk County is still only 4% (Suffolk County Improvement Act [L. 1933, ch. 566], § 13; General Municipal Law, § 3-a), and this rate is still valid and constitutional.

 

1983 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kearse


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Onondaga County


58 Misc. 2d 277; 295 N.Y.S.2d 192; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1060



November 13, 1968 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged a decision of the City Court of Syracuse (New York) that dismissed charges for curfew violations under Syracuse, N.Y. Rev. Gen. Ordinances § 16-58(d) against appellees, contending that the trial court erred in finding the ordinance unconstitutional because it was an unlawful delegation of legislative authority, was preempted by state law, denied constitutional guaranteed liberties, and was overly broad.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with curfew violations and filed a motion to dismiss because the city ordinance was unconstitutional. Specifically, defendants contended that Syracuse, N.Y. Rev. Gen. Ordinances § 16-58(d) was an unlawful delegation of legislative authority, was preempted by state law, denied constitutional guaranteed liberties and was overly broad. The statute read that anybody on the streets or in a public building was susceptible to arrest, excepting law enforcement or emergency vehicles. The court held that because the statute was susceptible to arbitrary enforcement and was a total prohibition rather than reasonable regulation, it was unconstitutional. On the merits, the court affirmed the trial court's dismissal. The court also addressed defendants' contention that the appeal was improperly taken, and held that the provisions of the Uniform City Court Act took precedence over the generalized New York Criminal Procedure Law, specifically that the Uniform City Ct. Act (23) took precedence over prior procedural provisions relating to an appeal from a city court outside New York City, thereby affirming all aspects of the trial court's dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of charges of curfew violations against appellees.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- curfew -- broadly drawn curfew ordinance was unconstitutional and void -- appeal by People from City Court's dismissal of informations dismissed.

1. An emergency curfew ordinance which provided that "No person shall enter or remain in any public street, park, square or building in any such part or parts of the city during the hours of the day as may be prescribed by the Mayor" was so broadly drawn as to make any enforcement thereof arbitrary and selective, and hence it contravened constitutional rights to equal protection of the laws, and therefore it was void.

2. Moreover, this appeal by the People from the City Court's dismissal of the informations must be dismissed (UCCA, arts. 20, 23; Code Crim. Pro., §§ 751, 759).

 

1984 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Long Island Beach Buggy Asso. v. Islip


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


58 Misc. 2d 295; 295 N.Y.S.2d 268; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1091



November 1, 1968 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The complaints are hereby dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, members of a travel association and a resident, filed actions to have defendant town's ordinance, which restricted use of certain routes, declared invalid and unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The resident owned real property within the town and was engaged in the general contracting business. In connection with his business, the resident used a motor vehicle to traverse the beach and inland route and claimed that the ordinance, which restricted his use of the routes, was unconstitutional and should be declared invalid. The association was composed of persons who were not residents of the town, but who desired to travel by vehicle over the routes and who were prohibited by the ordinance from doing so. In dismissing the complaints, the court held that no easement by prescription had been created with reference to the inland route or the beach route. Property affected with a public interest was not subject to an easement by prescription. The court further held that the association and the resident had not rebutted the presumption in favor of the constitutionality of the ordinance, and thus the court refused to declare the ordinance unconstitutional merely because it caused the association and the resident some inconvenience.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the complaints filed by the association and the resident.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- ordinances restricting vehicles -- ordinances restricting vehicular uses of beach route and inland route to Fire Island in Suffolk County are reasonable and constitutional.

Ordinances restricting vehicular uses of the beach route and of the inland route to Fire Island in Suffolk County are not confiscatory, but rather are in accord with public policy and are reasonable and constitutional exercises of the police power in order to prevent further erosion of the sand dunes and beaches and to protect pedestrians. Those routes are not public highways or prescriptive rights of way. Complaints of an association of nonresidents, and of an individual who is a resident and a real property owner and a businessman, both seeking a declaration of unconstitutionality, are dismissed.

 

1985 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Walsh v. Lomenzo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


57 Misc. 2d 1082; 294 N.Y.S.2d 166; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1114



October 22, 1968 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion denied, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate filed a motion for an order directing respondents, the Secretary of State of the State of New York and the Boards of Elections and Election Commissioners of several counties, to provide eight separate columns for the candidates for the supreme court and to determine the order of the names to be placed on the ballot by lot.


OVERVIEW: The candidate was nominated by the Democratic party to fill one of four vacancies on a state supreme court. Four political parties each nominated four candidates. There were a total of eight candidates on the ballot, and their names were listed in four rows according to the party that nominated the candidate. The candidate objected to the format, alleging that the placing of the names of two or more candidates in the same columns was deceptive to the voting public because it led them to believe that they had to choose between the candidates rather than voting for either of the candidates. The candidate petitioned for the use of eight separate columns. Regarding the candidate's motion to have the positions on the ballot determined by lot, the court held that under N.Y. Elec. Law § 104(1), the candidate had to make his request in writing within one week after his nomination. The court found that the candidate made his request too late. Regarding the position of the names on the ballot, the court held that the mandates of N.Y. Elec. Law § 248(1) had been met by using four rows for the parties and four columns for the four vacancies.


OUTCOME: The court denied the candidate's motion to place the candidates' names in separate columns and to determine the placement of the names by lot.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- voting machines -- arrangement of eight judicial candidates on voting machines ("Vote for any four") in four rows, one row for each party, is not discriminatory; motion for rearrangement and determination by lot denied.

The voting machines for the November 5, 1968 general election will read, in part, as to the eight candidates for Supreme Court Justice in the Eighth Judicial District: "(Vote for any four)

Republican:

Stiller

Marshall

Moore

Stakel

Democratic:

Levitt

Walsh

Doerr

Johnson

Conservative:

Stiller

Marshall

Moore

Johnson

Liberal:

Stiller

Marshall

Doerr

Stakel".

The Secretary of State certified these candidates on September 23, 1968. Now one of the candidates applies to the court, by motion on October 10, 1968 returnable October 14, 1968, for an order requiring eight columns for these candidates and a determination by lot as to the order in which their names shall be placed. It is now October 22 -- hardly time for a determination and possible appeals. The above arrangement is not discriminatory (Election Law, § 104, subd. 1; § 248, subd. 1; § 330, last unnumbered par.).  [***2] This application is denied.

 

1986 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Chase Manhattan Bank v. Broadway, Whitney Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


57 Misc. 2d 1091; 294 N.Y.S.2d 416; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1124



October 17, 1968 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owner applied for a license under N.Y. Real Prop. Acts. § 881 to enter respondent adjacent property owner's premises for five days during a one-month period in order to make repairs to the rear wall of its premises. The adjacent property owner moved to dismiss, asserting that the petition failed to state facts sufficient to constitute a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: A property owner instituted a proceeding under N.Y. Real Prop. Acts. § 881 seeking a license to enter the adjacent property over the adjacent property owner's objection in order to make repairs to the rear wall of its premises. The adjacent property owner moved to dismiss the petition. In granting the petition and denying the adjacent property owner's motion, the court concluded that, although inconvenience would result to the adjacent property owner and its tenants, the inconvenience would not be as substantial as the hardship that would accrue to the property owner if its application were denied. The repairs that the property owner sought to make were necessary, the hardship that would result if the repairs were not made would be permanent, and the repairs could not be made without entering the adjacent property.


OUTCOME: A property owner's petition for a license to enter adjacent property over the adjacent property owner's objection was granted, and the adjacent property owner's motion to dismiss was denied.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Adjoining landowners -- order permitting entry -- property owner may obtain order permitting him to enter on adjoining property in order to repair own property (Real Property Actions and Proceedings Law, § 881); statute is constitutional -- bank which needs to repair wall of its building should be permitted to erect scaffolding on part of adjoining parking lot of shopping center.

1. The Real Property Actions and Proceedings Law ( § 881) validly and constitutionally provides: "When an owner or lessee seeks to make improvements or repairs to real property so situated that such improvements or repairs cannot be made by the owner or lessee without entering the premises of an adjoining owner or his lessee, and permission so to enter has been refused, the owner or lessee seeking to make such improvements or repairs may commence a special proceeding for a license so to enter pursuant to article four of the civil practice law and rules. The petition and affidavits, if any, shall state the facts making such entry necessary and the date or dates on which entry is sought. Such license shall be granted by the court in an appropriate case upon such terms as justice requires. The licensee [***2] shall be liable to the adjoining owner or his lessee for actual damages occurring as a result of the entry."

2. Petitioner, a bank, alleges that its own interior wall has become damaged by moisture seeping through from outside and that it needs to waterproof and repoint the exterior brickwork; that this can be done only by erecting a scaffolding on a minor portion, about 54 square feet, of the adjoining parking area which respondent, a shopping center, owns and maintains for said center's seven stores; that the work can be completed in about 5 days of dry weather; that respondent has refused permission; and that, in order to be assured of 5 consecutive dry days, petitioner needs a license to enter respondent's premises for a period of 30 days. Respondent asserts that such license would interfere with its tenants' contract rights; but it has not asked that any tenant be joined as a party. Unless respondent elects to serve a formal answer alleging inconvenience, hardship, etc., the petition should be granted. Immediately on completion of the work, the scaffolding should be removed and the occupied premises cleaned and vacated.

 

1987 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Hempstead


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


58 Misc. 2d 134; 294 N.Y.S.2d 809; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1137



October 11, 1968 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town filed a condemnation proceeding against defendant claimant. The trial court (New York) ascribed an additional 10 percent increment in adjusting the comparable sales and then found a rounded total area of 24.3 acres. The town objected to the trial court's findings. The trial court also held that the quantum of interest was four percent. The claimant objected to the trial court's assessment of interest.


OVERVIEW: The town sought to acquire title to the claimant's real property for the purpose of building a park. On appeal, the town contended that the trial court erred in ascribing an additional 10 percent increment in adjusting the comparable sales. The court found that the additional 10 percent increment was reasonable, accurate, and just. Next, the town objected to the trial court's finding that the rounded total acres of the property were 24.3 acres. According to the town, the total area shown on the taking map was 23.7 acres. The court modified the trial court's decision by reducing the trial court's finding with respect to the total acreage. With respect to the claimant's objection regarding the amount of interest, the court held that N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 3-a, insofar as the rate of interest was concerned, was unconstitutional. Further, the court held that the award of should bear interest at the rate of 4 percent from the date of the de facto taking and then increase to 6 percent after August 1, 1966, which was the enactment date of N.Y. State. Fin. Law § 16. Section 16 provided for the payment of 6 percent interest in condemnation proceedings brought by the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision ascribing an additional 10 percent increment in adjusting the comparable sales. However, the court modified the trial court's finding regarding the total area of acres by reducing the amount of acres. Lastly, the court reversed the trial court's finding that the quantum of interest was four percent.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Eminent domain -- compensation -- in adjusting comparable sales, court ascribed 10% increment because rezoning had been accomplished -- amount of increase of acreage by gradual accretion was fixed at midpoint of surveys made before and after date of appropriation de facto -- municipal corporations, as well as State, shall pay interest at 6% from and after August 1, 1966 (State Finance Law, § 16, as amd.; cf. General Municipal Law, § 3-a).

1. In adjusting the comparable sales for the purpose of determining a just compensation for an appropriation, the court in this case ascribed a 10% increment by virtue of the fact that the rezoning of this parcel for residence purposes had been successfully accomplished.

2. Claimant's property was taken de facto on June 15, 1966, prior to the vesting date of November 16, 1966. A survey made in December, 1965, and another survey made in December, 1966, showed that between those dates claimant's acreage was increased by 0.59 acre by accretion. Since no engineering study pinpointed this gradual increase, the court inferred that half of it, or 0.295 acre, was added to claimant's acreage, as of June 15, 1966. At $ 57,000 per acre, this [***2] amounted to $ 16,815.

3. The General Municipal Law ( § 3-a) has, for many years, provided that the rate of interest payable in condemnation by a municipal corporation "shall not exceed four per centum per annum"; but, effective August 1, 1966 the State Finance Law ( § 16) has been amended so as to provide that the rate of interest payable in condemnation by the State "shall not exceed six per centum per annum." This makes the 4% rate for municipal corporations unconstitutional after August 1, 1966, since a municipal corporation is only a subdivision of the State itself. Accordingly, in this condemnation proceeding by a town, the court awards interest at 4% from the de facto taking date, June 15, 1966, to August 1, 1966, but at 6% from and after August 1, 1966.

 

1988 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Manufacturers & Traders Trust Co. v. Forestville


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


57 Misc. 2d 973; 294 N.Y.S.2d 59; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1144



October 9, 1968 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Thus, motion is denied, except that respondent is directed to honor the income execution, collecting 10% of the judgment debtor's income and forwarding it to the Sheriff of Chautauqua County, New York, starting upon the service of a copy of the order to be signed herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner judgment creditor moved for an order directing judgment against respondent employer for failure to comply with an income execution against moneys payable to judgment debtor.


OVERVIEW: The judgment creditor recovered two judgments against judgment debtor. An execution against judgment debtor's income from his employer was issued to county sheriff, and the sheriff served the execution upon the employer. The employer deducted one payment from the judgment debtor's income, but refused to pay more. The employer claimed that a family court had issued an execution against judgment debtor and that no other wage assignment would be effective while the family court's order was in effect. The judgment creditor moved for an order directing judgment against the employer for failure to comply with an income execution against moneys payable to judgment debtor. The court denied the motion, but directed the employer to honor the income execution of the trial court. The execution was to run concurrently with the family court payroll deduction order. The court held that the family court did not have the authority to exclude the trial court's execution order.


OUTCOME: The judgment creditor's motion for an order directing judgment against the employer for failure to comply with an income execution against moneys payable to judgment debtor was denied. However, the employer was directed to honor the income execution of the trial court.


HEADNOTES

Garnishment -- income execution versus family support order -- Family Court order directed village to deduct $ 15 weekly from employee's pay for support of his children, and directed that no other garnishment should be in effect; nevertheless, Supreme Court directs village to deduct 10% from said employee's pay, concurrently, and forward said 10% to Sheriff on judgment creditor's income execution ( CPLR 5231).

1. A judgment creditor of a village employee, who was being paid over $ 30 weekly, levied an income execution thereon. However, the Family Court ordered the village to deduct $ 15 a week from said employee's pay, for support of his minor children; moreover, the Family Court order provided that "While this payroll deduction order is in effect, no other wage assignment or garnishee execution shall be in effect". Nevertheless, such a provision cannot deprive the Supreme Court of its jurisdiction and [***2] power of garnishment. (N. Y. Const., art. VI, § 7; art. VI, § 13, subd. d; CPLR 5231.) The Supreme Court orders the village to honor the judgment creditor's income execution by forwarding 10% of the judgment debtor's pay to the Sheriff, and directs that this order shall run concurrently with the Family Court payroll deduction order.

2. The Legislature has given support orders for minor children priority over garnishments (Personal Property Law, § 49-b, subd. 2; cf. § 48-a, subd. 3). The Appellate Division, Fourth Department, has held that this means that a 10% garnishment ( CPLR 5231) may nevertheless be levied concurrently with a Family Court payroll deduction order. The Supreme Court, Erie County, will follow the holding of the Appellate Division, Fourth Department, rather than the contrary holding of the Appellate Term in the Second Department.

 

1989 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Smith v. Derison


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, Long Beach


57 Misc. 2d 1003; 294 N.Y.S.2d 339; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1150



October 8, 1968 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who owned a house in a one-family zone, was charged by the City with violation of the zoning law, Long Beach, N.Y., Mun. Code art. 1, ch. 9, § 9-105.6 by using his building for more than one-family occupancy in an area zoned for one-family use.


OVERVIEW: Defendant owned a house that was located in an area that was zoned for one-family use. Of the 1,500 houses in such area, one-third were designated as two-family houses and one-third had more families residing therein than were permitted under the zoning laws. Defendant's house was occupied by more than one family, and he was charged with violating § 9-105.6 in that his building was used for more than one-family occupancy. Defendant alleged that because there had been a drastic change of use of buildings in such area, § 9-105.6 was unconstitutional. The court held that: (1) the change in the nature of defendant's premises was brought about by defendant or by his predecessor in title, and the failure of the City to enforce the zoning ordinances in the past, and the classification of numerous houses as two-family in the one-family zone, did not estop the City from enforcing them at the present time; (2) violations of the ordinance by defendant and by others could not be used as the basis for finding that § 9-105.6 was invalid; and (3) there was no arbitrary, intentional, unfair, clear, or invidious discrimination against defendant in the enforcement of the zoning laws.


OUTCOME: The court found defendant guilty of violating the zoning ordinance, and he was directed to appear for sentencing.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- one-family zoning is not invalidated by widespread change of conditions or by widespread nonenforcement; defendant is found guilty of using his house for occupancy by more than one family.

About one third of the 1,500 houses in a one-family zone in the City of Long Beach are illegally occupied by at least one additional family. A report of the City Planning Board so indicates. Moreover, in the records of the city's water supply department, such houses are listed as two-family houses. Nevertheless, such a general change of conditions in the zone does not render the zoning unconstitutional, and these widespread violations do not estop the city from enforcing the zoning ordinance. The defendant in this case has not shown that this enforcement prosecution against him is arbitrary or that it invidiously discriminates against him. Several other defendants who are facing similar prosecutions have stipulated that the decision in this case shall apply to them too. The court finds this defendant guilty of using his house for more than one-family occupancy, in violation of the zoning ordinance.

 

1990 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Rupp v. Lindsay


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


57 Misc. 2d 946; 293 N.Y.S.2d 812; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1166



October 1, 1968 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the matter is remanded to the Commissioner for proceedings consistent with this opinion and the respondents' motion to dismiss is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner political activists sought relief in a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding of a decision by respondent city officials, who denied the political activists' request to use a public stadium for a political rally. The city officials filed a motion to dismiss the petition under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 7804(f).


OVERVIEW: The political activists tried to rent a public stadium for a political rally. The city officials denied the request on the ground that it was a prohibited use of a publicly owned facility. The political activists sought mandamus relief under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 and the city officials moved to dismiss under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 7804(f). The court denied the motion to dismiss and remanded the case to the city officials and the Commissioner of Parks of the City of New York, in particular, for proceedings consistent with the opinion. It noted that New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § 532-15.0 provided that the city officials could rent the stadium and New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § 532-15.0(b) provided that it could be rented for any public purpose. The court noted further that it could not order the city officials to act unless their decision was capricious, arbitrary, or unreasonable. It held that the decision to deny the use of the stadium for an important political rally conflicted with that standard because the stated political purpose was clearly in the public interest. It ordered the city officials to rent the stadium to the political activists on reasonable terms.


OUTCOME: The court denied the city officials motion to dismiss and remanded the matter for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- rental of municipal stadium -- city should rent municipal stadium to campaign committee of third-party Presidential candidate, for public address by such candidate.

Under the Administrative Code of the City of New York (§ 532-15.0) the city's Commissioner of Parks may and should rent the city's 50,000-seat stadium, known as the William A. Shea Municipal Stadium, to "any person or persons", on reasonable terms, for "events of civic, community and general public interest". These words and purposes include a renting for an address to be delivered by a third-party Presidential candidate. On this petition by the latter's campaign committee, the court remands this matter to the Commissioner of Parks for proceedings consistent with this opinion of the court ( CPLR, art. 78).

 

1991 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Skorupa


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, Buffalo


57 Misc. 2d 664; 293 N.Y.S.2d 412; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1215



September 6, 1968 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Therefore, based on the foregoing, the motion is, in all respects, denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved for an order vacating and quashing a certain search warrant, which authorized the search of certain premises and of defendant. Defendant argued that the warrant was improperly issued and that no probable cause existed for its issuance.


OVERVIEW: A police officer was conducting an investigation of intercepted telephone calls through a wire-tap. The calls were placed by defendant and involved defendant discussing taking bets. At a later date, the officer eavesdropped on a conversation between defendant and another individual in which betting was discussed. Based on the information, a warrant was issued to search defendant's premises, and defendant challenged the probable cause for the warrant. The court held that the unconstitutionality of eavesdropping orders under N.Y. Code Crim. P. § 813-a did not affect wiretapping. The court found that even if the wiretap was unconstitutional, defendant, as a party calling the tapped line, had no standing to challenge the constitutionality of the tap. The court ruled that the information discovered by the officer was sufficient to establish probable cause for the warrant.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to vacate or quash the search warrant.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- search warrant -- in affidavit on basis of which search warrant, authorizing search of defendant and certain premises, was issued, police officer alleged that he received information, relating to book-making activities and involving defendant and telephone number listed for said premises, as result of earlier search at other premises at which telephone calls were intercepted and that, six months later, on basis of information received from anonymous informer, surveillance of defendant commenced and conversations relating to book-making were overheard -- affidavit sets forth sufficient facts constituting timely probable cause for issuance of search warrant -- motion to suppress, as to persons arrested in earlier search, had been granted but only in mistaken belief that wiretapping provisions of statute, as well as those relating to eavesdropping, were unconstitutional -- accordingly, legality of said earlier search and seizure was never specifically determined and, in any event, present defendant would have no standing to attack it -- as to timeliness, court relied on observations made and  [***2] conversations overheard by officer after surveillance commenced.

1. Defendant moves to quash a search warrant, authorizing a search of him and of certain premises, which was issued on the basis of an affidavit executed in January, 1968 by a police officer who alleged, among other things, that he received information, relating to book-making activities and involving defendant and the telephone number listed for the premises for which the search warrant was sought, as a result of a search conducted in May, 1967 at other premises at which an interception of telephone calls was made pursuant to court order, which search resulted in the arrests of two persons other than defendant, and that in November, 1967, on the basis of information received from an anonymous informer, surveillance of defendant was commenced and conversations relating to book-making were overheard then and subsequently. This affidavit sets forth sufficient facts constituting timely probable cause for the issuance of the search warrant and the motion to quash the warrant is denied.

2. A motion to suppress, as to the persons arrested in May, 1967, the evidence obtained from the search then conducted was granted on [***3] a motion by the District Attorney, based on the mistaken belief that the decision in Berger v. New York (388 U.S. 41), striking down as unconstitutional those portions of section 813-a of the Code of Criminal Procedure which authorized eavesdropping orders, rendered the entire section unconstitutional. However, the Court of Appeals subsequently held that the wiretapping provisions of said section 813-a were not affected by the Berger case. Accordingly, the legality or illegality of the May, 1967 search and seizure was never specifically determined. In any event, the present defendant would have no standing to attack it.

3. As to timeliness, it was at the suggestion of the issuing Judge that the information from the May, 1967 search was incorporated into the affidavit. The court relied on the observations made and the conversations overheard by the officer in and after November, 1967 and these, coupled with the officer's prior knowledge of defendant and the telephone number, were overwhelming evidence of probable cause superior to an established standard.

 

1992 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Menechino v. Division of Parole, New York City


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


57 Misc. 2d 865; 293 N.Y.S.2d 741; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1242



August 27, 1968 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, acting pro se, filed an application under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 against respondents, a city division of parole and others. Petitioner sought review of determinations made by the New York State Board of Parole in 1965 and 1967 pursuant to which petitioner was remanded to prison as a parole violator and denied parole.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that his constitutional rights were violated because he was not afforded counsel at either the 1965 or 1967 proceedings. The court stated that it was clear that N.Y. Correct. Law § 218 mandated a hearing for one charged with violation of parole. Thus, under the United States Supreme Court's decision in Powell, petitioner should have been afforded the right to be represented by counsel, because in a situation where a person's liberty was at stake, the right to be heard was of little avail if the person did not have counsel to assist him.


OUTCOME: The court ordered the New York State Board of Parole to hold a new hearing on petitioner's alleged parole violations, after giving notice to petitioner of the accusations against him, his right to cross-examination, and his right to be represented by counsel.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Parole -- right to counsel -- on hearing to revoke parole, parolee was unconstitutionally denied right to counsel; new hearing ordered.

On a hearing to revoke petitioner's parole he was unconstitutionally denied the right to counsel. The Parole Board is ordered to hold a new hearing on reasonable notice to petitioner of the accusations against him, of his right to examine the witnesses against him, of his right to testify in his own behalf and of his right to be represented by counsel.

 

1993 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


McCartney v. Austin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Broome County


57 Misc. 2d 525; 293 N.Y.S.2d 188; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1255



August 16, 1968 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school board brought a motion for summary judgment in a declaratory judgment action by plaintiff parents alleging that N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2164 was unconstitutional, and seeking to enjoin the school board from interfering with the school attendance of plaintiff student.


OVERVIEW: The student was not immunized against poliomyelitis in accordance with N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2164, he was refused admittance to the school controlled by the school board. The parents brought an action against the school board seeking a declaration that N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2164 was unconstitutional, and enjoining the school board from interfering with the student's school attendance on the ground that the law violated the parents' freedom of worship. The school board brought a motion for summary judgment seeking to dismiss the action for failure to state a cause of action. The court ruled that legislative acts carried a strong presumption of constitutionality, and that the unconstitutionality of an act must be demonstrated beyond a reasonable doubt. Further, the court held that questions as to wisdom, need, or appropriateness were for the legislature, and that courts struck down statutes only as a last resort. The court entered summary judgment in favor of the school board, concluding that N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2164 did not interfere with the parents' freedom of worship.


OUTCOME: The school board's motion for summary judgment was granted, and the action was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Schools -- immunization of pupils -- Roman Catholic parent has standing to question validity of Public Health Law ( § 2164) which requires parents to inoculate child against polio, requires principal of school to exclude child who has not been immunized and exempts members of religious organization whose teachings are contrary to practice required by statute -- teachings of Roman Catholic faith are not contrary to practice of statute and plaintiffs' personal convictions against inoculation are not within exemption of statute -- exclusion of plaintiffs' child from school because he was not immunized is not arbitrary -- section 2164 is constitutional.

1. Section 2164 of the Public Health Law requires a parent of a school-age child to have the child immunized against poliomyelitis, requires the principal of a school to refuse admittance of a child who has not been immunized and exempts children whose parents are members of a religious organization whose teachings are contrary to the practice required by the statute. Plaintiff, a Roman Catholic parent, alleges that he has strong convictions against inoculation for poliomyelitis, that his child has not been inoculated and asks [***2] for judgment declaring the section unconstitutional. Plaintiffs have standing to question the validity of the statute.

2. The teachings of the Roman Catholic faith are not contrary to the practice required by the statute and plaintiffs' personal convictions as to immunization do not come within the exemption of section 2164.

3. The exclusion of plaintiffs' child from school because he was not immunized is not arbitrary, capricious or an abuse of discretion. Plaintiffs have not been discriminated against by the statute.

4. Section 2164 does not interfere with plaintiffs' freedom of worship and is constitutional and binding upon them.

 

1994 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Ithaca Journal News, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, Ithaca


57 Misc. 2d 356; 292 N.Y.S.2d 920; 1968 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1272



August 5, 1968 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, a newspaper and two of its employees, brought a motion for an order dismissing contempt proceedings brought against them upon an order to show cause issued on the affidavit of petitioner, an attorney for two youths accused of petit larceny. The newspaper claimed that it had the right to publish two articles naming the youths and disclosing that the court ordered the youths' proceeding withheld from the press.


OVERVIEW: The youths allegedly stole two gasoline cans from a motor boat, and a newspaper reporter was present when they were brought before the court. The court ordered that it would be prejudicial under N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 913, the Youthful Offender Act (Act), for the newspaper to reveal their identities or any content of the charges, but the articles were printed, and the attorney made the motion for contempt. Upon consideration of the order to show cause, the court found that pursuant to N.Y. Jud. Law § 750(3), made applicable by N.Y. Uniform City Ct. Act § 210, a court of record had the power to punish for criminal contempt a person guilty of a willful disobedience to its lawful mandate, that the Act served the goal of protecting juveniles, and that freedom of the press was to be balanced against other rights such as an accused's right to a fair trial or the right of a juvenile to be spared from publicity for an irresponsible act. The court found that its oral order was binding upon those who heard it, and that an order issued by a court with jurisdiction over the subject matter and the parties was to be obeyed until it was reversed even if the order was erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion and directed that a hearing was to be held to determine the facts surrounding the publication of the articles.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Contempt -- criminal contempt -- reporter and newspaper willfully and knowingly flouted direction of court not to reveal names of youths charged with petit larceny because they would receive youthful offender treatment; direction was lawful under Code of Criminal Procedure (§ 913-f) -- section applied to respondents and is constitutional -- oral direction in open court was binding on respondents; no written order was required -- hearing ordered.

1. Section 913-f of the Code of Criminal Procedure deals with youthful offenders and provides that "The court * * * may, but only as to the public, order the indictment or information sealed in the case of a youth charged with crime". Two youths were charged with petit larceny and brought before the Judge who directed that, because they will receive youthful offender treatment, one respondent, a member of the press employed by respondent newspaper, not reveal their identity or the charge. In the afternoon edition, both were revealed. The mandate issued by the court was lawful and within its power and respondents willfully and knowingly flouted it.

2. While freedom of the press is constitutionally protected, it is not an unbridled [***2] right and must be balanced against the right of an accused to a fair trial free from unwarranted press coverage or the right of an infant to be spared from publicity for one irresponsible act caused by immaturity.

3. Section 913-f applies to respondents and is constitutional.

4. An oral direction given in open court is as binding upon those who heard it as if it were written. The direction of the court was recorded in the stenographer's minutes and no written order was required.
